Ihram Required for Entering Mecca: Rule, Exception, and Legal Trick
States the ruling of ihram for entering Mecca with an exception and a legal trick.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that ihram is required for entering Mecca, explain the exception for the Conquest of Mecca, and identify the legal trick for residents inside the miqat.

Core Idea
Ihram is required for entering Mecca, except for the Prophet on the day of Conquest; a resident may enter without ihram if he does not intend Hajj/Umrah.

In this passage, the author from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a fundamental rule: the obligation of ihram applies to anyone entering Mecca, regardless of their purpose—be it Hajj, Umrah, trade, or even warfare. The only exception is the historical Conquest of Mecca (Fatḥ Makkah). The passage also presents a legal trick (hila) for residents inside the miqat to enter Mecca without ihram by simply not intending Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recognize that the author states ihram is required for anyone entering Mecca, whether for Hajj, Umrah, trade, or any other purpose. The reason is to honor the sacred place.
2
Recognize the Exception
The only exception is the day of the Conquest of Mecca, which was specific to the Prophet ﷺ. This is proven by the hadith: 'Mecca is sacred; it was not permitted for anyone after me...'.
The hadith is cited as evidence that the exception is not general.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The requirement of ihram is not tied to a specific act of worship but to the sanctity of Mecca itself. Therefore, even entering for trade or warfare requires ihram.
4
Delve into the Legal Trick (Hila)
For a person who is already inside the miqat (i.e., a resident of the Haram area), they may enter Mecca without ihram if they do not intend Hajj or Umrah. This is the 'trick' to avoid ihram.
This hila is only for residents; people from outside must make ihram at the miqat if they intend to enter Mecca.
5
Note the Restriction
The author mentions that this hila is not allowed for one who is 'commanded' (al-ma'mur). This likely refers to someone who has been ordered by a master (like a slave) or who is under a personal obligation to perform Hajj/Umrah.
The exact meaning of 'al-ma'mur' is ambiguous, but it restricts the hila for those who already have a duty to perform Hajj/Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق في الإحرام فشمل إحرام الحج وإحرام العمرة لأنه لا فرق بينهما في حق الآفاق، وشمل ما إذا كان قاصداً عند المجاوزة الحج أو العمرة أو التجارة أو القتال أو غير ذلك بعد أن يكون قد قصد دخول مكة لأن الإحرام لتعظيم هذه البقعة الشريفة فاستوى فيه الكل وأما دخوله مكة بغير إحرام يوم الفتح فكان مختصاً بتلك الساعة بدليل قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في ذلك اليوم «مكة حرام لم تحل لأحد بعدي وإنما أحلت لي ساعة من نهار ثم عادت حراماً» (۱) يعني الدخول بغير إحرام لإجماع المسلمين على حل الدخول بعده عليه الصلاة والسلام للقتال وقيدنا بقصد مكة لأن الآفاقي إذا قصد موضعاً من الحل كخليص يجوز له أن يتجاوز الميقات غير محرم وإذا وصل إليه التحق بأهله، ومن كان داخل الميقات فله أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام إذا لم يقصد الحج أو العمرة وهي الحيلة لمن أراد أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام. وينبغي أن لا تجوز هذه الحيلة للمأمور
He generalized in ihram, so it includes ihram for Hajj and ihram for Umrah, because there is no difference between them regarding the people of the horizons. And it includes if one intends at the time of passing by Hajj or Umrah or trade or warfare or other than that, after having intended to enter Mecca, because ihram is to honor this noble place, so all are equal in it. As for entering Mecca without ihram on the day of the Conquest, it was specific to that time, evidenced by his statement, peace be upon him, on that day: 'Mecca is sacred; it was not permitted for anyone after me, and it was only permitted for me for an hour of the day, then it returned to being sacred.' He means entering without ihram, due to the consensus of Muslims on the permissibility of entering after him, peace be upon him, for warfare. And we restrict it by the intention of Mecca, because if a person from the horizons intends a place outside the Haram, like Khulays, he may pass the miqat without ihram, and when he reaches it, he joins its people. And whoever is inside the miqat may enter Mecca without ihram if he does not intend Hajj or Umrah. This is the trick for one who wants to enter Mecca without ihram. And it is not permissible for one who is commanded to use this trick.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage states the general rule that the obligation of ihram for entering Mecca applies to all persons who intend to enter Mecca, regardless of their purpose—whether for Hajj, Umrah, trade, or even warfare. The only exception is the day of the Conquest of Mecca, which was specific to the Prophet ﷺ. The author then discusses a legal trick (hila): a person who is inside the miqat (i.e., a resident of the Haram area) may enter Mecca without ihram if he does not intend Hajj or Umrah. However, this trick is not allowed for one who is commanded (perhaps meaning a person who has been ordered to perform Hajj or Umrah, or a slave commanded by his master). The phrase 'المأمور' likely refers to someone who is under an obligation to perform Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-hīla): A legal trick to achieve a permissible outcome; here, entering Mecca without ihram by not intending Hajj/Umrah.
فتح مكة (Fatḥ Makkah): The Conquest of Mecca; an exemption from the requirement of ihram for entry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the legal trick (hila) for a person inside the miqat to enter Mecca without ihram?
A) He must intend to perform Umrah instead.
B) He may enter if he does not intend Hajj or Umrah.
C) He must be accompanied by a guide.
D) There is no trick; ihram is always required.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of ihram for entering Mecca is general, but residents inside the miqat may avoid it if they do not intend Hajj or Umrah.

Entering Makkah Without Ihram: Ruling and the Prohibited Trick for the Obliged Pilgrim
Explains the general rule of ihram for entering Makkah and the limited exception for those inside the miqat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering Makkah without ihram and distinguish when the legal trick (hila) is permissible versus prohibited.

Core Idea
Entering Makkah without ihram is generally prohibited; the exception for those inside the miqat is forbidden for the obligated pilgrim.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on entering Makkah without ihram. The general rule requires ihram from the miqat for anyone intending to enter Makkah, regardless of purpose. However, a narrow exception exists for those already inside the miqat who do not intend Hajj or Umrah. But this exception is strictly denied to those commanded to perform Hajj, ensuring the miqat obligation is fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is entering Makkah without ihram. The general ruling is that it is prohibited for all, based on the sanctity of Makkah and the hadith. However, an exception is made for the Prophet's day of conquest, which is not a precedent for others.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Makkah is sacred; it was not made lawful for anyone after me, and it was made lawful for me only for an hour of a day.' This establishes the general prohibition.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لم تحل لأحد بعدي' (it was not made lawful for anyone after me) indicates the prohibition for all generations after the Prophet. The exception 'أحلت لي ساعة' (made lawful for me for an hour) confirms the general rule for others.
Thus, entering without ihram is only permissible if a specific, strong evidence allows it.
4
Understand the hila (trick)
The text then gives a trick: one who is already inside the miqat may enter Makkah without ihram if they do not intend Hajj or Umrah. This is because the miqat is for those outside; those inside are regarded as residents.
This is a practical concession but must not be abused.
5
Identify the exception for the ma'mur
The author explicitly states that this trick is not permissible for the one commanded to perform Hajj (such as a deputy or one performing obligatory Hajj). Doing so would make his travel not for Hajj and violate the requirement of an 'Afaqi' Hajj (starting from the miqat).
This frequently occurs in sea travel to Jeddah; the obligated pilgrim may not use this trick to avoid ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق في الإحرام فشمل إحرام الحج وإحرام العمرة لأنه لا فرق بينهما في حق الآفاق، وشمل ما إذا كان قاصداً عند المجاوزة الحج أو العمرة أو التجارة أو القتال أو غير ذلك بعد أن يكون قد قصد دخول مكة لأن الإحرام لتعظيم هذه البقعة الشريفة فاستوى فيه الكل وأما دخوله مكة بغير إحرام يوم الفتح فكان مختصاً بتلك الساعة بدليل قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في ذلك اليوم «مكة حرام لم تحل لأحد بعدي وإنما أحلت لي ساعة من نهار ثم عادت حراماً» (۱) يعني الدخول بغير إحرام لإجماع المسلمين على حل الدخول بعده عليه الصلاة والسلام للقتال وقيدنا بقصد مكة لأن الآفاقي إذا قصد موضعاً من الحل كخليص يجوز له أن يتجاوز الميقات غير محرم وإذا وصل إليه التحق بأهله، ومن كان داخل الميقات فله أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام إذا لم يقصد الحج أو العمرة وهي الحيلة لمن أراد أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام. وينبغي أن لا تجوز هذه الحيلة للمأمور بالحج لأنه حينئذ لم يكن سفره للحج ولأنه مأمور بحجة آفاقية، وإذا دخل مكة بغير إحرام صارت حجته مكية فكان مخالفاً، وهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها فيمن يسافر في البحر الملح وهو مأمور بالحج ويكون ذلك في وسط السنة فهل له أن يقصد البندر المعروف بجدة ليدخل مكة بغير إحرام حتى لا يطول الإحرام عليه لو أحرم بالحج فإن المأمور بالحج ليس له أن يحرم بالعمرة .
It [the ruling] is absolute concerning ihram, including ihram for Hajj and ihram for Umrah because there is no difference between them with respect to the people of the horizons. It also includes if one, when passing [the miqat], intends Hajj or Umrah or trade or fighting or other than that, after having intended to enter Makkah, because ihram is for honoring this noble place, so all are equal in it. As for his entering Makkah without ihram on the day of the Conquest, it was specific to that time due to the proof of his ﷺ saying on that day: 'Makkah is sacred; it was not made lawful for anyone after me, and it was made lawful for me only for an hour of a day, then it returned to being sacred.' That is, entering without ihram, because of the consensus of the Muslims on the permissibility of entering after him ﷺ for fighting. And we restricted it by intending Makkah because if a person from the horizons intends a place in the Hal (outside the Haram) like Khulays, he may pass the miqat without ihram, and when he reaches it, he joins his family. And whoever is inside the miqat may enter Makkah without ihram if he does not intend Hajj or Umrah, and this is the trick for one who wants to enter Makkah without ihram. And it is not permissible to allow this trick for the one commanded to perform Hajj, because then his travel would not be for Hajj, and because he is commanded to perform an Afaqi Hajj, and if he enters Makkah without ihram, his Hajj becomes Makki, so he is disobedient. This matter frequently occurs for those who travel on the salt sea and are commanded to perform Hajj, and it happens in the middle of the year. So, is he allowed to head to the known port of Jeddah to enter Makkah without ihram so that the ihram does not become long for him if he were to assume ihram for Hajj? For the one commanded to perform Hajj is not allowed to assume ihram for Umrah.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the ruling of ihram for those entering Makkah. The author first states that the ruling on ihram applies equally to those intending Hajj, Umrah, trade, fighting, or any other purpose, as long as they intend to enter Makkah. He then notes an exception: entering Makkah without ihram on the day of the Conquest was specific to the Prophet ﷺ, as proven by the hadith. The author then provides a practical trick (hila) for those who want to enter Makkah without ihram: if a person is already inside the miqat (the boundary of the Haram), they may enter Makkah without ihram as long as they do not intend Hajj or Umrah. However, he strongly cautions that this trick is not permissible for someone who is obligated to perform Hajj (e.g., a deputy performing Hajj on behalf of another or someone performing their own obligatory Hajj). The reason is that such a person's travel should be specifically for Hajj, and if they enter Makkah without ihram, their Hajj would be considered a 'Makki' Hajj (i.e., starting from Makkah), which would violate the requirement to start from the miqat. This situation often arises for those traveling by sea to Jeddah; they might be tempted to enter Makkah without ihram to avoid the burdens of ihram. The author clarifies that such a person should not be allowed to do so, and moreover, if they are commanded to perform Hajj, they cannot switch to Umrah.

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-hila): The legal trick or stratagem to enter Makkah without ihram by being inside the miqat and not intending Hajj/Umrah.
المأمور بالحج (al-ma'mur bi al-hajj): A person who is commanded to perform Hajj, either as an obligation for themselves or as a deputy for someone else.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, is it permissible for a person who is commanded to perform Hajj (e.g., a deputy) to use the trick of entering Makkah without ihram by stating they are not intending Hajj/Umrah?
A) Yes, it is permissible because the trick is based on a valid legal principle.
B) No, it is not permissible because doing so would make their Hajj invalid.
C) Yes, but only if they are traveling by sea.
D) No, it is not permissible because they would be violating the condition to perform an Afaqi Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The hila of entering Makkah without ihram is only permissible for those not obligated to perform Hajj; the ma'mur must enter with ihram to fulfill the miqat requirement.

The Deputy's Ihram from the Miqat: Can Returning Rectify Violation?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on deputy's ihram from miqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a deputy who passes the miqat without ihram, identify the opposing view within the school, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A deputy who passes the miqat without ihram becomes a violator; returning to the miqat does not save the deputyship according to the relied-upon view.

This passage dives into a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person appointed to perform Hajj for another passes the miqat without entering ihram, can he later return to the miqat and rectify, or is his deputyship invalidated? The commentator reviews authoritative texts that declare him a violator, but notes some later scholars held a more lenient view. Understanding this dispute clarifies the strict conditions of deputyship in Hajj and the weight of transmitted authority versus reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon view from the texts cited (al-Muhit, al-Khaniyya): the deputy is a violator and his Hajj for the principal does not count, even if he returns to the miqat later.
This is based on the condition that the deputy must enter ihram from the miqat at the outset.
2
Identify the opposing view
Some later Hanafi scholars (al-Sindi, Qutb al-Din, Sinan al-Rumi, 'Ali al-Maqdisi) held that returning to the miqat and entering ihram there is sufficient.
They argue the condition is not absolute; it can be rectified by later action.
3
Follow the proofs for each side
The strict view relies on transmitted texts (al-Muhit, al-Khaniyya). The lenient view is based on the claim that the condition needs a definitive proof (dalil qat'i) and that a later scholar's statement without evidence is insufficient.
The commentator questions the reliability of al-Sindi's statement without attribution to a mujtahid.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator points out that the matter is transmitted from earlier authorities, and the muqallid follows the mujtahid even if the proof is not apparent. He cites al-Tatarkhaniyya and al-Muhit to support the strict view.
The rebuttal emphasizes that the condition is established by the transmitted texts, not by individual reasoning.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the strict view is taken, the deputy's Hajj for the principal is invalid, and he may have to perform Hajj for himself. If lenient, the deputyship can be saved by returning to the miqat.
This has practical implications for those arranging Hajj on behalf of others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وصح تقديمه عليها لا عكسه) أي جاز تقديم الإحرام على المواقيت ولا يجوز تأخير عنها . أما الأول فلقوله تعالى وأتموا الحج والعمرة لله وفسرت الصحابة الإتمام بأن يحرم بها من دويرة أهله ومن الأماكن القاصية. وقال عليه السلام من أهل من المسجد الأقصى بحجة أو بعمرة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه وما تأخر رواه الإمام أحمد. ولم يتكلم المصنف على أفضلية التقديم وعدمها لما أن فيه تفصيلاً ذكره في الكافي وهو أن التقديم أفضل إذا كان يملك نفسه أن لا يقع في محظور لأن المشقة فيه أكثر فكان أكثر ثواباً لأن الأجر بقدر من قولهم المنقول سابقاً ومن كان في بحر أو بر لا يمر بواحد من هذه المواقيت الخ قوله : (لأنه حينئذ لم يكن سفره للحج هذا التعليل يفيد أنه لا ترتفع المخالفة بخروجه بعد إلى أحد المواقيت وإحرامه منه، ونقل كلام المؤلف هنا الشيخ حنيف الدين المرشدي في شرح منسكه وأقره ونقله عنه القاضي محمد عيد في شرح منسكه كما في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار ثم قال فيها: ونقل المنلا علي القاري في رسالته المسماة بيان فعل الخير إذا دخل مكة من حج عن الغير أنه وقعت مسألة اضطرب فيها فقهاء العصر وهي أن الآفاقي الحاج عن الغير إذا انفصل عن الميقات بغير إحرام للحج مخالف أم لا؟ فقيل نعم فيبطل حجه عن الآمر وإن عاد إلى الميقات وأحرم، وقيل لا بل عليه إلى الميقات ويحرم عن الآمر واعتمد الأولون على ظاهر ما في المنسك الكبير للسندي أن من شروط صحة الحج عن الآمر أن يحرم من الميقات فلو اعتمر وقد أمره بالحج ثم حج من . يضمن في قولهم جميعاً ولا يجوز ذلك عن حجة الإسلام لأنه مأمور بحجة ميقاتية ا هـ . الاعتماد عليه لأن الشرط فرض لا يثبت إلا بدليل قطعي فمجرد قوله من غير نقله عن مجتهد وإسناده إلى دليل غير مقبول وأطال إلى أن قال وبما ذكرناه أفتى الشيخ قطب الدين وشيخنا سنان الرومي في منسكه، وأفتى به أيضاً الشيخ على المقدسي ونقل فتواه فراجعها ا هـ. ما في الحاشية ملخصاً. أقول: وفي رده ما ذكره السندي نظر لأن المسألة منقولة والمقلد متبع للمجتهد وإن لم يظهر دليله، ففي التتارخانية عن المحيط : ولو أمره بالحج فاعتمر ثم حج من مكة فهو مخالف في قولهم. وفي الخانية : ولا يجوز ذلك عن حجة الإسلام عن نفسه، وكذا لو حج ثم اعترم كان مخالفاً عند العامة. وفي المحيط : ولو أمره بالعمرة فاعتمر أولاً ثم حج عن نفسه لم يكن مخالفاً، وإن حج أولاً ثم اعتمر فهو مخالف ا هـ . فليتأمل. فقد يقال : إنه جعل مخالفاً لكونه أحرم أو لا بغير ما أمر به فقد جعل سفره لنفسه فلا يدل على اشتراط إحرام المأمور من الميقات وأنه لا يقع . عن الأمر وإن عاد إلى مكة ولا يصح
His statement: 'And its advance is valid over it, not the opposite' means that advancing the ihram before the miqat is permissible, but delaying it beyond the miqat is not permissible. As for the first, due to the Almighty's saying: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah.' The Companions interpreted 'completion' as entering into ihram from one's home and from distant places. And he ﷺ said: 'Whoever enters into ihram from the Aqsa Mosque for Hajj or Umrah, his past and future sins are forgiven.' Narrated by Imam Ahmad. The author did not discuss the preference of advancing or not because there is detail mentioned in al-Kafi: advancing is better if one can control himself from falling into prohibition, because the hardship is greater, so the reward is greater, as the reward is according to [hardship]. From their statement transmitted earlier: 'And whoever is on sea or land and does not pass any of these miqat...' His statement: 'because then his travel was not for Hajj' – this reason indicates that the violation is not removed by his later going to one of the miqat and entering into ihram from it. Sheikh Hanif al-Din al-Murshidi narrated the author's statement here in his commentary on al-Mansak and approved it, and Qadi Muhammad 'Eid narrated it from him in his commentary on al-Mansak, as in the Hashiya of al-Madani on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. Then he said in it: And al-Mulla 'Ali al-Qari narrated in his treatise called Bayan Fi'l al-Khayr... that a matter occurred about which the contemporary jurists differed: is the Afaqi pilgrim performing Hajj for another, if he passed the miqat without ihram for Hajj, a violator or not? Some said yes, so his Hajj for the one who commanded him is invalid even if he returns to the miqat and enters into ihram. Others said no, but he must go to the miqat and enter into ihram for the one who commanded him. The former relied on the apparent meaning of what is in al-Mansak al-Kabir by al-Sindi that from the conditions for the validity of Hajj for the one who commanded is that he enter into ihram from the miqat. So if he performed Umrah while having been commanded to perform Hajj, then performed Hajj from... they are all liable in their saying, and that is not permissible for the Hajj of Islam because he is commanded to perform a miqat-based Hajj. End quote. To rely on it because the condition is a stipulation that is not established except by a definitive proof, so mere saying without transmitting from a mujtahid and attributing it to a proof is unacceptable. And he elaborated until he said: 'And with what we have mentioned, Sheikh Qutb al-Din and our master Sinan al-Rumi gave fatwa in his Mansak, and Sheikh 'Ali al-Maqdisi also gave fatwa and its fatwa was transmitted, so refer to it.' End quote from the Hashiya summarized. I say: In his refutation of what al-Sindi mentioned, there is consideration because the matter is transmitted and the muqallid follows the mujtahid even if his proof is not apparent. So in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Muhit: 'If he commanded him to perform Hajj and he performed Umrah then performed Hajj from Makkah, he is a violator in their saying.' And in al-Khaniyya: 'And that is not permissible for the Hajj of Islam for himself, and similarly if he performed Hajj then performed Umrah, he is a violator according to the generality.' And in al-Muhit: 'If he commanded him to perform Umrah, and he performed Umrah first then performed Hajj for himself, he is not a violator, and if he performed Hajj first then performed Umrah, then he is a violator.' End quote. So let him ponder. For it may be said: he made him a violator because he entered into ihram or not with something other than what he was commanded, so his travel became for himself, and it does not indicate the condition of the ihram of the commanded from the miqat and that it does not occur for the one who commanded even if he returns to Makkah and it is not valid.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the ruling on advancing ihram before the miqat and the dispute concerning a deputy who passes the miqat without ihram. The commentator begins by explaining the matn's statement 'And its advance is valid over it, not the opposite': it is permissible to enter ihram before the miqat but not after passing it. He supports this with the Quranic command to complete Hajj and Umrah, interpreted by the Companions as entering ihram from one's home, and a hadith about the merits of entering ihram from al-Aqsa. The author then discusses the ruling on advancing ihram, noting that it is recommended (afdal) if one can avoid prohibitions, due to greater hardship and reward. He then turns to the dispute: if a deputy (ma'mur) passes the miqat without ihram, does returning to the miqat and entering ihram there rectify the violation? Some Hanafi scholars say the deputy is a violator (mukhalif) and his Hajj for the principal is invalid even if he returns, citing al-Sindi's condition that the deputy must enter ihram from the miqat. Others say he must return to the miqat and enter ihram, and that is sufficient. The commentator raises a critique: al-Sindi's condition is a stipulation that requires definitive proof, and the mere statement of a later scholar is not sufficient. However, he then cites strong authority from al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Khaniyya, and al-Muhit that the deputy is indeed a violator if he does not enter ihram from the miqat, and that performance of Umrah first or other variations also lead to violation. The commentator suggests that the matter is not straightforward and requires careful consideration (falyata'ammal). The dispute centers on whether the condition of ihram from the miqat is an absolute obligation or can be overlooked if the deputy later returns.

Key Terms
المخالفة (al-mukhalafa): Violation or disobedience of the command to perform Hajj from the miqat.
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The person commanded to perform Hajj, either as an obligation or as a deputy for another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dominant view in the passage, what is the status of a deputy who passes the miqat without ihram but later returns to the miqat and enters ihram?
A) His Hajj for the principal is valid because he eventually entered ihram from the miqat.
B) He is a violator and his Hajj for the principal is invalid.
C) He must perform Umrah first to rectify.
D) He is exempt from the condition because he is a deputy.

Key Takeaway
A deputy who passes the miqat without ihram is a violator, and his Hajj for the principal is invalid even if he returns, according to the relied-upon Hanafi texts.

Passing the Miqat Without Ihram: Ruling and Return
Explains the ruling for a person commanded to perform Hajj who passes the miqat without ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on passing the miqat without ihram and evaluate whether returning to the miqat removes the violation.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram is a violation; returning does not remove it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical question for those performing Hajj, especially on behalf of others: what happens if one passes the miqat without ihram? The author explains that early ihram is valid but delaying is not, and once the miqat is passed without ihram, a violation occurs that is not remedied by later returning to the miqat. This ruling has practical implications for pilgrims traveling by sea or air.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine the specific act: passing the miqat without ihram. The ruling is that it is a violation (mukhalafah) and requires a dam (sacrificial penalty).
The act is wajib from the miqat; omission without valid excuse is makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the textual evidence: Quran 2:196 ('Complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah') and the hadith 'Whoever assumes ihram from the Aqsa Mosque...' and the principle that the miqat must not be passed without ihram.
The hadith is from Imam Ahmad.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling: the imperative 'complete' includes starting ihram from the designated places; the prohibition of passing the miqat without ihram is derived from the command to complete and the practice of the Companions.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (command indicates obligation).
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
There is a dispute among Hanafi scholars: does returning to the miqat and assuming ihram remove the violation? The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it does not; the Hajj for the commissioner is invalid.
Some later scholars (e.g., al-Sindi) held it invalid; others (like Mulla Ali al-Qari) disagreed.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The author (Ibn Nujaym) supports the majority view that passing the miqat without ihram is a violation that is not removed by return, based on the transmitted rulings from the early authorities.
The tarjih authority is the text of al-Bahr al-Raiq itself, which follows Zahir al-Riwayah.

كان دلل
التعب بخلاف التقديم على الأشهر أجمعوا على أنه مكروه من غير تفصيل بين خوف الوقوع في محظور أو لا كما أطلقه في المجمع. ومن فصل كصاحب الظهيرية قياساً على الميقات المكاني فقد أخطأ، وإنما كره مطلقاً قبل الميقات الزماني شبهه بالركن وإن كان شرطاً فيراعي مقتضى ذلك الشبه احتياطاً ولو كان ركناً حقيقة لم يصح قبل أشهر الحج فإن كان شبيهاً به كره قبلها لشبهه وقربه من عدم الصحة ولشبه الركن لم يجز لفائت الحج استدامة الإحرام ليقضى به من قابل وأما الثاني فلقوله عليه السلام لا يجاوز أحد الميقات إلا محرماً وفائدة التاقيت بالمواقيت الخمسة المنع من التأخير قوله (ولداخلها الحل) أي الحل ميقات من المواقيت، وهو بكسر الحاء المواضع التي بين المواقيت والحرم، ولا فرق بين أن يكون في نفس الميقات أو بعده كما نص عليه محمد في كتبه. وقول المحقق في فتح القدير المتبادر من هذه العبارة أن يكون بعد المواقيت غير مسلم بل المتبادر منها من كان فيها نفسها وهو غير مقصود للمصنفين وإنما المقصود الإطلاق كما ذكرنا وإنما كان الحل ميقاته لأن خارج الحرم كله كمكان واحد في حقه والحرم حد في حقه كالميقات للآفاقي فلا يدخل الحرم عند قصد النسك إلا محرماً، وأما عند عدم هذا القصد فله الدخول بغير إحرام للحاجة والضرورة

قال :
الميقات إذا لم يفعل أولاً نسكاً لم يؤمر به، فينبغي التفصيل وهو أنه إن جاوز الميقات بلا إحرام قاصداً البستان ثم دخل مكة ثم خرج إلى الحل وقت الإحرام فأحرم من الميقات عن الآمر يجوز لأنه صار آفاقياً كما يأتي، وإن فعل نسكاً غير ما أمر به قبل إحرامه عن الأمر يكون مخالفاً وإن عاد إلى الميقات وأحرم عنه من الميقات فتأمل قوله : (أجمعوا على أنه مكروه الخ كذا نقل القهستاني الإجماع عن ا التحفة وفي المحيط إن أمن من الوقوع في محظور الإحرام لا يكره، وفي النظم عنه أنه يكره إلا عند أبي يوسف قوله : (فلا يدخل الحرم عند قصد النسك إلا محرماً) قال العلامة الشيخ قطب الدين في منسكه : ومما يجب التيقظ له سكان جدة - بالجيم - وأهل حدة - بالمهملة - وأهل الأودية القريبة من مكة فإنهم في الأغلب يأتون إلى مكة في سادس ذي الحجة أو في السابع بغير إحرام ويحرمون من مكة للحج؛ فعلى من كان حنفياً منهم أن يحرم بالحج قبل أن يدخل الحرم وإلا فعليه لمجاوزة الميقات بغير إحرام لكن للنظر هنا مجال إذا أحرم هؤلاء من مكة كما هو معتادهم وتوجهوا إلى عرفة ينبغي أن يسقط عنهم دم المجاوزة بوصولهم إلى أول الحل ملبين لأنه عود منهم إلى ميقاتهم مع الإحرام والتلبية وذلك مسقط لدم المجاوزة، اللهم إلا أن يقال: لا يعد هذا عوداً . منهم إلى الميقات لأنهم لم يقصدوا العود إليه لتلافي ما لزمهم بالمجاوزة بل قصدوا التوجه إلى عرفة ولم أجد من تعرض لذلك والله أعلم بالصواب ا هـ. وقد نقله الشيخ عبد الله العفيف في شرحه وأقره. وقال القاضي محمد عيد في شرح منسكه : والظاهر السقوط لأن العود إلى الميقات مع التلبية مسقط ، سواء نوى العود أو لم ينو، لحصول المقصود الذي هو كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار .
By Hajj because then his travel was not for Hajj, and because he is commanded to perform an Afaqi Hajj. If he enters Mecca without ihram, his Hajj becomes Meccan and he is in violation. This issue frequently occurs for those traveling by sea and commanded to perform Hajj in the middle of the year: may he head to Jeddah to enter Mecca without ihram so that the ihram does not prolong? Indeed, the one commanded to perform Hajj may not perform Umrah. His statement: (And its preceding over them is valid, not the opposite) meaning it is permissible to perform ihram before the miqat and not permissible to delay it. As for the first, due to His saying: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah', and the Companions interpreted completion as performing ihram from one's residence and distant places. And he said peace be upon him: 'Whoever assumes ihram from the Aqsa Mosque for Hajj or Umrah, his past and future sins are forgiven' narrated by Imam Ahmad. The author did not discuss the preference of early ihram because there is detail mentioned in al-Kafi: early ihram is better if one can avoid prohibitions because the hardship is greater so the reward is greater. His statement: (Because then his travel was not for Hajj) indicates that the violation is not removed by later going to a miqat and ihram from there. Sheikh Hanifuddin narrated the author's words and approved. Then he said: al-Mulla Ali al-Qari transmitted a case about which contemporaries disputed: if an Afaqi performing Hajj on behalf of another separates from the miqat without ihram for Hajj, is he in violation? It was said yes, so his Hajj for the commissioner is invalid even if he returns to the miqat and assumes ihram. And it was said no, rather he must go to the miqat and assume ihram for the commissioner. The former relied on al-Sindi's condition that ihram from miqat is a condition. The response: the condition is not established by a definitive proof. Then he said: by what we mentioned, Sheikh Qutb al-Din and our teacher Sinan al-Rumi gave fatwa, and also Sheikh Ali al-Maqdisi. I say: there is consideration in rejecting what al-Sindi mentioned because the issue is transmitted and the muqallid follows the mujtahid even if his evidence is not apparent. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Muhit: if he commanded him to perform Hajj and he performed Umrah then Hajj from Mecca, he is in violation in their view. In al-Khaniyya: that is not permissible for the Hajj of Islam on his own behalf...
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Raiq discussing two rulings: (1) the validity of early ihram before the miqat and the illegality of delaying it, and (2) the ruling on one who passes the miqat without ihram, especially when acting on behalf of another. The author cites Quran and Hadith for early ihram and discusses the dispute among later scholars about the sea traveler commanded to perform Hajj who wants to enter Mecca without ihram to avoid a long ihram. The relied-upon position is that passing the miqat without ihram is a violation, and returning to the miqat does not remove the sin; the Hajj for the commissioner is invalid. The passage also touches on the ruling for residents of Jeddah who commonly enter Mecca without ihram and then go to Arafat; the fatwa of Qutb al-Din suggests that if they go to the Hill with ihram and talbiya, the blood of violation is waived. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each matn fragment.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): The designated place or time for beginning ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by reciting the talbiya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Miqat Rulings for Residents of the Hal and the Makki
Explains miqat rulings and temporal ihram dislike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the miqat rulings for residents of the hal and the Makki, and explain why early ihram before the months of Hajj is makruh according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The miqat for a Makki is the Haram for Hajj and the hal for Umrah; the hal itself is a miqat for its residents.

The concept of miqat is central to the validity of Hajj and Umrah. The Hanafi school provides specific rules for those living within the miqat boundaries, including residents of the hal (areas between the miqat and the Haram) and the Makki (resident of Mecca). This lesson unpacks these rulings, their evidence from the Sunnah, and a related issue: the dislike of entering ihram before the prescribed months of Hajj. Understanding these distinctions ensures proper observance of the rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of people
Recognize the two groups: (1) those who reside in the hal (the areas between the five miqats and the Haram), and (2) the Makki (someone who is inside the Haram at the time of ihram). For each, state the miqat for Hajj and Umrah as given in the passage.
Residents of the hal have the hal as their miqat for both Hajj and Umrah. For the Makki, the miqat for Hajj is the Haram itself, and for Umrah it is the hal.
2
Examine the proof for the obligation of miqat
The passage cites the hadith: 'Let no one pass the miqat except in ihram.' Analyse the wording (imperative exclusion) to understand that it indicates obligation (wujub). Note also that the purpose of the five miqats is to prevent delay in entering ihram.
The hadith is ahad in transmission (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is definitive (qati al-dalala) in requiring ihram from the miqat.
3
Understand the ruling on early ihram before the months of Hajj
The passage states there is consensus that performing Hajj before its time (i.e., before Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, Dhul-Hijjah) is makruh (disliked). Some scholars made a distinction based on analogy to spatial miqat, but the Hanafi authors reject that. The dislike is due to resemblance to the rukn of Hajj, even though ihram is only a condition. This precautionary approach is taken because if it were a true rukn, it would be invalid; its resemblance makes it disliked.
This is a different issue from the spatial miqat. It relates to the temporal miqat (the months of Hajj).
4
Clarify the definition and scope of the hal as a miqat
The passage explains that the hal includes all areas between the miqats and the Haram. There is no difference whether one is at the miqat itself or beyond it—the entire hal area is the miqat for its residents. The author refutes the interpretation that the expression 'those inside it' refers to those after the miqat; rather, it refers to those within the hal itself. The proof is that all of outside the Haram is like one place for such a person, and the Haram acts as a boundary.
The hal is considered a miqat because the Haram is the boundary; one must not enter it for nusk without ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج ولداخلها الحل وللمكي الحرم للحج والحل للعمرة . . كان دلل التعب بخلاف التقديم على الأشهر أجمعوا على أنه مكروه من غير تفصيل بين خوف الوقوع في محظور أو لا كما أطلقه في المجمع. ومن فصل كصاحب الظهيرية قياساً على الميقات المكاني فقد أخطأ، وإنما كره مطلقاً قبل الميقات الزماني شبهه بالركن وإن كان شرطاً فيراعي مقتضى ذلك الشبه احتياطاً ولو كان ركناً حقيقة لم يصح قبل أشهر الحج فإن كان شبيهاً به كره قبلها لشبهه وقربه من عدم الصحة ولشبه الركن لم يجز لفائت الحج استدامة الإحرام ليقضى به من قابل وأما الثاني فلقوله عليه السلام لا يجاوز أحد الميقات إلا محرماً وفائدة التاقيت بالمواقيت الخمسة المنع من التأخير قوله (ولداخلها الحل) أي الحل ميقات من المواقيت، وهو بكسر الحاء المواضع التي بين المواقيت والحرم، ولا فرق بين أن يكون في نفس الميقات أو بعده كما نص عليه محمد في كتبه. وقول المحقق في فتح القدير المتبادر من هذه العبارة أن يكون بعد المواقيت غير مسلم بل المتبادر منها من كان فيها نفسها وهو غير مقصود للمصنفين وإنما المقصود الإطلاق كما ذكرنا وإنما كان الحل ميقاته لأن خارج الحرم كله كمكان واحد في حقه والحرم حد في حقه كالميقات للآفاقي فلا يدخل الحرم عند قصد النسك إلا محرماً، وأما عند عدم هذا القصد فله الدخول بغير إحرام للحاجة والضرورة
Book of Hajj: And for those inside it (the miqat) is the hal, and for the Makki, the Haram for Hajj and the hal for Umrah. ... With the exception of performing (Hajj) before the months (of Hajj), they are agreed upon that it is disliked without distinction between fear of falling into a prohibition or not, as he (the author of al-Majma') stated absolutely. And whoever makes a distinction, like the author of al-Zahiriyya, by analogy to the spatial miqat, has erred. Rather, it was absolutely disliked before the temporal miqat because of its resemblance to the pillar (rukn), even though it is a condition. So the requirement of that resemblance is taken into account out of precaution. If it were actually a pillar, it would not be valid before the months of Hajj. Since it resembles it, it is disliked before them due to its resemblance and its closeness to invalidity. And due to the resemblance to the pillar, it is not permissible for one who missed Hajj to continue ihram to perform it the next year. As for the second (proof), because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Let no one pass the miqat except in ihram.' And the benefit of specifying the five miqats is to prevent delay. His statement: (And for those inside it is the hal) means the hal is one of the miqats, and it is (with kasr of the ha) the places between the miqats and the Haram. There is no difference between being at the miqat itself or beyond it, as Muhammad stated in his books. The statement of the commentator in Fath al-Qadir 'the apparent from this expression is that it is after the miqats' is not accepted; rather, the apparent is that it is those who are in it (the hal) itself, and that is not intended by the authors; rather, the intended meaning is absolute, as we mentioned. And indeed, the hal is his miqat because all of outside the Haram is like a single place in his regard, and the Haram is a boundary in his regard, like the miqat for the afaqi. So he should not enter the Haram when intending a ritual (nusk) except in ihram. As for when there is no such intent, he may enter without ihram for need and necessity.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of miqat. The author begins by stating the general rule: for those who live inside the miqat boundaries (i.e., in the hal areas between the miqat and the Haram), their miqat is the hal itself. For the Makki (a resident of Mecca), the miqat for Hajj is the Haram and for Umrah is the hal. Then he discusses the kirahah (dislike) of performing Hajj before its prescribed time (the months of Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and Dhul-Hijjah). The author notes that there is consensus that this is makruh, without distinguishing whether one fears committing a prohibited act of ihram or not. He criticizes some scholars like the author of al-Zahiriyya who made a distinction based on analogy to the spatial miqat. The reason for dislike is that performing ihram before its time resembles the actual rukn (pillar) of Hajj, even though it is only a condition. Out of caution, this resemblance is taken into account. He further explains that if it were a true rukn, it would be invalid; since it only resembles it, it is disliked. Then he provides proof from the hadith 'None should pass the miqat except in ihram' and explains that the purpose of the five miqats is to prevent delay. Commenting on the phrase 'and for those inside it is the hal', he clarifies that the hal is also a miqat, and it is the areas between the miqat and the Haram. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani stated that there is no difference between being at the miqat itself or beyond it—the ruling applies to the entire hal area. The author refutes a claim from Fath al-Qadir that the expression refers to those after the miqat, asserting that it refers to those within the hal itself. The reason the hal is considered a miqat is that all of the outside of the Haram is like one place for them, and the Haram acts as a boundary. Therefore, when intending any nusk (Hajj or Umrah), they must not enter the Haram without ihram. However, if they have no such intent, they may enter without ihram for necessity.

Key Terms
الميقات (al-miqat): The boundary place or time set for entering ihram; here spatial miqat is meant.
الحل (al-hall): The areas outside the Haram but within the miqat boundaries; the permissible zones for those not in ihram.
المكي (al-Makki): A person residing in Mecca or within the Haram; their miqat for Hajj is the Haram itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the miqat for a resident of Mecca (Makki) when performing Hajj?
A) The miqat of the afaqi, e.g., Dhu'l-Hulayfah
B) The hal (outside the Haram)
C) The Haram itself
D) Any place of his choice

Key Takeaway
The hal is a miqat for its residents; the Makki's miqat differs for Hajj (Haram) and Umrah (hal), and early ihram before Hajj months is absolutely disliked.

Passing the Miqat Without Ihram: Ruling and Waiver
Fatwa and legal analysis on passing miqat without ihram and waiver by return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for passing the miqat without ihram and apply the concept of 'return to the miqat' to determine if the dam is waived.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram incurs a dam, but returning to it with ihram and talbiyah can waive the obligation.

In this lesson, you will examine a critical issue in Hajj: what happens if someone passes the miqat without entering the state of ihram? The Hanafi school holds that this is a violation requiring a sacrifice (dam), but there is an important practical escape: if the person later returns to the miqat area while in ihram and making talbiyah, the dam may be waived. This lesson unpacks the ruling, including a fatwa concerning residents of Jeddah who often enter Mecca without ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Violation
Recognize that passing the miqat without ihram is a violation of a wajib requirement.
The miqat is the boundary set by the Prophet for entering ihram.
2
Determine the Consequence
State that the default Hanafi ruling is that a dam (blood sacrifice) is required for the violation.
The dam is a sheep or goat, or equivalent charity.
3
Analyze the Exception: Return to the Miqat
Understand that if the person later returns to the miqat area (the hal) while in ihram and making talbiyah, the dam may be waived. This is based on the principle of 'awn (return) discharging the obligation.
The return must be to the original miqat or the hal, not just any place outside the Haram.
4
Apply to the Jeddah Case
Consider the fatwa of Qutb al-Din: Hanafi residents of Jeddah who enter Mecca without ihram and later leave for Arafat in ihram and talbiyah will pass the hal – this constitutes a return and may waive the dam.
The key is whether the return is intentional; the relied-upon view is that intention is not required.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Recognize that Abu Yusuf holds a different view on the timing of ihram (disliked before its months), but the majority opinion is followed.
The mufta bihi position is that returning to the miqat with ihram waives the dam even if not intended for that purpose.

الميقات إذا لم يفعل أولاً نسكاً لم يؤمر به، فينبغي التفصيل وهو أنه إن جاوز الميقات بلا إحرام قاصداً البستان ثم دخل مكة ثم خرج إلى الحل وقت الإحرام فأحرم من الميقات عن الآمر يجوز لأنه صار آفاقياً كما يأتي، وإن فعل نسكاً غير ما أمر به قبل إحرامه عن الأمر يكون مخالفاً وإن عاد إلى الميقات وأحرم عنه من الميقات فتأمل قوله : (أجمعوا على أنه مكروه الخ كذا نقل القهستاني الإجماع عن ا التحفة وفي المحيط إن أمن من الوقوع في محظور الإحرام لا يكره، وفي النظم عنه أنه يكره إلا عند أبي يوسف قوله : (فلا يدخل الحرم عند قصد النسك إلا محرماً) قال العلامة الشيخ قطب الدين في منسكه : ومما يجب التيقظ له سكان جدة - بالجيم - وأهل حدة - بالمهملة - وأهل الأودية القريبة من مكة فإنهم في الأغلب يأتون إلى مكة في سادس ذي الحجة أو في السابع بغير إحرام ويحرمون من مكة للحج؛ فعلى من كان حنفياً منهم أن يحرم بالحج قبل أن يدخل الحرم وإلا فعليه لمجاوزة الميقات بغير إحرام لكن للنظر هنا مجال إذا أحرم هؤلاء من مكة كما هو معتادهم وتوجهوا إلى عرفة ينبغي أن يسقط عنهم دم المجاوزة بوصولهم إلى أول الحل ملبين لأنه عود منهم إلى ميقاتهم مع الإحرام والتلبية وذلك مسقط لدم المجاوزة، اللهم إلا أن يقال: لا يعد هذا عوداً . منهم إلى الميقات لأنهم لم يقصدوا العود إليه لتلافي ما لزمهم بالمجاوزة بل قصدوا التوجه إلى عرفة ولم أجد من تعرض لذلك والله أعلم بالصواب ا هـ. وقد نقله الشيخ عبد الله العفيف في شرحه وأقره. وقال القاضي محمد عيد في شرح منسكه : والظاهر السقوط لأن العود إلى الميقات مع التلبية مسقط ، سواء نوى العود أو لم ينو، لحصول المقصود الذي هو كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار . التعظيم ا هـ.
The miqat: if one did not initially perform a nusk (ritual), he is not commanded to do so. It is appropriate to distinguish: if he passed the miqat without ihram intending a garden (bustan), then entered Mecca, then went out to the hal at the time of ihram and performed ihram from the miqat for the command (of Hajj), it is permissible because he has become an afaqi (a non-resident) as will come. If he performed a nusk other than the one commanded before his ihram for the command, he would be violating. And if he returned to the miqat and performed ihram from it, then contemplate. His statement: (they agreed that it is disliked...) Similarly, al-Qahistani transmitted consensus from al-Tuhfah, but in al-Muhit, if one is secure from falling into a prohibited act of ihram, it is not disliked. In al-Nazm, it is disliked except according to Abu Yusuf. His statement: (He should not enter the Haram when intending a nusk except in ihram.) The scholar Shaykh Qutb al-Din said in his Manasik: Among the things one must be alert to are the residents of Jeddah (with a jim) and the people of Hadda (with a important ha) and the people of the valleys near Mecca, for they often come to Mecca on the 6th or 7th of Dhul-Hijjah without ihram and then perform ihram from Mecca for Hajj. It is obligatory for those who are Hanafi among them to perform ihram for Hajj before entering the Haram; otherwise, they are liable for the blood (dam) for passing the miqat without ihram. However, there is room for consideration here. If these people perform ihram from Mecca as is their custom then head to Arafat, it should be that the blood for overstepping the miqat is waived by their arrival at the first part of the hal while making talbiyah, because this is a return to their miqat with ihram and talbiyah, and that does waive the blood for overstepping. Unless it is said: this is not considered a return to the miqat because they did not intend to return to make up for what was owed by overstepping, rather they intended to go to Arafat. I have not found anyone who addressed this. And Allah knows best what is correct. This was reported by Shaykh Abd Allah al-Afif in his commentary and he approved it. And Qadi Muhammad Eid said in his commentary on the Manasik: The apparent view is that it is waived because returning to the miqat with talbiyah waives it, whether one intended to return or not, because the purpose is achieved. This is in the Hashiya of al-Madani on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. Al-Ta'zim (?) end.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage deals with the specific scenario of someone who passes the miqat without ihram. The author first distinguishes between different intentions. If one passes the miqat without ihram to go to a garden (i.e., a non-ritual purpose), then enters Mecca, then later goes out to the hal with the intention of performing Hajj and performs ihram from the miqat, this is permissible because he then becomes like an afaqi (a non-resident) who can use the miqat. However, if he performs a nusk other than the one commanded (e.g., Umrah instead of Hajj), then he would be violating the order. The author then discusses the famous ruling that performing ihram before its time is disliked, but notes that al-Muhit qualifies it: if one is safe from committing prohibited acts of ihram, it is not disliked. Abu Yusuf also holds a different view. The main body of the passage is a practical fatwa from Qutb al-Din al-Hanafi regarding residents of Jeddah and similar areas. They often come to Mecca on the 6th or 7th of Dhul-Hijjah without ihram and then enter Mecca without ihram, then perform ihram from Mecca for Hajj. According to the Hanafi school, this is problematic because they have passed the miqat (the hal is their miqat) without ihram. They should have performed ihram before entering the Haram. However, Qutb al-Din suggests that if they then leave Mecca with ihram and talbiyah heading to Arafat, they will pass through the hal again. This return to the hal with ihram and talbiyah may discharge the blood obligation (dam) for having passed the miqat initially. He notes that some might argue this is not a true return because their intention is not to make up for the overstepping but just to go to Arafat. Qutb al-Din says he hasn't found anyone who explicitly addressed this. Later, Qadi Muhammad Eid and others held that the blood is waived because the purpose of returning to the miqat—i.e., being in ihram while in the hal—is achieved, regardless of intention.

Key Terms
دم المجاوزة (dam al-mujawaza): The blood sacrifice required for passing the miqat without ihram.
العود إلى الميقات (al-'awd ila al-miqat): Returning to the miqat area after having passed it, while in ihram, which may expiate the violation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Dam is obligatory and not waived
B) Dam is waived upon reaching the hal with ihram and talbiyah
C) Dam is waived only if they intended to return to the miqat
D) They must repeat the Hajj

Key Takeaway
Passing the miqat without ihram requires a dam, but returning to it in ihram with talbiyah waives the obligation, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Legal Definition of Ihram: Intention with Dhikr or Specificity
Legal definition with conditions and preparatory acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi shar'i definition of ihram, list its essential conditions, and distinguish between the functions of intention and dhikr in its realization.

Core Idea
Ihram is not just clothing—it is a state entered by intention joined with dhikr or a specific act of the nusk.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the legal (shar'i) meaning of ihram, distinguishing it from its linguistic roots. It establishes that ihram is realized through the intention of performing Hajj or Umrah together with a verbal or physical expression. Understanding this definition is crucial because it sets the foundation for the obligations and prohibitions of the sacred state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and legal definitions
Note the multiple linguistic meanings: entering a sacred state, entering the Haram, entering the sacred month. The legal definition is specifically the intention of the nusk with dhikr or specificity.
2
Break down the legal definition into its components
The two required components: intention (niyyah) and either dhikr (like talbiyah) or a specific act (like driving a hadi). Note that these are conditions, not parts of the essence, as stated in al-Fath.
The author quotes al-Nahr and al-Fath to emphasize this point.
3
Compare with the analogy to prayer
Ihram is likened to takbir al-iftitah in prayer—both are conditions for validity and involve a transition from permissible to prohibited states. However, Hajj ihram is stronger because one cannot exit except by completing the nusk, even if corrupted, and it must be made up even if entered under a mistaken obligation.
This comparison highlights the unique binding nature of ihram.
4
Identify the recommended preparations
Wudu and ghusl are recommended (sunnah muakkadah) for cleanliness, not for ritual purity, as indicated by the earlier chapter on ghusl.
These are not conditions for ihram validity.
5
Recognize the dispute on the definition of 'Makki'
The author criticizes a narrow definition of Makki as only a resident of Mecca proper, arguing that it includes those in the Haram area without evidence.
This is a minor intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإحرام . منعه . أحرم الرجل إذا دخل في حرمة لا تنتهك من ذمة وغيرها، وأحرم للحج لأنه يحرم عليه ما يحل لغيره من الصيد والنساء ونحو ذلك، وأحرم الرجل إذا دخل في الحرم أو دخل في الشهر الحرام، وأحرمه لغة في حرمه العطية أي . كذا في ضياء الحلوم مختصر شمس العلوم. وهو في الشريعة نية النسك من حج أو عمرة مع الذكر أو الخصوصية على ما سيأتي. وهو شرط صحة النسك كتكبيرة الافتتاح في الصلاة فالصلاة والحج لهما تحريم وتحليل بخلاف الصوم والزكاة لكن الحج أقوى من غيره من وجهين : الأول أنه إذا تم الإحرام للحج أو للعمرة لا يخرج عنه إلا بعمل النسك الذي أحرم به وإن أفسده إلا في الفوات فبعمل العمرة وإلا الإخصار فبذبح الهدي . الثاني أنه لا بد من قضائه مطلقاً ولو كان مظنوناً ، فلو أحرم بالحج على ظن أنه عليه ثم ظهر خلافه وجب عليه المضي فيه والقضاء إن أبطله بخلاف المظنون في الصلاة فإنه لا قضاء لو أفسده قوله (وإذا أردت أن تحرم فتوضأ والغسل أفضل) قد تقدم دليله في الغسل وهو للنظافة لا للطهارة قوله : (والمراد بالمكي الخ) فسر في النهر المكي بساكن مكة وقال: أما القار في حرمها فليس بمكي وإن أعطى حكمه واعترض المؤلف بأن ما قاله من التعميم عدول عن المعنى الحقيقي بلا دليل . باب الإحرام قوله : (وهو في الشريعة نية النسك الخ) قال في النهر : هو - شرعاً ـ الدخول في حرمات مخصوصة أي التزامها غير أنه لا يتحقق شرعاً إلا بالنية مع الذكر والخصوصية. كذا في الفتح. فهما شرطان في تحققه لا جزآن لماهيته كما توهمه في البحر قوله : (أو الخصوصية) قال الرملي : أي الإتيان بشيء من خصوصيات النسك، سواء كان تلبية أو ذكراً يقصد به التعظيم أو سوق الهدي أو تقليد
Chapter of Ihram. Its prevention. A man performs ihram if he enters into a sacred state that cannot be violated, from a pledge (dhimma) or other. And he performs ihram for Hajj because it prohibits him what is permitted for others, such as hunting, women, and the like. And a man performs ihram if he enters the Haram or enters the sacred month. And 'ahramahu' linguistically from 'haramahu al-atiyya' meaning. As in Diya' al-Hulum, abridgement of Shams al-Ulum. And it is in the Shari'ah: the intention of a nusk, whether Hajj or Umrah, along with dhikr or specificity (khushusiyya), as will come. And it is a condition for the validity of the nusk, like the takbir al-iftitah in prayer. So prayer and Hajj have both tahrīm (prohibition) and tahlīl (analysis), unlike fasting and zakat. But Hajj is stronger than others in two ways: first, when ihram is completed for Hajj or Umrah, one cannot exit it except by performing the nusk for which he performed ihram, even if he corrupts it, except in the case of fawat (missing the time) then by performing Umrah, and in ihsar (prevention) then by sacrificing a hadi. Second, it is necessary to make it up absolutely, even if it was speculative (maznun). So if one performs ihram for Hajj thinking it is obligatory upon him, then it becomes known that it is not, he must proceed and make it up if he nullifies it, unlike the speculative case in prayer where there is no make-up if nullified. His statement: (When you intend to perform ihram, perform wudu, and ghusl is better) has previously appeared in the chapter on ghusl, and it is for cleanliness, not for purification. His statement: (And the meaning of Makki...) was explained in al-Nahr as a resident of Mecca, and he said: As for the one in its Haram (outside Mecca), he is not a Makki, even if given its ruling. The author objected that what he said is a deviation from the true meaning without evidence. Chapter of Ihram. His statement: (And it is in Shari'ah: the intention of nusk...) said in al-Nahr: It is, according to Shari'ah, entering into specific prohibitions (hurmāt), i.e., undertaking them, except that it is not realized in Shari'ah except with intention along with dhikr and specificity. This is in al-Fath. So they are two conditions for its realization, not two parts of its essence, as was misunderstood in al-Bahr. His statement: (or specificity) said al-Ramli: meaning performing something specific to the nusk, whether talbiyah or dhikr intended for glorification, or driving a sacrificial animal, or marking it (taqlid).
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines ihram and discusses its prerequisites. It begins with a linguistic explanation: ihram means entering a sacred inviolable state. For Hajj, it prohibits otherwise permissible acts like hunting and marital relations. It also means entering the Haram or the sacred month. The legal (shar'i) definition is 'the intention of a nusk (Hajj or Umrah) along with dhikr (e.g., talbiyah) or specificity (e.g., wearing ihram garments, driving a sacrificial animal).' The author likens ihram to takbir al-iftitah in prayer: both are conditions for validity and involve a transition from permissible to prohibited states. However, Hajj is stronger than prayer in two ways: (1) Once in ihram, you cannot exit except by completing that specific nusk, even if you corrupt it (except in specific cases like fawat: if you miss the time for Hajj, you can exit by performing Umrah; or ihsar: if prevented, you sacrifice a hadi). (2) You must complete and make up the Hajj under any circumstances, even if your initial obligation was uncertain. For example, if you thought Hajj was obligatory upon you and then find it is not, you must still complete it and make it up if you nullify it. This contrasts with prayer where a speculative obligation does not require making up. The author then mentions the recommendation of wudu and that ghusl is better before ihram, noting that this is for cleanliness, not ritual purity. He also addresses a dispute about the definition of 'Makki' (resident of Mecca): some scholars defined it as a resident of Mecca proper, excluding those in the surrounding Haram area, but the author criticizes this as deviation from the true meaning. Finally, he returns to the definition of ihram, quoting al-Nahr and al-Fath: ihram is the undertaking of specific prohibitions, realized only by intention with dhikr and specificity. These are conditions, not parts of the essence. Al-Ramli explains that 'specificity' includes things like talbiyah, dhikr, driving a hadi, or taqlid.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by intention accompanied by dhikr or specific acts.
النية (al-niyyah): The intention of performing Hajj or Umrah; a condition for the validity of ihram.
الخصوصية (al-khususiyyah): Specific acts of the nusk such as talbiyah, dhikr, driving a hadi, or marking the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Just the intention without any verbal expression
B) Intention accompanied by dhikr or a specific act of the nusk
C) Wearing two white cloths only
D) Performing wudu and ghusl

Key Takeaway
Ihram is legally defined as the intention of the nusk accompanied by dhikr or a specific act; both are conditions, not parts of its essence.

Ihram Entry and Miqat for the Makki
Practical rulings for ihram and miqat for the Makki

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts for entering ihram and identify the correct miqat for a Makki for Hajj and Umrah, and explain the consequence of violating it.

Core Idea
The miqat for a Makki is the Haram for Hajj and the Hill for Umrah; violation requires a dam.

Entering ihram is the start of Hajj or Umrah, and the Hanafi school specifies both recommended preparations and precise spatial boundaries (miqat) that vary depending on whether the pilgrim is a Makki (inside the Haram) or an Afaqi (outside). This lesson clarifies those rulings from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, including the definition of Makki and the consequences of ihram from the wrong zone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts for entering ihram
Before assuming ihram, the passage recommends performing wudu (ablution) and states that ghusl (full bath) is better. Also, wear two new or washed garments.
These are sunnan, not fard.
2
Distinguish between Makki and Afaqi
A Makki is anyone inside the Haram boundaries, not only Meccans. An Afaqi is from outside the Haram. The miqat rules differ.
The definition of Makki is expanded to include residents and visitors in the Haram.
3
Determine the miqat for the Makki for Hajj and Umrah
For Hajj, the Makki enters ihram from within the Haram itself. For Umrah, the miqat is the Hill (the area outside the Haram but before the outer miqat).
This is the agreed-upon ruling (mujma' alayh).
4
State the consequence of violating the correct miqat
If a Makki enters ihram for Hajj from the Hill, or for Umrah from the Haram, he must offer a dam (sacrifice) because he left his proper miqat.
Dam is a penalty, not an invalidator of the act.
5
Understand the exception for leaving the Haram temporarily
If a Makki leaves the Haram for a need and returns without passing the outer miqat (the boundary of the Afaqi), he may re-enter without ihram. If he passes it, he becomes like an Afaqi and must enter with ihram.
This preserves the ruling while accommodating travel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أردت أن تحرم فتوضأ والغسل أفضل والبس إزاراً ورداء جديـديـن أو كالمكي إذا خرج من الحرم لحاجة أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام بشرط أن لا يكون جاوز الميقات كالآفاقي، فإن جاوزه فليس له أن يدخل مكة من غير إحرام لأنه صار آفاقياً قوله (وللمكي الحرم للحج والحل للعمرة أي ميقات المكي إذا أراد الحج الحرم فإن أحرم له من الحل لزمه دم وإذا أراد العمرة الحل، فإذا أحرم بها من الحرم لزمه دم لأنه ترك ميقاته فيهما وهو مجمع عليه. والمراد بالمكي من كان داخل الحرم سواء كأنه بمكة أو لا، وسواء كان أهلها أو من لا، وبه يعلم أن المراد بداخل المواقيت من كان ساكناً في الحل والله سبحانه أعلم.
When you intend to enter ihram, perform wudu, and ghusl is better, and wear two garments, new or washed. Likewise for the Makki if he leaves the Haram for a need, he may enter Mecca without ihram provided he has not passed the miqat like the Afaqi. If he passes it, he may not enter Mecca without ihram because he becomes an Afaqi. He said: (And for the Makki, the Haram is the miqat for Hajj, and the Hill is the miqat for Umrah, meaning the miqat for the Makki when he intends Hajj is the Haram. If he enters ihram for it from the Hill, a dam is incumbent. When he intends Umrah, the Hill is the miqat; if he enters ihram for it from the Haram, a dam is incumbent because he left his miqat in both cases. This is agreed upon. And by 'Makki' is meant whoever is inside the Haram, whether he is in Mecca or not, and whether he is a resident or not. From this it is known that by 'those inside the miqats' is meant those who reside in the Hill. And Allah knows best.)
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq as explained by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, and further commented on in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It lays out the recommended acts when intending ihram: performing wudu (with ghusl being superior), and wearing two garments that are either new or washed. The text then extrapolates rulings for a person who is a Makki (resident within the Haram). If such a person leaves the Haram for a need, they may re-enter Mecca without ihram as long as they have not passed the miqat (the boundary). If they do pass it, they become like an Afaqi (someone from outside) and must enter with ihram. The author (in the original matn) states that the miqat for a Makki for Hajj is the Haram itself, and for Umrah it is the Hill (the area outside the Haram). Violating this by entering ihram from the wrong zone requires a dam (sacrifice). The commentary clarifies that 'Makki' includes anyone inside the Haram, not only residents of Mecca. This is a straightforward ruling with no proofs cited here, as the passage is meant to be a memorization anchor.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, marked by intention and wearing specific garments.
ميقات (miqat): The designated boundary for entering the state of ihram, varying by location.
مكي (makki): A person within the Haram boundaries, whether in Mecca or not, resident or visitor.
آفاقي (afaqi): A person from outside the Haram boundaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a Makki do if he intends Umrah?
A) He must enter ihram from the Haram.
B) He must enter ihram from the Hill.
C) He must go to the nearest outer miqat.
D) He can enter ihram from anywhere.

Key Takeaway
The miqat for a Makki is the Haram for Hajj and the Hill for Umrah; violation requires a dam.

Definition of Ihram: Intention and Specific Action as Conditions
Defining ihram and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ihram and distinguish between conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan) in its realization.

Core Idea
Ihram requires both intention and a specific ritual action; they are conditions, not parts of its essence.

In this lesson, we examine how the Hanafi school defines the state of ihram. The passage clarifies that ihram is not merely a mental intention but requires an outward sign—a specific action such as talbiyah or driving a sacrificial animal. Understanding this distinction between conditions and essence is crucial for valid ihram.

Guided Path
1
State the legal definition
Identify the precise Hanafi definition: ihram is 'entering into specific prohibitions' (al-dukhul fi hurumat makhsusah), realized by intention (niyyah) accompanied by dhikr (remembrance) and khususiyyah (specific action).
This definition is taken from al-Nahr and al-Fath.
2
Identify the two conditions
The two conditions are intention and a specific action. Both must be present for ihram to be valid in Sharia.
The specific action can be talbiyah, a remembrance of glorification, driving the hady, or garlanding the animal.
3
Explain why they are conditions, not pillars
The text explicitly states they are shurut (conditions) for its realization, not ajza' (integral parts) of its essence. This means the essence of ihram is the commitment to prohibitions, but it is not legally realized without these conditions.
The author refutes a misconception that they are parts of mahiyyah (essence).
4
Summarize the evidence and application
The Hanafi position is based on the Sunnah: the Prophet (SAW) would combine intention with talbiyah or other actions. Practical application: one must verbalize or act to enter ihram, not just intend silently.
For a mute person, a gesture may suffice.

Source Text

باب الإحرام
قوله : (وهو في الشريعة نية النسك الخ) قال في النهر : هو - شرعاً ـ الدخول في حرمات مخصوصة أي التزامها غير أنه لا يتحقق شرعاً إلا بالنية مع الذكر والخصوصية. كذا في الفتح. فهما شرطان في تحققه لا جزآن والغسل أفضل قال المرشدي : في شرحه : وهذا الغسل أحد الأغسال المسنونة في الحج . ثانيها لدخول مكة . ثالثها للوقوف بعرفة رابعها للوقوف بمزدلفة . خامسها لطواف الزيارة . سادسها وسابعها وثامنها لرمي الجمار شرح بكر قوله : (وفيه نظر لأن التيمم الخ) قال في النهر أقول : فيه نظر إذ مبناه على أن المخالفة راجعة إلى قوله «ولهذا لا يعتبر التيمم عند العجز والظاهر رجوعها إلى قوله والمراد بهذا الغسل تحصيل النظافة لا الطهارة بخلاف الجمعة والعيدين فإنه يلاحظ فيهما مع النظافة الطهارة أيضاً لأنه إنما شرع للصلاة ولذا لم تأمر به الحائض والنفساء مع أنه قد قيل بأنهما يحضران العيدين كما مر ، نعم ما في الكافي هو التحقيق كذلك، بل من حيث قيام الوضوء مقام الغسل ولفظها، فعلم أن هذا الاغتسال للنظافة ليزول ما به من الدرن والوسخ فيقوم الوضوء مقامه كما في العيدين والجمعة لكن الغسل أحب لأن النظافة به أتم ا.هـ. والإقامة حكاها Chapter of Ihram. His statement: (And it is in Sharia the intention of the ritual etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is, legally, entering into specific prohibitions, i.e., undertaking them, but it is not realized legally except with intention along with remembrance and specificity. Thus in al-Fath. They are two conditions for its realization, not two parts of its essence as mistakenly thought in al-Bahr. His statement: (or specificity) Al-Ramli said: i.e., performing something from the specifics of the ritual, whether it be talbiyah or remembrance intended for glorification, or driving the sacrificial animal, or garlanding the sacrificial animal as in al-Mustasfa. His statement: (The author: and ghusl is better) Al-Murshidi said in his commentary: This ghusl is one of the recommended ghusls in Hajj. Second: for entering Makkah. Third: for standing at Arafah. Fourth: for standing at Muzdalifah. Fifth: for Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Sixth, seventh, and eighth: for throwing the pebbles on the days of Tashreeq. Ninth: for Tawaf al-Sadr. Tenth: for entering the Haram of Madinah. He said in al-Bahr al-Amiq: There is no ghusl for throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr. End. Likewise in Hashiyat al-Madani. His statement: (He said the commentator etc.) His expression: The purpose of this ghusl is to achieve cleanliness and remove odor, not purification, so the menstruating woman and postpartum woman are commanded to do it, and purification for her is not conceivable, therefore tayammum is not prescribed for it when unable to use water, unlike Friday and the two Eids. He ended. He said in al-Nahr: He attributed it in al-Mi'raj to Sharh Bakr. His statement: (And there is consideration because tayammum etc.) He said in al-Nahr: I say: There is consideration because it is based on the difference referring to his statement 'therefore tayammum is not considered when unable to use water', and the apparent refutation refers to his statement 'the purpose of this ghusl is to achieve cleanliness, not purification, unlike Friday and the two Eids because in them purification is also observed along with cleanliness because it is prescribed for prayer, and therefore the menstruating woman and postpartum woman are not commanded to do it, although it has been said that they attend the two Eids as has passed. Indeed what is in al-Kafi is the verification. End. Shaykh Ismail said: The fair view is that the original expression of al-Zayla'i is suggestive of tayammum being prescribed for them, and the refutation does not remove the objection. Then the expression of al-Bahr is also suggestive where it reports from al-Kafi the equality, and its outward appearance is regarding the non-consideration of tayammum, but it is not so. Rather, it is from the perspective of wudu taking the place of ghusl, and its wording: 'It is understood that this washing is for cleanliness to remove dirt and grime, so wudu takes its place as in the two Eids and Friday, but ghusl is more beloved because cleanliness is more complete with it.' End. And the substitution is narrated by al-Shumunni from al-Quduri: Every ghusl for cleanliness, wudu takes its place like the ghusl of Friday and the two Eids. End. And it is not hidden that equality in not considering tayammum, even if not explicit, is known from his branching of wudu taking the place of ghusl on the basis that it is for cleanliness. And since cleanliness does not consider tayammum due to its absence, and since he equated between ihram and Friday and the two Eids in wudu taking its place, branching on what was mentioned, it necessitates equality in not considering tayammum among all. The author's statement: (And wear an izaar and a ridaa).
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of ihram and the ruling on ghusl for ihram. It begins by refining the Sharia definition: ihram is the intention (niyyah) along with remembrance (dhikr) and a specific action (khususiyyah), such as talbiyah or driving a sacrificial animal. These are conditions (shurut) for the validity of ihram, not parts of its essence. The text then discusses the ghusl for ihram, which is one of the ten recommended (masnun) ghusls in Hajj. The key point is that this ghusl is for cleanliness (nazafah), not purification (taharah). Evidence: the Prophet ordered Asma' bint Abu Bakr, who was postpartum, to perform ghusl and then assume ihram. Since a postpartum woman is not in a state of purity, the ghusl cannot be for purification. Consequently, if water is unavailable, tayammum is not valid for this ghusl, unlike the ghusls for Friday and Eid, which are for purification and thus permit tayammum. The commentary addresses a potential objection: the statement from al-Zayla'i may suggest tayammum is valid, but the correct view (as in al-Kafi) is that tayammum is not valid. Wudu suffices as a substitute for this ghusl because it is merely for cleanliness. The passage concludes by equating ihram ghusl with Friday/Eid ghusl in that wudu suffices, but not tayammum.

Key Terms
نية النسك (niyyat al-nusk): Intention to perform Hajj or Umrah, which is a condition for the validity of ihram.
خصوصية (khususiyyah): A specific action indicating the intent of ihram, such as talbiyah or driving a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two conditions for the realization of ihram according to the Hanafi school?
A) Intention and purity
B) Intention and remembrance of Allah
C) Intention and a specific ritual action
D) Remembrance and wearing ihram garments

Key Takeaway
Ihram in Hanafi fiqh requires both the intention to perform Hajj or Umrah and a specific outward action (khususiyyah) as conditions for its validity.

Ghusl for Ihram: Cleanliness, Not Purification
Ruling on ghusl for ihram and its comparison with Friday/Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the ghusl for ihram is for cleanliness not purification, and apply the ruling that tayammum is invalid while wudu suffices.

Core Idea
Ghusl for ihram is about cleanliness, so tayammum is invalid; wudu suffices.

This lesson unpacks the ruling on the recommended ghusl for ihram. The Hanafi school holds that this ghusl is prescribed for physical cleanliness (nazafah) rather than ritual purification (taharah). Understanding this distinction is key to knowing when tayammum can substitute and when it cannot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its textual basis
The ghusl for ihram is one of the ten recommended (masnun) ghusls in Hajj. The author states 'الغسل أفضل' (ghusl is better), indicating it is sunnah muakkadah. The passage then explains the nature of this ghusl.
It is listed among the ten ghusls, with a note that there is no ghusl for throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah.
2
Determine the purpose of the ghusl
The commentator explicitly says: 'المراد بهذا الغسل تحصيل النظافة وإزالة الرائحة لا الطهارة' – the purpose is to achieve cleanliness and remove odor, not purification. Evidence: menstruating and postpartum women are commanded to perform it, despite being in a state of ritual impurity.
This is based on the hadith of Asma' bint Abu Bakr (RA).
3
Analyze the implication for tayammum
Since the ghusl is for cleanliness, tayammum (which is a substitute for purification) is not valid when water is unavailable. Tayammum can only replace an act that has purification as its objective. The text contrasts this with ghusl for Friday and Eid, which have purification as a component.
Al-Kafi is cited as the authoritative source for this ruling.
4
Determine the substitute when water is unavailable
Wudu (ablution) suffices in place of the ghusl because it also achieves cleanliness. The passage equates ihram ghusl with Friday/Eid ghusl in that wudu takes its place, but tayammum does not.
The author emphasizes that wudu is sufficient, but ghusl is more beloved for completeness.
5
Summarize the thamarah (practical outcome)
If a person cannot find water for ghusl before ihram, they should perform wudu. Tayammum is not acceptable. This is the mufta bihi position.
This resolves a potential misconception that tayammum could substitute.
