End. And the substitution is narrated by al-Shumunni from al-Quduri: Every ghusl for cleanliness, wudu takes its place like the ghusl of Friday and the two Eids. End. And it is not hidden that equality in not considering tayammum, even if not explicit, is known from his branching of wudu taking the place of ghusl on the basis that it is for cleanliness. And since cleanliness does not consider tayammum due to its absence, and since he equated between ihram and Friday and the two Eids in wudu taking its place, branching on what was mentioned, it necessitates equality in not considering tayammum among all. The author's statement: (And wear an izaar and a ridaa).
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of ihram and the ruling on ghusl for ihram. It begins by refining the Sharia definition: ihram is the intention (niyyah) along with remembrance (dhikr) and a specific action (khususiyyah), such as talbiyah or driving a sacrificial animal. These are conditions (shurut) for the validity of ihram, not parts of its essence. The text then discusses the ghusl for ihram, which is one of the ten recommended (masnun) ghusls in Hajj. The key point is that this ghusl is for cleanliness (nazafah), not purification (taharah). Evidence: the Prophet ordered Asma' bint Abu Bakr, who was postpartum, to perform ghusl and then assume ihram. Since a postpartum woman is not in a state of purity, the ghusl cannot be for purification. Consequently, if water is unavailable, tayammum is not valid for this ghusl, unlike the ghusls for Friday and Eid, which are for purification and thus permit tayammum. The commentary addresses a potential objection: the statement from al-Zayla'i may suggest tayammum is valid, but the correct view (as in al-Kafi) is that tayammum is not valid. Wudu suffices as a substitute for this ghusl because it is merely for cleanliness. The passage concludes by equating ihram ghusl with Friday/Eid ghusl in that wudu suffices, but not tayammum.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable.
غسل مسنون (ghusl masnun): Recommended bath, such as the ten ghusls of Hajj.
نظافة (nazafah): Cleanliness, removal of dirt and odor, as opposed to ritual purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for the ghusl of ihram when water is unavailable?
A) Tayammum is valid because it substitutes any ghusl.
B) Tayammum is invalid; wudu takes the place of ghusl.
C) Tayammum is invalid; no substitute is required.
D) Tayammum is valid only if the person is also in a state of janabah.

Key Takeaway
The ghusl for ihram is for cleanliness, not purification, so tayammum is invalid; wudu suffices when water is insufficient.

Ghusl for Ihram: Cleanliness not Purification
Explains that ghusl for ihram is for cleanliness; tayammum not applicable; compares with Friday/Eid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for ihram, identify its purpose as cleanliness rather than ritual purification, and explain why tayammum is not a valid substitute.

Core Idea
Ghusl for ihram is for cleanliness, not purification; thus tayammum cannot replace it.

Before entering ihram for Hajj or Umrah, Muslims are recommended to perform ghusl. However, this ghusl is not for lifting ritual impurity but for physical cleanliness. This distinction has important consequences: even a menstruating woman may perform it, and tayammum is not a valid substitute. The following passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the proof and the ongoing debate with related acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? What is its hukm level (sunnah, wajib, etc.)?
The passage states it is 'recommended' (yustaḥabbu), i.e., sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith cited as proof. Who narrated it? What is the exact wording?
The hadith of Asma' bint Abi Bakr narrated by Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
Why does this hadith indicate that the ghusl is for cleanliness, not purification? Consider the context: the woman was in nifas (postpartum bleeding).
The command 'let her perform ghusl' was given despite her state of major impurity, showing the purpose is physical cleanliness (nazafah).
4
Explain the consequence: no tayammum
Since the ghusl is not for ritual purification, tayammum (which only lifts hadath) is not a substitute.
Compare with Friday/Eid ghusl, which are for purification and thus allow tayammum when water is unavailable.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis (e.g., author of al-Kafi) equated ihram ghusl with Friday/Eid ghusl, but the relied-upon view rejects that analogy.
The commentator (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) points out that tayammum for Friday/Eid is not actually prescribed if one is already pure, so the parallel does not hold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيستحب في حق الحائض أو النفساء والصبي لما روي أن أبا بكر رضي الله عنه قال لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن أسماء قد نفست فقال : مرها فلتغتسل ولتحرم بالحج. ولهذا لا يشرع التيمم له عند العجز عن الماء. قال الشارح بخلاف الجمعة والعيدين يعني أن الغسل فيهما للطهارة لا للتنظيف ولهذا يشرع التيمم لهما عند العجز وفيه نظر، لأن التيمم لم يشرع لهما عند العجز إذا كان طاهراً عن الجنابة ونحوها والكلام فيه لأنه ملوث ومغير لكن جعل طهارة ضرورة أداء الصلاة ولا ضرورة فيهما ولهذا سوى المصنف في الكافي بين الإحرام وبين الجمعة والعيدين. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه يستحب لمن أراده كمال التنظيف من قص الأظفار والشارب وحلق الإبطين والعانة والرأس لمن اعتاده من الرجال أو أراده وإلا فتسريحه وإزالة الشعث والوسخ عنه وعن بدنه بغسله بالخطمي والأشنان ونحوهما، ومن المستحب عند إرادته جماع زوجته أو جاريته إن كانت معه ولا مانع من الجماع فإنه من السنة
It is recommended for the menstruating woman, the woman with post-partum bleeding, and the child, because it is narrated that Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) said to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Asma' has given birth.' He said: 'Order her to perform ghusl and enter ihram for Hajj.' Therefore, tayammum is not prescribed for one unable to use water. The commentator said: unlike Friday and the two Eids, meaning that the ghusl in those is for purification, not for cleanliness, and so tayammum is prescribed for them when unable. But there is a consideration, because tayammum is not prescribed for them when unable if one is pure from janaba and the like; the discussion is about it because it is [the water] is polluted and changed, but it is made a purification of necessity for performing prayer, and there is no necessity in them. For this reason, the author in al-Kafi equated between ihram and Friday and the two Eids. And the author indicated that it is recommended for one who intends complete cleanliness: cutting the nails, mustache, shaving armpits, pubic hair, and the head for men who are accustomed to it or intend it; otherwise, combing and removing dishevelment and dirt from him and his body by washing with soap, ash of chenopodium, and the like; and among the recommended things when intending it is intercourse with his wife or concubine if she is with him and there is no prevention, for it is from the Sunnah.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage addresses the nature of the recommended ghusl for ihram. The author explains that this ghusl is sunna even for women in menstruation or post-partum bleeding, and for a child, based on the hadith of Asma' bint Abi Bakr when she gave birth at Dhul-Hulayfa. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered her to perform ghusl and enter ihram. This indicates that the ghusl is not for ritual purification (since she was in a state of major impurity), but for cleanliness and removal of odor. Consequently, if one cannot find water, tayammum is not a substitute, because tayammum is only for ritual purification, not for cleaning. The commentator contrasts this with the ghusl for Friday and the two Eids, which are also for purification (to be fit for prayer), and thus tayammum is allowed. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq points out a consideration: tayammum is not actually prescribed for Friday/Eid if one is already pure; the issue is when water is unavailable. The author of al-Kafi equates ihram with Friday/Eid in that wudu suffices if ghusl is for cleanliness, but the absence of tayammum remains a point of difference. The passage then lists other recommended acts: grooming (cutting nails, shaving, washing) and intercourse if possible, all for the purpose of entering ihram in a state of complete cleanliness.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): The full-body wash recommended before ihram; it is for cleanliness, not ritual purification.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution as a substitute for wudu/ghusl when water is unavailable; not valid for ghusl intended for cleanliness.
نظافة (nazafah): Physical cleanliness and removal of dirt/odor, as opposed to ritual purity (taharah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is tayammum not prescribed for the ghusl of ihram when water is unavailable?
A) Because tayammum is only for ritual purification, not for cleanliness.
B) Because tayammum is not valid when one is in a state of menstrual bleeding.
C) Because the ghusl of ihram is wajib, and tayammum cannot substitute for wajib ghusl.
D) Because the ghusl of ihram must be performed with water, unlike Friday ghusl.

Key Takeaway
The ghusl for ihram is a sunnah for physical cleanliness, proven by the Prophet's order to a woman in nifas; tayammum does not replace it.

Sunan Before Ihram: Grooming, Garments, Perfume, and Prayer
Lists recommended acts before ihram: cutting nails, shaving, washing, wearing new/clean garments, applying perfume, and praying two rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five recommended acts (sunan) before entering ihrām according to the Hanafi school and identify the relied-upon ruling on applying perfume.

Core Idea
Before ihrām, groom, wear clean izār and ridā’, apply perfume on the body, pray two rak‘ahs — all are Sunnah.

This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rā’iq enumerates the sunan (recommended acts) that a pilgrim should perform before entering the state of ihrām. These acts are rooted in the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions. Understanding them helps the pilgrim prepare physically and spiritually for the sacred rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grooming acts
List the recommended grooming acts: cutting nails, trimming mustache, shaving armpits and pubic hair, washing the body with cleansers like soap. Note that the head may be shaved for those accustomed.
These are sunan, not obligatory.
2
Specify the garments
The pilgrim should wear a new or washed izār (lower wrap) and ridā’ (upper wrap). The izār covers from navel to below knee; the ridā’ covers back, shoulders, and chest, tied above the navel.
White is preferred. Pinning or tying with a rope is disliked but not harmful.
3
Understand the ruling on perfume
Perfume on the body before ihrām is Sunnah, even if the trace remains (like musk). Perfume on the garment with a trace is not allowed. The relied-upon position follows Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
Muhammad ibn al-Hasan’s objection is considered weak; the hadith of ‘A’isha is the evidence.
4
Recognize the prayer and talbiya
After putting on the ihrām garments, it is Sunnah to pray two rak‘ahs, reciting in the first rak‘ah Sūrat al-Fātiḥa and Sūrat al-Kāfirūn, and in the second al-Fātiḥa and Sūrat al-Ikhlāṣ. Then recite the talbiya.
The prayer is performed before the talbiya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أنه يستحب لمن أراده كمال التنظيف من قص الأظفار والشارب وحلق الإبطين والعانة والرأس لمن اعتاده من الرجال أو أراده وإلا فتسريحه وإزالة الشعث والوسخ عنه وعن بدنه بغسله بالخطمي والأشنان ونحوهما، ومن المستحب عند إرادته جماع زوجته أو جاريته إن كانت معه ولا مانع من الجماع فإنه من السنة قوله ( وألبس إزارا ورداء جديدين أو غسيلين لأنه عليه السلام لبسهما هو وأصحابه. وتطيب وصل ركعتين ولب دبر صلاتك تنوى بها الحج وهي لبيك اللهم لبيك كما رواه مسلم ولأنه ممنوع عن لبس المخيط ولا بد من ستر العورة ودفع الحر والبرد وذلك فيما عيناه والإزار من السرة إلى ما تحت الركبة يذكر ويؤنث كما في ضياء الحلوم . والرداء على الظهر والكتفين والصدر ويشده فوق السرة وإن غرز طرفيه في إزاره فلا بأس به، ولو خلله بخلال أو مسلة أو شده على نفسه بحبل أساء ولا شيء عليه. وما في الكتاب بيان للسنة وإلا فساتر العورة كاف كما في المجمع. وأشار بتقديم الجديد إلى أفضليته، وكونه أبيض أفضل من غيره كالتكفين، وفي عدم غسل الثوب العتيق ترك للمستحب ولا يخفى أن هذا في حق الرجل قوله (وتطيب) أي يسن له استعمال الطيب في بدنه قبيل الإحرام أطلقه فشمل ما تبقى عينه بعده كالمسك والغالية وما لا تبقى لحديث عائشة في الصحيحين: كنت أطيب رسول الله ل وإحرامه قبل أن يحرم. وفي لفظ لهما : كأني أنظر إلى وبيض الطيب في مفرق رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الإحرامه قبل أن يحرم. في لفظ لمسلم كأني أنظر إلى وبيض المسك وهو البريق واللمعان وكرهه محمد بما تبقى عينه والحديث حجة عليه. وقيدنا بالبدن إذ لا يجوز التطيب في الثوب بما تبقى عينه على قول الكل على أحد الروايتين عنهما قالوا وبه نأخذ والفرق لهما بينهما أنه اعتبر في البدن تابعاً على الأصح والمتصل بالثوب منفصل عنه فلم يعتبر تابعاً، والمقصود من حصول الارتفاق به حالة المنع منه كالسحور للصوم وهو يحصل بما في البدن فأغنى عن تجويزه في الثوب إذ لم يقصد كمال الارتفاق حالة الإحرام لأن الحاج الشعث التفل، الفتاوى الظهيرية أن ما عن محمد رواية ضعيفة وأن مشهور مذهبه كمذهبهما. قوله : وصلى ركعتين) قال في التتارخانية وفي المحيط : وإن قرأ في الركعة الأولى بفاتحة الكتاب وقل يا أيها الكافرون وفي الثانية بفاتحة الكتاب و «قل هو الله أحد» تبركاً بفعل رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فهو أفضل.
And the author indicated that it is recommended for one who intends complete cleanliness: cutting the nails, mustache, shaving armpits, pubic hair, and the head for men who are accustomed to it or intend it; otherwise, combing and removing dishevelment and dirt from him and his body by washing with soap, ash of chenopodium, and the like; and among the recommended things when intending it is intercourse with his wife or concubine if she is with him and there is no prevention, for it is from the Sunnah. His statement: (And he should wear a new or washed izār and ridā’), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) wore them himself and his companions. And he should apply perfume and pray two rak’ahs, then say after your prayer, intending by them Hajj: ‘Labbayk Allahumma labbayk’ as narrated by Muslim, and because he is forbidden from wearing sewn garments, and there must be covering of the ‘awrah and protection from heat and cold, and that is in what we specified. The izār is from the navel to below the knee, masculine and feminine, as in Diya’ al-Hulūm. The ridā’ is over the back, shoulders, and chest, and he should tie it above the navel. If he fastens its ends into his izār, there is no harm. If he pins it with a toothpick or an iron pin, or ties it on himself with a rope, he does wrong but nothing is upon him. What is in the book is a clarification of the Sunnah; otherwise, a cover for the ‘awrah is sufficient, as in al-Majma‘. And he indicated by mentioning 'new' its superiority, and being white is better than other colors, like for the shroud. Not washing an old garment is abandoning the recommended. It is clear that this applies to men. His statement: (and apply perfume), i.e., it is recommended for him to use perfume on his body shortly before ihrām. He made it absolute, so it includes what remains after it, like musk and 'ghāliya', and what does not remain, due to the hadith of ‘Ā’isha in the two Sahīhs: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for his ihrām before he would enter ihrām.' In another wording: 'I can still see the glistening of the perfume in the parting of the hair of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for his ihrām before he would enter ihrām.' In a wording of Muslim: 'I can still see the glistening of musk.' Muḥammad disliked what remains in substance, but the hadith is evidence against him. We restricted it to the body, because it is not permissible to apply perfume on the garment with what remains in substance according to the consensus of all, on one of two narrations from them. They said: we take this position. The distinction between them is that what is on the body is considered a follower (tābi‘) on the stronger opinion, while what is attached to the garment is separate from it and thus not considered a follower. The purpose of obtaining allowance while it is prohibited is like the pre-dawn meal (sahūr) for fasting, and this is achieved by what is on the body, so it suffices without allowing it on the garment, since complete allowance is not intended in the state of ihrām because the pilgrim is unkempt and disheveled. In al-Fatāwā al-Ẓahīriyya: what is reported from Muḥammad is a weak narration, and the well-known position of his madhhab is like theirs. His statement: (and he prays two rak‘ahs). In al-Tātārkhāniyya and al-Muhīt: if he recites in the first rak‘ah Sūrat al-Fātiḥa and 'Qul yā ayyuhā l-kāfirūn' and in the second Sūrat al-Fātiḥa and 'Qul huwa llāhu aḥad', seeking blessing by the action of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), it is better.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage enumerates the sunan (recommended acts) before entering ihrām. First, the author mentions grooming: cutting nails, trimming the mustache, shaving armpits and pubic hair, and shaving the head for those accustomed (or combing if not). Washing the body with cleansing agents like soap (khiṭmī) is recommended to remove dirt. Second, intercourse with one's spouse is considered from the Sunnah to ensure purity and cleanliness. Third, wearing a new or washed izār (lower wrap) and ridā’ (upper wrap) is recommended, following the practice of the Prophet. The izār covers from navel to below the knee, the ridā’ covers the back, shoulders, chest, and is tied above the navel. Pinning or tying with a rope is disliked but does not invalidate ihrām. The author emphasizes that the specification is for the Sunnah; the bare minimum of covering the ‘awrah is sufficient. Wearing white is superior, like for the shroud. Fourth, applying perfume on the body before ihrām is recommended, even if the substance remains (like musk), due to the hadith of ‘Ā’isha. Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥasan disliked perfume that leaves a trace, but the majority of the school (including Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf) permit it, and the fatwa is on this position. However, perfume on the garment is not allowed if a trace remains, as the garment is separate from the body and the prohibition of perfume in ihrām would be violated. Fifth, praying two rak‘ahs after putting on the ihrām garments, in which it is recommended to recite Sūrat al-Kāfirūn and al-Ikhlāṣ, is Sunnah before reciting the talbiya.

Key Terms
إزار (izār): A lower garment worn from navel to below the knee; one of the two cloths of ihrām.
رداء (ridā’): An upper garment covering the back, shoulders, and chest; the other cloth of ihrām.
طيب (tīb): Perfume applied to the body before ihrām; its application is Sunnah even if the scent remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on applying perfume on the body before entering ihrām if the scent remains?
A) It is haram because the pilgrim will be prohibited from perfume.
B) It is makruh tahrimi based on Muhammad's view.
C) It is Sunnah, even if the trace remains, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
D) It is permissible but disliked (makruh tanzihi).

Key Takeaway
Perfuming the body before ihrām is Sunnah even if the trace remains, following the Prophet's practice and the majority of the Hanafi school.

Iḍṭibā‘: Sunnah During Ṭawāf, Not Before Ihram
Corrects common practice about iḍṭibā‘ timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when iḍṭibā‘ is sunna according to the Hanafi school and identify the common error corrected in the passage.

Core Idea
Iḍṭibā‘ (uncovering the right shoulder) is sunna only during tawaf, not from the moment of ihram.

Many pilgrims assume that the sunna of iḍṭibā‘—passing the upper garment under the right arm and over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder bare—applies from the moment they assume ihram. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq corrects that misunderstanding, citing multiple Hanafi authorities and hadith evidence. It clarifies that the prescribed sunna is specifically for the tawaf, not for the entire state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common error
What is the mistaken practice that the passage corrects? Look at the text: 'the common people act upon this, but it is not so.'
The error is thinking iḍṭibā‘ begins with ihram.
2
Find the correct ruling
When does the sunna of iḍṭibā‘ apply? The passage states: 'The place of the sunna iḍṭibā‘ is only shortly before the tawaf until its completion.'
It is specifically for tawaf, not before.
3
Examine the evidence
What support is given? The passage cites hadiths and the consensus of most Hanafi books, agreeing with al-Shafi‘i.
The hadiths describe the Prophet performing iḍṭibā‘ during tawaf.
4
Understand the practical implication
How does this affect a pilgrim's practice? A pilgrim should only uncover the right shoulder when beginning tawaf, and cover it afterward.
Failure to do so may mean missing the sunna's proper time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدخل الرداء تحت اليد اليمنى ويلقيه على كتفه الأيسر ويبقى كتفه الأيمن مكشوفاً، كذا في الخزانة ذكره البرجندي في هذا المحل، وهو موهم أن الاضطباع يستحب من أول أحوال الإحرام وعليه العوام وليس كذلك، فإن محل الإضطباع المسنون إنما يكون قبيل الطواف إلى انتهائه لا غير. كذا في شرح اللباب لمنلا علي القاري. وقال المرشدي في شرح مناسك الكنز : وهو الأصح وأنه هو السنة ونقله الشيخ رحمه الله السندي في منسكه الكبير عن الغاية ومناسك الطرابلسي والفتح، وقال: فالحاصل أن أكثر كتب المذهب ناطقة بأن الاضطباع يسن في الطواف لا قبله في الإحرام وعليه تدل الأحاديث وبه قال الشافعي ا هـ . كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار قوله: (وإلا فساتر العورة كاف) قوله : (فيجوز في ثوب واحد وأكثر من ثوبين وفي أسودين أو قطع خرق مخيطة، والأفضل أن لا يكون فيهما خياطة ا هـ ( لباب المناسك )
And he should put the rida’ under his right arm and throw it over his left shoulder, leaving his right shoulder uncovered. Thus in al-Khizana, al-Burjandi mentioned it in this place, but it gives the impression that idtiba‘ is recommended from the very beginning of ihram, and the common people act upon this, but it is not so. The place of the sunna idtiba‘ is only shortly before the tawaf until its completion, no other. Thus in Sharh al-Lubab by Mulla ‘Ali al-Qari. And al-Murshidi said in Sharh Manasik al-Kanz: It is the more correct (asahh) and it is the Sunnah. And Shaykh al-Sindi transmitted it in his Manasik al-Kabir from al-Ghayah and the Manasik of al-Tarabulusi and al-Fath, and said: The conclusion is that most books of the madhhab state that idtiba‘ is sunna during the tawaf, not before it in ihram, and the hadiths indicate this, and al-Shafi‘i also said this. Thus in Hashiyah al-Madani on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. His statement: (and if not, a cover for the ‘awrah is sufficient). His statement: (it is permissible in one cloth, more than two cloths, in two black ones, or pieces of sewn rags; but the best is that they have no stitching). From Lubab al-Manasik.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage clarifies the sunna of iḍṭibā‘ (uncovering the right shoulder). Some misunderstanding arises from earlier texts that mention placing the rida’ under the right arm and over the left shoulder as part of the description of the ihram garments. However, the correct sunna position is that iḍṭibā‘ is specifically practiced during the tawaf (circumambulation) of the Ka‘ba, not at the time of entering ihram. The author corrects the common practice of the ‘common people’ who keep the right shoulder uncovered throughout the entire state of ihram. He cites multiple authorities (Mulla ‘Ali al-Qari, al-Murshidi, al-Sindi) affirming that most Hanafi works state that iḍṭibā‘ is sunna only during tawaf, and the hadiths support this. The commentator also notes that the Shafi‘i school agrees. The passage then reiterates that the minimal requirement for ihram clothing is covering the ‘awrah; even one cloth or sewn garments (though stitching is best avoided) suffices in necessity.

Key Terms
اضطباع (iḍṭibā‘): The act of passing the ridā’ under the right arm and throwing it over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder uncovered, during tawaf.
طواف (tawāf): Circumambulation of the Ka‘ba, for which iḍṭibā‘ is prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) As soon as one puts on the ihram garments.
B) During the entire duration of ihram.
C) Only during the tawaf of the Ka‘ba.
D) Only during the sa‘y between Safa and Marwa.

Key Takeaway
Iḍṭibā‘ is a sunna of tawaf, not a continuous sunna of ihram.

Applying Perfume Before Ihram: Sunnah, Proof, and Intra-Hanafi Resolution
Explains ruling, proof, and intra-madhhab dispute on perfume before ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that applying perfume before ihram is a confirmed sunnah even if it leaves a trace, cite the hadith of Aisha as proof, and explain why Imam Muhammad's dissenting view is not relied upon.

Core Idea
Perfume before ihram is sunnah; the Prophet's practice overrides concerns about visible residue.

A common question about ihram is whether one may apply perfume before entering the state, especially if it leaves a visible trace. The Hanafi school, based on the explicit practice of the Prophet (PBUH), confirms that it is a recommended sunnah. This lesson explains the ruling, the proof from the hadith of Aisha, and how an internal disagreement within the school was resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what level of ruling (hukm) is assigned. Here, applying perfume to the body shortly before ihram is ruled as a sunnah muakkadah.
The ruling applies to the body, not the garment.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the textual evidence that supports the ruling. The passage cites the hadith of Aisha (RA) from Bukhari and Muslim: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah for his ihram before he entered ihram.'
The hadith is ahad but mutawatir in meaning? Actually sahih and widely accepted.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The phrase 'kuntu utayyibu' indicates a habitual action of the Prophet, establishing sunnah. The timing 'before he entered ihram' limits the ruling to before ihram.
The hadith also mentions visible residue of musk, showing it is not problematic.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the difference within the Hanafi school. Imam Muhammad disliked perfumes that leave a trace, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allowed it.
Muhammad's view is based on the idea that the trace might contradict the state of ihram.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine which position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The hadith is proof against Muhammad's view, and later authorities (e.g., Fatawa al-Zahiriyya) declared his narration weak. The well-known position is that of the majority.
Therefore, the mufta bihi is that applying perfume is sunnah even if it leaves a trace.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتطيب) أي يسن له استعمال الطيب في بدنه قبيل الإحرام أطلقه فشمل ما تبقى عينه بعده كالمسك والغالية وما لا تبقى لحديث عائشة في الصحيحين: كنت أطيب رسول الله ل وإحرامه قبل أن يحرم. وفي لفظ لهما : كأني أنظر إلى وبيض الطيب في مفرق رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إحرامه قبل أن يحرم. في لفظ لمسلم كأني أنظر إلى وبيض المسك وهو البريق واللمعان وكرهه محمد بما تبقى عينه والحديث حجة عليه. وقيدنا بالبدن إذ لا يجوز التطيب في الثوب بما تبقى عينه على قول الكل على أحد الروايتين عنهما قالوا وبه نأخذ والفرق لهما بينهما أنه اعتبر في البدن تابعاً على الأصح والمتصل بالثوب منفصل عنه فلم يعتبر تابعاً، والمقصود من حصول الارتفاق به حالة المنع منه كالسحور للصوم وهو يحصل بما في البدن فأغنى عن تجويزه في الثوب إذ لم يقصد كمال الارتفاق حالة الإحرام لأن الحاج الشعث التفل، الفتاوى الظهيرية أن ما عن محمد رواية ضعيفة وأن مشهور مذهبه كمذهبهما .
His saying (and apply perfume): meaning it is sunnah for him to use perfume on his body shortly before ihram. He [the author] gave it absolutely, so it includes what leaves a trace after it, like musk and ghaliyah, and what does not leave a trace, due to the hadith of Aisha in the two Sahihs: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah for his ihram before he entered ihram.' In another wording of them: 'I can still see the whiteness of the perfume on the parting of the hair of the Messenger of Allah when he was in ihram before he entered ihram.' In a wording of Muslim: 'I can still see the whiteness of musk' which is gleam and shine. And Muhammad disliked that which leaves a trace, but the hadith is proof against him. And we restricted it to the body, because applying perfume on the garment which leaves a trace is not permissible according to all, on one of the two narrations from them, they said: and we take it. And the distinction for them is that on the body it is considered secondary (tabi') according to the most correct view, while what is connected to the garment is separate from it, so it is not considered secondary. The intent of obtaining benefit from it in the state of prohibition is like the pre-dawn meal for fasting, and that is obtained by what is on the body, so it suffices from permitting it on the garment, since complete benefit is not intended in the state of ihram because the pilgrim is disheveled and unkempt. Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah state that what is reported from Muhammad is a weak narration, and the well-known view of his madhhab is like theirs.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the sunnah of applying perfume (tayyib) before entering ihram. The author explains that it is recommended (sunna) for a man to apply perfume to his body shortly before ihram, regardless of whether the perfume leaves a visible trace (like musk) or not. The proof is the hadith from Aisha (RA) recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim, where she states she would perfume the Prophet (PBUH) for his ihram before he entered the state, and the whiteness of the fragrance was visible on his head. This hadith is presented as evidence against the view of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, who disliked perfumes that leave a trace. The text clarifies that the prohibition on perfume in ihram is for the body after entering the state, but applying it before is sunnah. However, applying perfume to the garment that leaves a trace is not allowed according to the majority, based on one of two narrations. The rationale is that the benefit from perfume on the body is secondary (taba'i) to the act of ihram, whereas the garment is separate. The state of ihram does not aim for complete comfort; the pilgrim is meant to be simple (sha'ith tafil). The Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah declare Muhammad's reported view weak, and the well-known position of the Hanafi school aligns with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, allowing perfume with a trace on the body.

Key Terms
الطيب (al-ṭīb): Perfume, any fragrant substance applied to the body.
الغالية (al-ghāliyah): A compound perfume, typically containing musk and other ingredients, used as an example of a perfume that leaves a trace.
المسك (al-misk): Musk, a strong-scented perfume derived from the musk deer, used as an example of a perfume that leaves a visible residue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani dislike applying perfume before ihram that leaves a trace, and how is this refuted?
A) He argued it is wasteful; refuted by the principle of avoiding extravagance
B) He argued it may remain after ihram and the trace would be visible; refuted by the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet (PBUH) had visible perfume residue
C) He argued it is not mentioned in the Quran; refuted by ijma'
D) He argued it is only for women; refuted by the Prophet's example

Key Takeaway
Applying perfume to the body before ihram is a confirmed sunnah even if it leaves a trace, based on the explicit hadith of Aisha; Imam Muhammad's contrary view is weak and not relied upon.

The Sunnah of Ihram Clothing: Izar and Rida
Describes recommended ihram clothing and clarifies idtiba' timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts for ihram clothing, explain the ruling on idtiba', and distinguish what is permissible versus recommended.

Core Idea
The izar and rida are sunnah; covering awrah is sufficient; idtiba' is only for tawaf.

When a Muslim enters ihram for Hajj or Umrah, he is prohibited from wearing sewn garments. The Prophet ﷺ taught specific clothing practices: a lower wrap (izar) and an upper wrap (rida). This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details what is sunnah, what is acceptable, and the correct timing for leaving the right shoulder bare (idtiba'). By understanding these details, you will avoid common mistakes and follow the confirmed sunnah as transmitted in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah clothing items
The text specifies that the sunnah for a man is to wear two cloths: an izar covering from navel to below the knee, and a rida covering the back, shoulders, and chest, tied above the navel.
These cloths should preferably be new, white, and without stitching.
2
Recognize what is sufficient and what is recommended
Covering the awrah is the essential obligation (wajib). If one cannot obtain the specific two cloths, any covering is sufficient. However, following the sunnah is better.
The text says: 'otherwise covering the awrah is sufficient.'
3
Distinguish permissible and disliked fastening methods
Tucking the ends of the rida into the izar is permissible. But using a toothpick, needle, or rope to fasten it is disliked (makruh tanzihan), though it does not invalidate ihram.
The illa (reason) is that such fastening resembles sewn garments.
4
Clarify the timing of idtiba'
Idtiba' (placing the rida under the right arm and over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder bare) is sunnah only during tawaf, not from the start of ihram.
This corrects a common misunderstanding; the relied-upon Hanafi position is that idtiba' is before tawaf until its end.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The Hanafi school unanimously holds that the izar and rida are sunnah, and idtiba' is specifically for tawaf. This is the view in Zahir al-Riwayah and confirmed by later authorities.
This is based on hadith and the majority of Hanafi books.

Source Text

Washings, apply perfume, pray two rak'ahs, and recite the talbiyah after the prayer intending the Hajj with it: 'Labbayka Allahumma Labbayk' as reported by Muslim. And because he is prohibited from wearing sewn garments, and there is no escape from covering the awrah and repelling heat and cold, that is with what we specified: the izar from the navel to below the knee (it is used as masculine and feminine, as in Diya' al-Huloom), and the rida over the back, shoulders, and chest, and he ties it above the navel. If he tucks its ends into his izar, there is no harm. If he fastens it with a toothpick or a needle, or ties it on himself with a rope, he did wrong and nothing is upon him. Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the sunan related to the clothing of ihram. The author begins by listing the acts: wearing two cloths, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and reciting the talbiyah. However, the focus here is on the clothing. For a man, the sunnah is to wear an izar and a rida. The izar should extend from the navel to below the knees, and the rida covers the back, shoulders, and chest, tied above the navel. Tucking the ends of the rida into the izar is permissible. However, using a needle or pin to fasten the rida, or tying it with a rope, is disliked (makruh tanzihan) though it does not invalidate the ihram. The author also clarifies that if one cannot obtain these specific cloths, covering the awrah with any garment is sufficient. It is better to wear new and white cloths, similar to the shroud. The passage then addresses a common misunderstanding regarding idtiba', which is wearing the rida under the right arm and over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder bare. Some people mistakenly think this is sunnah from the start of ihram, but the correct Hanafi position is that idtiba' is only sunnah during tawaf, not before. This is based on hadith and the consensus of Hanafi authorities like al-Khazanah, al-Ghayah, and others. The text also notes that it is permissible to wear a single garment or black cloths without stitching, though a pair without stitching is preferable.

Key Terms
الإزار (izār): The lower garment worn in ihram, covering from the navel to below the knees.
الرداء (ridā’): The upper garment worn over the shoulders and chest, covering the back and chest.
الاضطباع (idtibā‘): To wear the rida under the right arm and over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder uncovered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Two Rak'ahs and the Talbiyah at Ihram
Details the sunnah of praying two rak'ahs before ihram and reciting the talbiyah with proper intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the two rak'ahs before ihram and explain the correct intention (niyyah) for ihram per the Hanafi school, including the role of verbalization.

Core Idea
Intention is in the heart; verbalizing it is not required and may be an innovation.

This lesson explores the opening sunan of Hajj: the two rak'ahs before ihram and the talbiyah. While these acts are simple, they carry important legal distinctions about what constitutes a proper intention and how the Hanafi school treats verbalization. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling, the proof, and a key intra-Hanafi difference on whether the two rak'ahs are sunnah or merely recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled on and its hukm level (sunnah, nadb, etc.). The text explicitly states the two rak'ahs are performed 'on the face of sunnah'.
Some scholars consider it nadb (recommended) rather than sunnah; this is a later issue.
2
Understand the proof and the debate on substitution
The proof is the Prophet's (PBUH) action recorded in the two Sahihs. The text notes that the fard prayer suffices for these two rak'ahs, which leads to a debate about their status (sunnah vs nadb).
The author of al-Nahr argued that if fard suffices, it must be nadb, not sunnah; but the relied-upon view is sunnah.
3
Analyze the intention requirement
The passage emphasizes that intention (niyyah) is in the heart. Verbalizing the intention is recommended only if the heart's determination is not already settled. The Prophet (PBUH) did not command or practice a specific verbal formula.
This is a key Hanafi position: verbalization is not part of niyyah and may be bid'ah if considered necessary.
4
Apply the rule on ambiguous ihram
If one enters ihram without specifying Hajj or 'Umrah (mubham), it is valid. The pilgrim must specify before beginning the rituals; otherwise it becomes an 'Umrah.
This shows the flexibility of the Hanafi school in intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول المصنف : وصلى ركعتين) قال في التتارخانية وفي المحيط : وإن قرأ في الركعة الأولى بفاتحة الكتاب وقل يا أيها الكافرون وفي الثانية بفاتحة الكتاب و «قل هو الله أحد» تبركاً بفعل رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فهو أفضل. وفي الظهيرية قال قوله (وصل ركعتين) أي على وجه السنية بعد اللبس والتطيب لأنه عليه السلام صلاهما كما في الصحيحين ولا يصليهما في الوقت المكروه وتجزئه المكتوبة كتحية المسجد ثم ينوي بقلبه الدخول في الحج ويقول بلسانه مطابقاً لجنانه : اللهم إني أريد الحج فيسره لي وتقبله مني لأني محتاج في أداء أركانه إلى تحمل المشقة فيطلب التيسير والقبول اقتداء بالخليل وولده عليهما السلام حيث قالا : ربنا تقبل منا إنك أنت السميع العليم. ولم يؤمر بمثل هذا الدعاء عند إرادة الصلاة لأن سؤال التيسير يكون في العسير لا في اليسير وأداؤها يسير . عادة . كذا في الكافي، وقدمنا ما فيه من الخلاف في بحث نية الصلاة قوله (ولب دبر الصلاة تنوي بها الحج) أي لب عقبها ناوياً لتلبية الحج . والدبر بضم الباء وسكونها آخر الشيء . كذا في الصحاح. وإنما يلبي لما صح عنه عليه السلام من تلبيته بعد الصلاة وفي قوله تنوي بها إشارة إلى أن ما ذكره المشايخ من أنه يقول اللهم إني أريد الحج إلى آخره ليس محصلاً للنية ولهذا قال في فتح القدير : ولم نعلم أن الرواة لنسكه أنه روی سمعه عليه السلام يقول نويت العمرة ولا الحج ولهذا قال مشايخنا : إن الذكر باللسان حسن ليطابق القلب. وعلى قياس ما قدمناه في نية الصلاة إنما يحسن إذا لم تجتمع عزيمته وإلا فلا فالحاصل أن التلفظ باللسان بالنية بدعة مطلقاً في جميع العبادات وفي بعض النسخ وقل اللهم إني أريد الحج فيسره لي وتقبله مني ولب. وقوله «تنوي الحج بيان للأكمل وإلا فيصح الحج بمطلق النية . وإذا أبهم الإحرام بأن لم يعين ما أحرم به جاز أحداً من ، - الشيخ الواعظ الإسكندري : إن كثيراً من علمائنا يقرؤن بعد الفراغ من سورة «قل يا أيها الكافرون» «ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا الآية، وبعد الفراغ من (قل هو الله أحد ربنا آتنا من لدنك رحمة وهيء لنا من أمرنا رشداً قوله : (أي على وجه السنية صرح بالسنية في السراج وفي النهر : هذا الأمر أي ـ قوله وصل - للندب وفي الغاية السنة ا هـ . لكن قد يقال ينافي كونها سنة إجزاء المكتوبة عنها فلذا مشى في النهر على الندب تأمل قوله : ( وتجزئه المكتوبة كذا جزم به في اللباب. قال شارحه : وفيه نظر لأن صلاة الإحرام سنة مستقلة كصلاة الإستخارة وغيرها مما لا تنوب الفريضة منابها بخلاف تحية المسجد وشكر الوضوء فإنه ليس لهما صلاة على حدة كما حققه في فتاوى الحجة فتتأدى في ضمن غيرها أيضاً، فقول المصنف في المنسك الكبير وتجزئ المكتوبة عنها كتحية المسجد» قياس مع الفارق وهو غير صحيح ا هـ . لكن في حاشية المدني أنه رده المرشدي . قوله : (ناوياً بالتلبية الحج قال الرملي أشار إلى أن قوله في المتن «تنوي بها» ليس بإضماره قبل الذكر لأن قوله «لب» يدل على ذلك. ذكره العيني قوله : (وفي بعض النسخ الخ) أي قبل قوله «ولب» ولهذا قال ولب بعد وتقبله مني قوله : (بيان) للأكمل الخ قال في لباب المناسك : وتعيين النسك ليس بشرط فصح مبهماً وبما أحرم به الغير. ثم قال في محل آخر : ولو أحرم بما أحرم به غيره فهو مبهم فيلزمه حجة أو عمرة وقيده شارحه بما إذا لم يعلم بما أحرم به غيره قوله : (وإلا فيصح الحج بمطلق النية أي وعليه التعيين قبل الشروع في الأفعال وإلا لم يصح الحج بل هو عمرة
His saying: 'and pray two rak'ahs.' It is stated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah and al-Muhit: If he recites in the first rak'ah al-Fatihah and 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun', and in the second rak'ah al-Fatihah and 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad', following the act of the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) in seeking blessing, that is best. In al-Zahiriyyah: He said: His saying: and pray two rak'ahs, i.e., as a sunnah after wearing and applying perfume, because he (PBUH) prayed them as in the two Sahihs, and he should not pray them in a disliked time. The obligatory prayer suffices for them like tahiyyat al-masjid. Then he intends with his heart the entry into Hajj and says with his tongue corresponding to his heart: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me,' because he needs to bear hardship in performing its pillars, so he asks for ease and acceptance, following al-Khalil and his son (peace be upon them) when they said: 'Our Lord, accept from us; indeed You are the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing.' He was not commanded with such a supplication at the time of wishing to pray because asking for ease is in difficult matters, not in easy ones, and prayer is easy by custom. This is in al-Kafi. We have previously mentioned the disagreement about it in the discussion of the intention of prayer. His saying: (and recite the talbiyah after the prayer intending the Hajj with it), i.e., recite after it intending the talbiyah of Hajj. 'Dubur' (after) is with a damma or sukun on the ba, meaning the end of something, as in al-Sihah. He recites the talbiyah because it is established from him (PBUH) that he recited the talbiyah after the prayer. In his saying 'intending with it' is an indication that what the mashayikh mentioned, that he says 'O Allah I intend Hajj' etc., does not constitute the intention. For this reason it is said in Fath al-Qadir: We do not know that the narrators of his rituals reported hearing him say 'I intend 'umrah' nor Hajj. For this reason our mashayikh said: Verbal mention with the tongue is good to match the heart. According to what we previously presented in the intention of prayer, it is good only if his determination is not already settled; otherwise it is not. The conclusion is that verbalizing the intention is absolutely an innovation in all acts of worship. In some copies: 'and say O Allah I intend Hajj, make it easy for me and accept it from me, and recite the talbiyah.' And his saying 'intending the Hajj' is an explanation of the perfect way; otherwise, Hajj is valid with absolute intention. If he makes his ihram ambiguous by not specifying what he is assuming, it is valid.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers the sunnah of praying two rak'ahs before ihram and the recitation of the talbiyah. The author states that these two rak'ahs are sunnah, performed after putting on the ihram garments and applying perfume, following the Prophet's (PBUH) practice as recorded in the two Sahihs. They are not prayed at a disliked time. An important point is that the obligatory prayer (fard) can substitute for these two rak'ahs, similar to how the tahiyyat al-masjid is fulfilled by the fard prayer. However, there is a discussion among scholars: some, like the author of al-Nahr, consider it merely recommended (nadb) rather than sunnah, citing the principle that if a fard suffices, it must be nadb, not sunnah. But others, including the author of al-Ghayah, affirm it is sunnah. The passage also emphasizes that the intention (niyyah) for ihram must be made in the heart; verbal pronouncement is recommended to align the heart and tongue, but it is not required. The Prophet (PBUH) did not command a specific verbal formula for intention. The text from Fath al-Qadir notes that the narrators never heard the Prophet (PBUH) say 'I intend Hajj' etc., so verbalizing is an innovation if considered necessary. The talbiyah ('Labbayka Allahumma Labbayk') is recited after the prayer, based on the Prophet's practice. The passage also discusses ambiguous ihram (mubham), where one does not specify whether it is for Hajj or 'Umrah. Such an ihram is valid, and the pilgrim becomes bound to perform whichever he first intends when starting the actions. If he does not specify before the forbidden acts, it becomes an 'Umrah. The best practice however is to specify the intention and recite the recommended supplication.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbayka Allahumma Labbayk' etc., which is said after the prayer when entering ihram.
النية (al-niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform Hajj or 'Umrah. Verbalization is not required but recommended.
الإحرام المبهَم (al-iḥrām al-mubham): Ambiguous ihram where one does not specify whether it is for Hajj or 'Umrah. It is valid but must be specified before beginning the rituals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a person enters ihram without specifying whether it is for Hajj or 'Umrah?
A) The ihram is invalid
B) He must perform both Hajj and 'Umrah
C) The ihram is valid, but he must specify before starting the actions; otherwise it becomes 'Umrah
D) He must immediately make a new intention

Key Takeaway
The intention for ihram is in the heart; the two rak'ahs are a sunnah established by the Prophet's practice, and the talbiyah follows the prayer.

The Sunnah Prayer Before Ihram: Ruling, Proof, and Intention Du'a
Describes the sunnah prayer before ihram and the recommended du'a for intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling of the two rak'ahs before ihram, explain the evidence from the Sahihs, and identify the conditions for their validity.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs before ihram are sunnah, not wajib, and the obligatory prayer suffices for them.

This lesson examines the recommended practice of praying two rak'ahs before entering ihram for Hajj. We will explore the ruling, the proof from the Prophet's ﷺ practice, the condition of avoiding disliked times, the substitution by obligatory prayers, and the optional du'a for intention. Understanding this helps distinguish between sunnah and wajib in Hajj preparation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states 'على وجه السنية'—the two rak'ahs are sunnah (recommended), not obligatory. Confirm the Hanafi hukm level: sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah in Hanafi jurisprudence is a distinct category between wajib and mubah.
2
Locate the dalil and understand its implication
The proof is the Prophet's ﷺ practice as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. The phrase 'لأنه عليه السلام صلاهما' indicates he performed it, establishing sunnah, not obligation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it supports sunnah, not wajib.
3
Note the conditions and exceptions
The prayer should not be performed during a disliked time (makruh). Also, the obligatory prayer (e.g., Fajr) suffices for it, similar to tahiyyat al-masjid.
This substitution is a Hanafi specificity; other schools may not allow it.
4
Understand the intention (niyyah) and the du'a
Intention in the heart is required for entering ihram. The verbal du'a ('O Allah, I intend Hajj...') is recommended but not obligatory, as it is a request for ease and acceptance, unlike prayer which is easy.
The du'a follows the example of Prophet Ibrahim and Isma'il (Quran 2:127).
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If one skips these two rak'ahs, the Hajj remains valid because they are sunnah. However, missing them without excuse loses a recommended reward. The obligatory prayer can substitute if one prayed it at that time.
Some later Hanafis argued the obligatory prayer does not substitute because this sunnah is independent, but the mufta bihi is that it does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وصل ركعتين) أي على وجه السنية بعد اللبس والتطيب لأنه عليه السلام صلاهما كما في الصحيحين ولا يصليهما في الوقت المكروه وتجزئه المكتوبة كتحية المسجد ثم ينوي بقلبه الدخول في الحج ويقول بلسانه مطابقاً لجنانه : اللهم إني أريد الحج فيسره لي وتقبله مني لأني محتاج في أداء أركانه إلى تحمل المشقة فيطلب التيسير والقبول اقتداء بالخليل وولده عليهما السلام حيث قالا : ربنا تقبل منا إنك أنت السميع العليم. ولم يؤمر بمثل هذا الدعاء عند إرادة الصلاة لأن سؤال التيسير يكون في العسير لا في اليسير وأداؤها يسير . عادة . كذا في الكافي، وقدمنا ما فيه من الخلاف في بحث نية الصلاة
His saying (and pray two rak'ahs) i.e. on the basis of sunnah after wearing (ihram garments) and applying perfume because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed them as in the two Sahihs. He should not pray them in a disliked time. The obligatory prayer suffices for them like the prayer of greeting the mosque. Then he intends in his heart entering into Hajj and says with his tongue matching his inner self: O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me, because I need to bear hardship in performing its pillars, so he asks for ease and acceptance following the example of al-Khalil (Abraham) and his son (Ishmael), peace be upon them, when they said: Our Lord, accept from us; indeed You are the Hearing, the Knowing. He was not commanded with such a supplication when intending prayer because asking for ease is for something difficult, not for something easy, and performing it is usually easy. Thus in al-Kafi, and we have presented what is in it of disagreement in the discussion of the intention of prayer.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn (author's text) regarding the two rak'ahs before ihram. It clarifies that these two rak'ahs are sunnah (recommended) after wearing the ihram garments and applying perfume, based on the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. The prayer should not be performed during a disliked time (makruh). The commentator also states that a person's obligatory prayer (e.g., Fajr or Zuhr) suffices for these sunnah rak'ahs, analogous to the way the obligatory prayer suffices for the prayer of greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid). After the prayer, one should form the intention in the heart for entering Hajj and verbally express a supplication asking Allah to make it easy and accept it. The reasoning is that Hajj involves hardship, unlike prayer which is easy. The commentator notes that this verbal du'a is not compulsory but is recommended to align the tongue with the heart. The passage also points to a previous discussion about the intention in prayer, indicating that the requirement for verbal utterance differs.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): In this context, sunnah means a recommended act (mandub), not obligatory.
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): The two-rak'ah prayer performed when entering a mosque as a greeting.
النية (al-niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform the act of worship; verbal utterance is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs before ihram are sunnah, not wajib; the obligatory prayer can substitute for them, and the intention is in the heart with a recommended verbal du'a.

Talbiyah After Prayer: Timing and Sunnah
Explains the recommended time for talbiyah and the meaning of 'dubur'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that reciting talbiyah immediately after the obligatory prayer is sunnah and identify the linguistic meaning of 'dubur'.

Core Idea
Talbiyah after prayer is sunnah, following the Prophet's practice.

This lesson unpacks the phrase 'ولب دبر الصلاة' (and recite Labbayk after the prayer). The author clarifies that the Prophet (ﷺ) himself recited talbiyah after prayer, making it a recommended practice. We will examine the word 'dubur' and understand that the talbiyah is a separate act from the intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
The passage commands to recite talbiyah 'dubur al-salah' – immediately after the prayer. The word 'dubur' means the end or immediately after.
2
Recognize the sunnah basis
The proof is the Prophet's practice: 'لما صح عنه عليه السلام من تلبيته بعد الصلاة' – it is authentically reported that he recited talbiyah after prayer.
3
Differentiate talbiyah from intention
The phrase 'تنوي بها' (intending by it) indicates that the talbiyah is a verbal declaration, while the intention is in the heart. The verbal du'a is not required.
4
Understand the ruling level
The command 'ولب' is interpreted as sunnah, not wajib, because the talbiyah is a sunnah act of the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولب دبر الصلاة تنوي بها الحج) أي لب عقبها ناوياً لتلبية الحج . والدبر بضم الباء وسكونها آخر الشيء . كذا في الصحاح. وإنما يلبي لما صح عنه عليه السلام من تلبيته بعد الصلاة وفي قوله تنوي بها إشارة إلى أن ما ذكره المشايخ من أنه يقول اللهم إني أريد الحج إلى آخره ليس محصلاً للنية ولهذا قال في فتح القدير : ولم نعلم أن الرواة لنسكه أنه روی سمعه عليه السلام يقول نويت العمرة ولا الحج ولهذا قال مشايخنا : إن الذكر باللسان حسن ليطابق القلب. وعلى قياس ما قدمناه في نية الصلاة إنما يحسن إذا لم تجتمع عزيمته وإلا فلا فالحاصل أن التلفظ باللسان بالنية بدعة مطلقاً في جميع العبادات وفي بعض النسخ وقل اللهم إني أريد الحج فيسره لي وتقبله مني ولب. وقوله «تنوي الحج بيان للأكمل وإلا فيصح الحج بمطلق النية . وإذا أبهم الإحرام بأن لم يعين ما أحرم به جاز
His saying (and say 'Labbayk' after the prayer, intending by it Hajj) meaning say 'Labbayk' immediately after it, intending the talbiyah of Hajj. Al-dubur (with dammah on the ba or sukun) means the end of something. Thus in al-Sihah. He only recites the talbiyah because it is authentically reported from him (peace be upon him) that he recited the talbiyah after prayer. In his saying 'intending by it' there is an indication that what the scholars mentioned about him saying 'O Allah, I intend Hajj' etc. is not achieving the intention. Hence it is said in Fath al-Qadir: We do not know that the narrators of his rites reported that he was heard to say 'I intend Umrah' or 'Hajj'. Hence our scholars said: Verbal mention with the tongue is good to match the heart. And according to what we presented regarding the intention of prayer, it is only good if his determination has not gathered, otherwise not. So the conclusion is that uttering the intention with the tongue is an innovation (bid'ah) absolutely in all acts of worship. In some copies: 'And say: O Allah I intend Hajj, make it easy for me and accept it from me, and say Labbayk.' His saying 'intending Hajj' is an explanation of the most complete, otherwise Hajj is valid with absolute intention. And if he made the ihram ambiguous by not specifying what he entered into, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the phrase 'and say Labbayk after the prayer intending by it Hajj'. It clarifies that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited the talbiyah after the prayer, so this is the sunnah. The word 'dubur' means the end of something (here, after the prayer). The commentator notes that the verbal du'a 'O Allah I intend Hajj' is not required for the intention; rather the intention is in the heart. The Prophet (ﷺ) was not reported to verbally say 'I intend Hajj'. The scholars say that uttering the intention with the tongue is good to align with the heart, but it is not an obligation. In fact, if one insists on it as a requirement, it becomes a bid'ah (innovation). The ruling is that the intention is sufficient in the heart. The phrase 'intending Hajj' in the matn is for completeness, but a valid Hajj can be performed with an absolute intention, and even if one does not specify Hajj or Umrah at all (ibham), it is allowed. Later, he must specify before beginning the actions.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The uttering of 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' as a declaration of entering the state of ihram.
الدبر (al-dubur): The end or immediately after something; here, after the prayer.
إبهام الإحرام (ibham al-ihram): Entering ihram without specifying whether for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Reciting talbiyah immediately after the obligatory prayer is a sunnah act established by the Prophet's practice.

Intention for Ihram: Verbal Utterance and Ambiguity
Explains that verbal utterance of intention is not required and ambiguous ihram is permissible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why verbal utterance of the intention is not required and that entering ihram without specifying (ibham) is valid in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Intention is in the heart; verbal utterance is not required, and unspecified ihram is valid.

This lesson focuses on the nature of intention (niyyah) for ihram. The passage strongly emphasizes that the intention is an act of the heart, not the tongue. The common practice of saying 'O Allah, I intend Hajj' is not required and, if treated as mandatory, becomes an innovation. Moreover, one may enter ihram without specifying whether it is for Hajj or Umrah—this is called ibham.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of verbal du'a
The passage notes that the du'a 'اللهم إني أريد الحج' is not the intention; it is merely a verbal expression that is good to match the heart.
2
Identify the evidence from prophetic practice
The Prophet (ﷺ) was not reported to say 'I intend Hajj' or 'I intend Umrah' verbally. This shows that the verbal utterance is not part of the Sunnah.
3
Learn the ruling on verbal intention as a requirement
If one considers uttering the intention as obligatory, it becomes bid'ah. The passage states: 'فالحاصل أن التلفظ باللسان بالنية بدعة مطلقاً في جميع العبادات'.
4
Apply the principle of absolute intention
The matn says 'تنوي الحج' is for completeness, but Hajj is valid with 'مطلق النية' (absolute intention). This means one does not need to specify Hajj or Umrah definitely.
5
Understand ambiguous ihram (ibham)
If one enters ihram without specifying (e.g., just intending to enter the sacred state), it is valid. The passage concludes 'وإذا أبهم الإحرام بأن لم يعين ما أحرم به جاز'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولب دبر الصلاة تنوي بها الحج) أي لب عقبها ناوياً لتلبية الحج . والدبر بضم الباء وسكونها آخر الشيء . كذا في الصحاح. وإنما يلبي لما صح عنه عليه السلام من تلبيته بعد الصلاة وفي قوله تنوي بها إشارة إلى أن ما ذكره المشايخ من أنه يقول اللهم إني أريد الحج إلى آخره ليس محصلاً للنية ولهذا قال في فتح القدير : ولم نعلم أن الرواة لنسكه أنه روی سمعه عليه السلام يقول نويت العمرة ولا الحج ولهذا قال مشايخنا : إن الذكر باللسان حسن ليطابق القلب. وعلى قياس ما قدمناه في نية الصلاة إنما يحسن إذا لم تجتمع عزيمته وإلا فلا فالحاصل أن التلفظ باللسان بالنية بدعة مطلقاً في جميع العبادات وفي بعض النسخ وقل اللهم إني أريد الحج فيسره لي وتقبله مني ولب. وقوله «تنوي الحج بيان للأكمل وإلا فيصح الحج بمطلق النية . وإذا أبهم الإحرام بأن لم يعين ما أحرم به جاز
His saying (and say 'Labbayk' after the prayer, intending by it Hajj) meaning say 'Labbayk' immediately after it, intending the talbiyah of Hajj. Al-dubur (with dammah on the ba or sukun) means the end of something. Thus in al-Sihah. He only recites the talbiyah because it is authentically reported from him (peace be upon him) that he recited the talbiyah after prayer. In his saying 'intending by it' there is an indication that what the scholars mentioned about him saying 'O Allah, I intend Hajj' etc. is not achieving the intention. Hence it is said in Fath al-Qadir: We do not know that the narrators of his rites reported that he was heard to say 'I intend Umrah' or 'Hajj'. Hence our scholars said: Verbal mention with the tongue is good to match the heart. And according to what we presented regarding the intention of prayer, it is only good if his determination has not gathered, otherwise not. So the conclusion is that uttering the intention with the tongue is an innovation (bid'ah) absolutely in all acts of worship. In some copies: 'And say: O Allah I intend Hajj, make it easy for me and accept it from me, and say Labbayk.' His saying 'intending Hajj' is an explanation of the most complete, otherwise Hajj is valid with absolute intention. And if he made the ihram ambiguous by not specifying what he entered into, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the phrase 'and say Labbayk after the prayer intending by it Hajj'. It clarifies that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited the talbiyah after the prayer, so this is the sunnah. The word 'dubur' means the end of something (here, after the prayer). The commentator notes that the verbal du'a 'O Allah I intend Hajj' is not required for the intention; rather the intention is in the heart. The Prophet (ﷺ) was not reported to verbally say 'I intend Hajj'. The scholars say that uttering the intention with the tongue is good to align with the heart, but it is not an obligation. In fact, if one insists on it as a requirement, it becomes a bid'ah (innovation). The ruling is that the intention is sufficient in the heart. The phrase 'intending Hajj' in the matn is for completeness, but a valid Hajj can be performed with an absolute intention, and even if one does not specify Hajj or Umrah at all (ibham), it is allowed. Later, he must specify before beginning the actions.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The uttering of 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' as a declaration of entering the state of ihram.
الدبر (al-dubur): The end or immediately after something; here, after the prayer.
إبهام الإحرام (ibham al-ihram): Entering ihram without specifying whether for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on entering ihram without specifying whether it is for Hajj or Umrah?
A) It is impermissible (haram)
B) It is permissible (ja'iz)
C) It is recommended (mustahabb)
D) It is invalid (batil)

Key Takeaway
Intention in the heart suffices; verbal utterance is not required, and ambiguous ihram is valid.

The Wording and Transmission of the Talbiyah
Quotes the full talbiyah and its transmission authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact wording of the talbiyah as transmitted in the six canonical hadith books and identify its ruling as sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The talbiyah wording is mutawatir from the Prophet, making it a sunnah to recite as narrated.

The talbiyah is a central declaration of the pilgrim entering ihram. Its wording is not arbitrary but established through rigorous transmission. In this lesson, we examine the exact text reported in the six major hadith collections and clarify its legal status within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the talbiyah text
Locate the talbiyah wording as quoted in the passage and note that it is attributed to the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam).
The passage begins: 'قوله (وهي لبيك اللهم لبيك...'
2
Recognize the chain of transmission
The passage states that the six canonical books (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.) narrate this exact wording, giving it a high level of reliability (mutawatir).
The phrase 'هكذا روى أصحاب الكتب الستة تلبيته' confirms this.
3
Determine the legal ruling
Reciting the talbiyah is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommendation) in the Hanafi school, though some consider it wajib. The focus here is on its wording.
The hanafi_position_box from the source confirms this.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
A pilgrim should recite the talbiyah as narrated, without altering the wording, to follow the sunnah.
The wording is fixed; deviations are not recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وهي لبيك اللهم لبيك لبيك لا شريك لك لبيك إن الحمد والنعمة لك والملك لا شريك لك) هكذا روى أصحاب الكتب الستة تلبيته الله ، ولفظها مصدر مثنى تثنية يراد بها التكثير وهو ملزوم النصب والإضافة والناصب له من غير لفظه تقديره أجبت إجابتك إجابة بعد إجابة إلى ما لا نهاية له، وكأنه من ألب بالمكان إذا أقام فهو مصدر محذوف الزوائد والقياس الباب، ومفرد لبيك لب واختلف في الداعي فقيل هو الله تعالى، وقيل إبراهيم الخليل عليه السلام، ورجحه المصنف في الكافي وقال : إنه الأظهر . وقيل رسولنا . واختلف في همز «إن الحمد» بعد الاتفاق على جواز الكسر والفتح واختار في الهداية أن الأوجه الكسر على استئناف الثناء وتكون التلبية للذات. وقال الكسائي : الفتح أحسن على أنه تعليل للتلبيه أي لبيك لأن الحمد. ورجح الأول في فتح القدير بأن تعليق الإجابة التي لا نهاية لها بالذات أولى منه باعتبار صفة هذا وإن كان استئناف الثناء لا يتعين مع الكسر لجواز كونه تعليلاً مستأنفاً كما في قولك علم ابنك العلم أن العلم نافعه قال تعالى وصل عليهم إن صلاتك سكن لهم ﴾ [التوبة: ١٠٣] وهذا مقرر في مسالك العلة من علم الأصول لكن لما جاز فيه كل منهما يحمل على الأول لأولويته ولأكثريته بخلاف الفتح ليس فيه سوى أنه تعليل
His saying (And it is: Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk, Labbayk la sharika laka Labbayk, inna al-hamda wa al-ni'mata laka wa al-mulka la sharika laka) Thus the authors of the six canonical books narrated his (peace be upon him) talbiyah. Its wording is a verbal noun in the dual form, intending multiplicity. It is necessarily in the accusative case and annexed, and the governing word is implicit, being approximately: 'I have responded to Your call, a response after response without end'. It is derived from 'alibba bil-makan' meaning he stayed in a place, so it is a verbal noun with extra letters removed, and the regular form would be 'lubb'. The singular of Labbayk is 'Labb'. There is disagreement about the caller: it is said it is Allah Almighty, and it is said it is Ibrahim al-Khalil (Abraham) peace be upon him, which the author in al-Kafi preferred, saying it is the more apparent. And it is said it is our Prophet. There is also disagreement about the hamzah of 'Inna al-hamda' after agreement on the permissibility of kasr (breaking) and fatha (opening). Al-Hidayah chose that the more correct is kasr, considering it an independent praise, and the talbiyah is for the Essence (dhat). Al-Kisai said: fatha is better, as it is a reason for the talbiyah, i.e., 'I respond because the praise belongs to You'. The first was preferred in Fath al-Qadir by saying that linking the endless response to the Essence is more appropriate than considering a attribute. Although restarting the praise is not necessarily required with kasr because it can still be a renewed reason, as in saying 'Teach your son knowledge, for knowledge benefits him'. Allah says: 'And pray for them, indeed your prayer is a comfort for them' [9:103]. This is established in the methods of 'illah in Usul. However, since both are possible, it is taken as the first due to its precedence and frequency, unlike fatha which only indicates reason.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage provides the exact wording of the talbiyah as narrated in the six major hadith books. The commentator then explains the linguistic form: 'Labbayk' is a dual form (masdar muthanna) used to indicate repetition and abundance. It is considered to be a verbal noun meaning 'I respond repeatedly', with the implied verb 'Ijabtuka' (I respond to You). The singular is 'Labb'. There is a discussion about who originally called out the talbiyah: it is attributed to Allah, Prophet Ibrahim, or our Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), with the author preferring Ibrahim. Then a grammatical debate: whether to read 'Inna al-hamda' with a kasra (inna) or fatha (anna). In the Hidayah, the choice of kasra is preferred because it makes the praise an independent statement, not a reason. The commentator Fath al-Qadir prefers kasra as well, arguing that linking the endless response (labbayk) to Allah's essence rather than a specific attribute is more appropriate. However, even with kasra, it can still function as a reason. The alternative fatha makes it purely a reason. The Hanafi school generally follows kasra.

Key Terms
التلبية (talbiyah): A specific declaration: 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' uttered during ihram.
الكتب الستة (al-kutub al-sittah): The six canonical hadith collections (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, from which source is the talbiyah wording transmitted?
A) Only from Imam Malik's Muwatta
B) From the six canonical hadith books
C) From the Quran directly
D) From the consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The talbiyah wording is fixed and mutawatir from the Prophet, and the Hanafi school follows the exact wording as sunnah muakkadah.

Linguistic and Grammatical Analysis of the Talbiyah
Explains linguistic and grammatical aspects of the talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the linguistic form of 'Labbayk' as a dual verbal noun indicating repetition and analyze the preferred reading of 'inna al-hamda' in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Labbayk is a dual form meaning 'I respond repeatedly', and reading 'inna' with kasr makes the praise independent, which is preferred in the Hanafi school.

The talbiyah is not a simple phrase; its words carry deep linguistic meaning. In this lesson, we unpack the dual form of 'Labbayk', the implied verb, and the grammatical debate over the hamzah in 'inna al-hamda'. Understanding these nuances helps us appreciate why the Hanafi school prefers one reading over another.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the word 'Labbayk' linguistically
Identify that 'Labbayk' is a verbal noun (masdar) in the dual form (muthanna) used to indicate multiplicity. Note that it is derived from 'alibba' meaning to stay.
The passage says: 'ولفظها مصدر مثنى تثنية يراد بها التكثير'
2
Understand the grammatical construction
Recognize that 'Labbayk' is in the accusative case (mansub) and annexed (mudaf). The governing word is implicit, approximately 'Ijabtuka' (I respond to You).
The singular is 'labb'.
3
Examine the disagreement about the caller
Note the three opinions: the caller is Allah, Ibrahim (alayh al-salam), or our Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam). The author of al-Kafi prefers Ibrahim.
This is not a legal dispute but a historical one.
4
Analyze the grammatical reading of 'inna al-hamda'
Focus on the debate: reading with kasr (inna) as an independent statement vs. fatha (anna) as a reason (ta'lil). The Hanafi school, through al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir, prefers kasr.
The preference is based on linking the response to Allah's essence rather than an attribute.
5
Apply the preferred reading in recitation
When reciting the talbiyah, a Hanafi pilgrim should pronounce 'inna' with a kasrah to follow the preferred practice.
Both readings are valid, but kasr is more virtuous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
