Fulfilling Hajjat al-Islam with Absolute Intention
Examines if the obligatory Hajj is performed through supererogatory intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether Hajjat al-Islam is performed by a nafl or absolute intention, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
An absolute intention for Hajj suffices for the obligation; a nafl intention does not.

When a Muslim intends to perform Hajj without specifying whether it is fard or nafl, what is the ruling? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer: it counts as the obligatory Hajj if the person is obligated. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
The passage asks: does entering ihram with a nafl intention fulfill Hajjat al-Islam? Or does an absolute (unspecified) intention do so? Understand the two scenarios.
2
State the Hanafi Principle
The principle: Hajjat al-Islam is not performed by a nafl intention, but it is performed by an absolute intention. The reasoning involves two resemblances: the time is like a measurement (mi'yariyyah) and like a container (zarfiyyah).
Mi'yariyyah prevents nafl from fulfilling fard; zarfiyyah allows absolute intention to fulfill fard.
3
Outline the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf (in the sound narration) hold that absolute intention suffices. Muhammad al-Shaybani differs on the combined intention case (vow+nafl). Another narration from Abu Yusuf aligns with Shafi'i, requiring explicit fard intention.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text declares the position of Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf as the correct and relied-upon one: absolute intention makes the Hajj count as fard.
The opposing view (Abu Yusuf's other narration) is not taken.
5
Apply to Practical Scenarios
If someone intends Hajj for another person, or as a vow, or as nafl, it does not fulfill Hajjat al-Islam. If they intend both vow and nafl, the more cautious view is that it is nafl (Muhammad's view).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر في الكتاب أن حجة الإسلام تتأدى بنية التطوع .اهـ. والمنقول في الأصول أنها لا تتأدى بنية النفل وتتأدى بمطلق النية نظراً إلى أن الوقت له فيه شبهة المعيارية وشبهة الظرفية فالأولى للثاني والثاني للأول . قال في شرح اللباب : ولو أحرم بالحج ولم ينو فرضاً ولا تطوعاً فهو فرض أي يقع عن حجة الإسلام استحساناً بالاتفاق في ظاهر المذهب وقيل يقع نفلاً. ولو نوى الحج عن الغير أو النذر أو النفل كان عما نوى وإن لم يحج للفرض أي لحجة الإسلام. كذا ذكره غير واحد وهو الصحيح المعتمد المنقول الصريح عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف من أنه لا يتأدى الفرض بنية النفل في هذا الباب، وروي عن أبي يوسف وهو مذهب الشافعي عن حجة الإسلام. ولو نوى للمنذور والنفل معاً قيل هو نقل وهو قول محمد، وقيل نذر وهو قول أبي يوسف والأول أظهر وأحوط والثاني أوسع ويؤيده أنه لو نوى فرضاً ونفلاً فهو فرض . ا هـ متناً وشرحاً ملخصاً.
And it was not mentioned in the book that the Hajj of Islam is performed by the intention of supererogation. The transmitted view in the usul (principles) is that it is not performed by the intention of nafl, but is performed by absolute intention, considering that the time (for Hajj) has a resemblance to measurement (mi'yariyyah) and a resemblance to container (zarfiyyah); the first (not performed by nafl) is for the second (resemblance to container), and the second (performed by absolute intention) is for the first (resemblance to measurement).
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage deals with a subtle issue: if a person intends to perform Hajj but does not specify whether it is the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam) or a supererogatory Hajj (nafl), what is the ruling? The author states that the book (likely al-Hidayah or the matn) did not explicitly mention this. The principle in the usul (fiqh principles) is that the obligatory Hajj is not performed with a mere nafl intention, but it is performed with an absolute intention (i.e., just intending Hajj without specifying). The reasoning is that the time for Hajj has two aspects: one is like a measurement (mi'yariyyah) — the Hajj is measured by the intention as to whether it is obligatory or nafl — and the other is like a container (zarfiyyah) — the time encompasses the act. The explanation is somewhat technical: the first aspect (mi'yariyyah) prevents a nafl intention from fulfilling the obligation, while the second aspect (zarfiyyah) allows an absolute intention to fulfill the obligation, since the time is dedicated to Hajj and the absolute intention is sufficient. The passage then quotes from Sharh al-Lubab: if a person enters ihram for Hajj without specifying fard or nafl, it falls as fard (obligatory) by istihsan according to the majority of the madhhab, although some said it falls as nafl. If he intends Hajj on behalf of another person, or as a vow (nadhr), or as nafl, it counts as what he intended and does not fulfill the obligatory Hajj. This is the sound, relied-upon position transmitted explicitly from Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, that the fard is not performed by a nafl intention in this matter. It is also reported from Abu Yusuf (and it is the view of al-Shafi'i) regarding Hajjat al-Islam. If one intends both a vow and nafl together, some say it is nafl (Muhammad's view), some say it is a vow (Abu Yusuf's view); the first is more apparent and cautious, the second is broader. This is supported by the fact that if someone intends fard and nafl together, it is fard.

Key Terms
حجة الإسلام (hajjat al-islam): The obligatory Hajj that every capable Muslim must perform once in a lifetime.
نية التطوع (niyyat al-tatawwu'): Intention to perform a supererogatory act of worship (nafl).
المطلق (al-mutlaq): Absolute or unspecified intention, i.e., just intending Hajj without specifying fard or nafl.
المعية (al-mi'yariyyah): Resemblance to a measurement – the intention measures the act; specifying nafl makes it nafl.
الظرفية (al-zarfiyyah): Resemblance to a container – the time 'contains' the worship; absolute intention is enough.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a person enters ihram for Hajj and intends 'Hajj' without specifying fard or nafl, what is the ruling?
A) It is invalid because the intention is ambiguous.
B) It counts as nafl Hajj.
C) It counts as Hajjat al-Islam (fard) if the person is obligated.
D) It counts as a vowed Hajj.

Key Takeaway
An absolute intention for Hajj (without specifying fard or nafl) fulfills the obligatory Hajj in the Hanafi school, based on the principle that the time is like a container.

intermediate
15 min
The Talbiyah and Intention for Ihram: Rulings and Proofs
Defines the talbiyah wording, rulings on additions/deletions, and the necessity of intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the talbiyah (its wording, increase, decrease) and explain the requirement of intention for ihram, citing the proof from the hadith of Ali and distinguishing the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Ihram requires both intention and a verbal expression; the talbiyah is a sunnah, and any remembrance of Allah suffices.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the talbiyah and the intention for entering the state of ihram. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands upon the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the precise wording of the talbiyah, the rulings on increasing or decreasing it, and the essential requirement of specifying one's intention. We will explore the textual proof from the hadith of Ali and the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Abu Yusuf, as well as the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the talbiyah wording and its status
The text provides the exact wording of the talbiyah as narrated in the six books. Recognize that the talbiyah is a sunnah, not a condition; the condition is any remembrance of Allah with the intent of magnification.
The linguistic analysis of 'labbayk' indicates repetition and endless response.
2
Understand the ruling on increase and decrease
The author states 'increase in it and do not decrease.' Increase is recommended (mustahabb), while decrease is disliked (makruh tanzihi), though some earlier texts said it is not permissible. The commentator reconciles by noting that the talbiyah is a sunnah, so leaving it entirely is disliked, and decreasing is similarly disliked.
3
Analyze the requirement of intention and specification
Ihram requires both intention and a verbal expression (talbiyah or equivalent). The hadith of Ali is cited as proof that a general intention suffices if not specified. However, Hanafi school holds that specification (ta'yin) of Hajj or Umrah is required before beginning actions; otherwise, the first circumambulation determines it for Umrah.
The text also discusses scenarios like ihsar or intercourse that determine the type.
4
Compare the Hanafi position with intra-Hanafi and Shafi'i views
Abu Yusuf held that intention alone suffices for ihram, analogous to fasting. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require both intention and talbiyah, analogous to prayer. The Shafi'i school also holds that intention alone suffices. The relied-upon position is the majority view.
The difference stems from whether ihram is seen as a commitment to actions (like prayer) or mere abstinence (like fasting).

The Book of Hajj: Chapter of Ihram. 'You have no partner, here I am at Your service. Indeed, all praise, grace, and sovereignty are Yours. You have no partner.' And increase in it, and do not decrease. And specification (of intention) is required before beginning the actions. The origin is the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) when he came from Yemen and said: I entered ihram with what the Messenger of Allah entered ihram, and he approved it. If he does not specify and performs one circumambulation, it is for Umrah. Likewise, if he is prevented before the actions and exits with a sacrifice, it is determined for Umrah, so that he must make it up to complete Hajj. Likewise, if he has intercourse and invalidates, he must continue in Umrah. Al-Zahiriyyah said: It is not mentioned in the book that the Hajj of Islam is performed with the intention of voluntary. End quote. And what is transmitted in the principles is that it is not performed with the intention of supererogatory, but is performed with absolute intention, considering that the time has the semblance of measurement and the semblance of container. So the first is for the second, and the second is for the first. His statement: 'And it is: Here I am, O Allah, here I am, here I am, You have no partner, here I am. Indeed, all praise, grace, and sovereignty are Yours. You have no partner.' Thus the compilers of the six books narrated his (the Prophet's) talbiyah. Its wording is a doubled infinitive intended for repetition, and it is in the accusative case and annexed. The implicit governing word is: 'I answer Your call, an answering after answering without end.' It is derived from 'alabba bi al-makan' meaning to stay. It is an infinitive with the extra letters omitted, and the measure is 'al-baab'. The singular is 'labb'. There is disagreement about the caller: some say it is Allah, some say it is Ibrahim al-Khalil (peace be upon him), and the author preferred this in al-Kafi and said it is the more apparent. Some say it is our Prophet. They disagreed about the hamza of 'inna al-hamda' after agreement on the permissibility of kasr and fath. Al-Hidayah chose that kasr is more appropriate for beginning praise, and the talbiyah is for the Essence. Al-Kisai said: fath is better as a cause for the talbiyah, i.e., 'Here I am because praise is Yours.' The first was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because attributing endless response to the Essence is more appropriate than to a quality. Even though beginning praise is not specific with kasr because it is permissible for it to be a separate cause, as in your saying 'Teach your son knowledge, indeed knowledge benefits him.' Allah says (Quran 9:103): 'Pray for them, indeed your prayer is a comfort for them.' This is established in the methods of cause from the science of principles. But since both are permissible, it is taken as the first due to its priority and frequency, unlike fath which only indicates a cause. His statement: 'It occurs' as understood from later. His statement: 'And it is not mentioned in the book, etc.' He said in Sharh al-Lubab: If he enters ihram for Hajj and does not intend obligatory nor voluntary, it is obligatory, i.e., it falls for the Hajj of Islam by istihsan, by agreement in the apparent school. Some say it falls as voluntary. And if he intends Hajj for another, or for a vow, or as voluntary, it is for what he intended, even if he did not intend the obligatory Hajj of Islam. Thus many mentioned it, and it is the correct, relied-upon, explicit transmission from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that the obligatory is not performed by the intention of voluntary in this chapter. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf, and it is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, that the Hajj of Islam (is performed by intention). And if he intends both the vowed and voluntary, some say it is voluntary—this is the saying of Muhammad; some say it is a vow—this is the saying of Abu Yusuf. The first is more apparent and more cautious, the second is broader. It is supported by the fact that if he intends obligatory and voluntary, it is obligatory. End from the text and commentary summarized. And in its text: He entered ihram with something then forgot it, then Hajj and Umrah are binding on him, he performs their actions first, and the hady of qiran is not binding on him. His statement: 'So the first is for the second' means that it is not performed with the intention of voluntary due to its semblance of container like prayer, and the second is for the first means it is performed with absolute intention due to its semblance of measurement like fasting. The author's statement: 'And increase' in it means increase upon these words. So when you say the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. So fear lewdness, transgression, argument, killing of game, and pointing to it. And increase in it and do not decrease means in the talbiyah. The increase is like: 'Here I am, and ready to obey, goodness is in Your hands, desire is to You, action is for You, here I am, Creator of creation, Forgiver of sins, here I am, Possessor of grace and beautiful favor, here I am, as many as the grains of dust, here I am, indeed life is the life of the Hereafter,' as narrated from several Companions. The author stated in al-Kafi that increase is good like repetition. Al-Halabi stated in his Manasik that it is recommended in our school. As for decrease, the author said it is not permissible. Ibn al-Malik said in Sharh al-Majma': It is disliked by agreement. Apparently it is a disliked of tanzih because the talbiyah is only a sunnah. Indeed the condition is only remembrance of Allah, whether in Persian or Arabic—this is well-known from our scholars. The particular talbiyah is a sunnah. So if one leaves it entirely, he commits a disliked of tanzih. So if he decreases from it, likewise by priority. So the author's statement 'not permissible' has apparent consideration. And the saying of whoever said that the talbiyah is a condition means remembrance intended for magnification, not its specific form. We restricted to increase in the talbiyah because increase in the adhan is not legislated because it is for announcement, and it is not achieved by other than the customary. And in the tashahhud in prayer, if it is the first, it is not legislated like its repetition because it is in the middle of prayer, so one restricts to what is transmitted. If it is the last, it is legislated because it is a place of remembrance and praise. His statement: 'So when you say the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram.' It indicates that one is not a muhrim except with both. So if he performs both, he has entered into specific prohibitions, so they are the essence of ihram legally. Husam al-Din al-Shahid mentioned that he becomes a starter with intention but at the time of talbiyah, not by the talbiyah, just as he becomes a starter in prayer with intention but at the time of takbir, not by the takbir. And he does not become a starter with intention alone by analogy to prayer. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that intention suffices by analogy to fasting, in that both are acts of worship that refrain from prohibitions. Our analogy is more appropriate because it is a commitment to actions like prayer, not mere refraining; rather, refraining is a condition, so it is more similar to prayer. And what is meant by talbiyah is a condition from the specifics of the rituals, whether it be talbiyah or remembrance intended for magnification, or driving a sacrificial animal, or garlanding the camel, as mentioned by the author in al-Mustasfa. Al-Asbijabi mentioned that if he drives a sacrificial animal intending for Makkah, he becomes a muhrim by driving, whether he intended or not. Thus in the commentary. He said in al-Nahr: So the container is in the meaning of 'upon' because increase is only after coming with it during it, as in al-Siraj. End. His statement: 'So if he decreases from it, likewise by priority.' He said in al-Nahr: In it is consideration, for in al-Fath, the talbiyah once is a condition, and increase is sunnah. He said in al-Muhit: So that he is not blameworthy for leaving it. Then he said: Indeed raising the voice with it is sunnah, so if he leaves it, he is blameworthy! So decreasing with blameworthiness is more appropriate! But in al-Fath also: It is recommended to raise the voice in all of the talbiyah without straining so as not to weaken, and the author transmitted it from al-Halabi. And one may dispute the claim of priority, especially since the author previously mentioned that blameworthiness is less than dislike, so let it be considered. His statement: 'It indicates that he is not a muhrim except with both.' He said in al-Nahr: Then this expression only indicates that he becomes a muhrim at intention and talbiyah, but not that ihram is with both or with one conditioned on mentioning the other. And al-Shahid mentioned that he becomes a starter with intention.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the talbiyah and the requirements for entering ihram. It is an expansion of the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by stating the wording of the talbiyah as transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and explains its linguistic meaning and the differing opinions on who first uttered it. He then discusses the requirement of specifying intention (ta'yin al-niyyah) before beginning the actions of Hajj or Umrah, citing the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where he entered ihram with the same intention as the Prophet. The passage clarifies that if one does not specify, the first circumambulation determines it for Umrah. A significant portion is devoted to the ruling on increasing or decreasing the talbiyah: increase is recommended (mustahabb), while decrease is disliked (makruh tanzihi), contrary to the author's initial statement that it is not permissible (la yajuza), which the commentator critiques. The text also addresses the relationship between intention and talbiyah in constituting ihram. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that both are necessary; intention alone is insufficient, analogous to prayer where intention and takbir are both required. This is contrasted with the view of Abu Yusuf that intention alone suffices, analogous to fasting. The passage further explains that the essential element is remembrance of Allah (dhikr) with the intent of magnification, not necessarily the specific talbiyah wording. Therefore, if one drives a sacrificial animal or garlands it with the intention of entering ihram, that suffices. This commentary is based solely on the provided Arabic text, explaining each ruling and the reasoning behind it within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The specific phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by the muhrim upon entering ihram, considered a sunnah.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by intention and the talbiyah (or equivalent), which imposes prohibitions on certain actions.
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specifying whether the ihram is for Hajj or Umrah, or for a particular type (obligatory, voluntary, etc.). Required before beginning the actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on decreasing the talbiyah (leaving out some words)?
A) Haram (unlawful)
B) Makruh tanzihi (disliked, but not sinful)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Sunnah (recommended)

Key Takeaway
Ihram requires both intention and a verbal expression; the talbiyah is a sunnah, but any remembrance of Allah with magnification suffices; increase is recommended, decrease is disliked.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Rulings on Increasing or Decreasing the Talbiyah
Explaining the ruling on adding to or reducing the talbiyah for ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increasing and decreasing the talbiyah and distinguish between the views of al-Marghinani and the preferred view.

Core Idea
Increasing talbiyah is recommended; decreasing it is makruh tanzihi, not haram.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the commentator explains a matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the talbiyah during ihram. He clarifies that while increasing the talbiyah with extra phrases is recommended (mustahabb), decreasing it is only mildly disliked (makruh tanzihi) according to the preferred view, not prohibited. This distinction is based on the principle that the essential requirement of ihram is any remembrance of Allah intending veneration, not the specific wording of the talbiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two rulings
The passage addresses two acts: increasing the talbiyah (adding extra phrases) and decreasing it (omitting parts). Note that each has a different ruling.
The matn says 'increase and do not decrease', but the commentator refines the decrease ruling.
2
Understand the basis for the increase ruling
The author cites reports from several Companions showing that they added phrases. He also quotes al-Nasafi and al-Halabi who consider increase hasanah or mustahabb.
Increase is deemed good and recommended, not obligatory.
3
Analyze the decrease ruling dispute
Al-Marghinani's matn states 'do not decrease', which some take as a prohibition. Ibn al-Malak says it is makruh by agreement. The commentator prefers makruh tanzihi.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school: haram vs. makruh tanzihi.
4
Examine the commentator's tarjih reasoning
The commentator argues that since the talbiyah itself is sunnah (not fard), and the condition for ihram is any dhikr, decreasing is only a minor offense by analogy to leaving it entirely.
The logical argument (dalil aqli) uses the principle of a fortiori: if leaving entirely is only makruh tanzihi, then decreasing is likewise.
5
Distinguish from adhan and tashahhud
The commentator notes that increase in adhan is not allowed because adhan is for announcement, and unconventional wording defeats that purpose. Similarly, increase in first tashahhud is not allowed, but in last tashahhud it is.
This contrast shows that the ruling on increase is specific to the talbiyah context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام فإذا لبيت ناوياً فقد أحرمت فاتق الرفث والفسوق والجدال وقتل الصيد والإشارة إليه وزد فيها ولا تنقص أي في التلبية ولا تنقص منها والزيادة مثل لبيك وسعديك والخير بيديك والرغباء إليك والعمل لبيك إله الخلق غفار الذنوب لبيك ذا النعمة والفضل الحسن لبيك عدد التراب لبيك إن العيش عيش الآخرة كما ورد ذلك عن عدة من الصحابة. وصرح المصنف في الكافي بأن الزيادة حسنة كالتكرار، وصرح الحلبي في مناسكه باستحبابها عندنا . وأما النقص فقال المصنف إنه لا يجوز. وقال ابن الملك في شرح المجمع : إنه مكروه اتفاقاً. والظاهر أنها كراهة تنزيهية لما أن التلبيية إنما هي سنة فإن الشرط إنما هو ذكر الله تعالى فارسياً كان أو عربياً هو المشهور عن أصحابنا وخصوص التلبية سنة فإذا تركها أصلاً ارتكب كراهة تنزيهية فإذا نقص عنها فكذلك بالأولى، فقول المصنف لا يجوز فيه نظر ظاهر، وقول من قال إن التلبية شرط مراده ذكر يقصد به التعظيم لا خصوصها. قيدنا بالزيادة في التلبية لأن الزيادة في الأذان غير مشروعة لأنه للإعلام ولا يحصل بغير المتعارف، وفي التشهد في الصلاة إن كان الأول فليست بمشروعة كتكراره لأنه في وسط الصلاة فيقتصر فيه على الوارد، وإن كان الأخير فهي مشروعة لأنه محل الذكر والثناء
The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: When you have pronounced the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. So beware of rafath, fusooq, jidal, killing game, and pointing to it. And increase in it and do not decrease, i.e., in the talbiyah, and do not decrease from it. The increase is like: Labbayka wa sa'dayka, wal-khayru bi-yadayka, war-raghba'u ilayka, wal-'amal Labbayka, ilaha al-khalqi ghaffaru al-dhunubi Labbayka, dha al-ni'mati wal-fadli al-hasani Labbayka, 'adada al-turabi Labbayka, inna al-'aysha 'ayshu al-akhirah. As has been reported from several companions. And the author stated in al-Kafi that increase is good like repetition. And al-Halabi stated in his Manasik that it is mustahabb according to us. As for decrease, the author said it is not permissible. And Ibn al-Malak said in Sharh al-Majma' that it is makruh by agreement. And the apparent view is that it is makruh tanzihi, because the talbiyah itself is sunnah. For the condition is only the remembrance of Allah, whether in Persian or Arabic — this is the well-known view of our companions — and the specific talbiyah is sunnah. So if one leaves it entirely, he commits a makruh tanzihi. So if he decreases from it, then likewise a fortiori. So the author's statement that it is not permissible is subject to apparent consideration. And the statement of those who said that the talbiyah is a condition — what is meant is remembrance intended for veneration, not its specific wording. We restricted [the discussion] to increase in the talbiyah because increase in the adhan is not legislated, because it is for announcement and it is not achieved with unconventional wording. And in the tashahhud in prayer, if it is the first tashahhud, it is not legislated to increase, like repeating it, because it is in the middle of the prayer, so one limits to what is transmitted. And if it is the last, then it is legislated because it is a place of remembrance and praise.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the talbiyah during ihram. The author first quotes the matn which states: 'And increase in it and do not decrease.' He then explains that the permissible increase includes various phrases reported from the Companions, such as 'Labbayka wa sa'dayka...' The author cites that the author of al-Kafi (i.e., al-Nasafi) considered increase as good (hasanah), and al-Halabi considered it mustahabb (recommended) in our school. As for decreasing the talbiyah, the matn stated it is not permissible, but the commentator clarifies that this is not a prohibition of haram but rather makruh tanzihi. He reasons that the talbiyah itself is sunnah, and its essential requirement is merely remembering Allah in any language, so decreasing the specific wording is not a major sin. He supports this by citing Ibn al-Malak's view that it is makruh by agreement, and he prefers the tanzihi classification. He then distinguishes between increase in talbiyah (which is recommended) and increase in adhan (not allowed) and in tashahhud (allowed only in the last tashahhud). The overall message is that while increasing the talbiyah is a meritorious act, decreasing it is only mildly disliked, not forbidden.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The specific phrases recited by the pilgrim upon entering ihram, beginning with 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' According to this text, the essential requirement is any remembrance of Allah intending veneration, not necessarily the specific wording.
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): Adding extra phrases of praise to the standard talbiyah, which is considered recommended (mustahabb) in the Hanafi school.
النقص (al-naqṣ): Reducing or omitting parts of the standard talbiyah, which is considered makruh tanzihi according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on decreasing the talbiyah according to the preferred view in al-Bahr al-Raiq?
A) Haram
B) Makruh tanzihi
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Increasing the talbiyah is recommended; decreasing it is only mildly disliked (makruh tanzihi), not a sin.

Intention and Talbiyah: The Two Essentials for Ihram
Explaining the role of intention and talbiyah in becoming a muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on the requirement of intention and talbiyah for ihram, explain the analogy to salah, and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-analogy to fasting.

Core Idea
Ihram requires both intention and an initiating action (talbiyah), like prayer requires intention and takbir.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: what exactly initiates the state of ihram? While the matn states that pronouncing the talbiyah with intention brings one into ihram, the commentators explore whether intention alone suffices. By analyzing analogies to salah and sawm, the majority affirms that an external action must accompany the intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's ruling
The matn says that by pronouncing talbiyah with intention, one enters ihram. So both are needed.
2
Analyze Husam al-Din's position
He says one becomes muhrim by intention at the time of talbiyah, not by talbiyah itself, analogous to salah.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position
He says intention alone suffices, analogizing to sawm because both are acts of abstention.
4
Compare the analogies
The majority argues ihram is more like salah because it involves undertaking actions, not just abstention.
5
Understand the final clarification
Later scholars clarified that the essence is intention accompanied by the initiating action, so both expressions are equivalent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فإذا لبيت ناوياً فقد أحرمت) أفاد أنه لا يكون محرماً إلا بهما فإذا أتى بهما فقد دخل في حرمات مخصوصة فهما عين الإحرام شرعاً. وذكر حسام الدين الشهيد أنه يصير شارعاً بالنية لكن عند التلبية لا بالتلبية كما يصير شارعاً في الصلاة بالنية لكن عند التكبير لا بالتكبير ولا يصير شارعاً بالنية وحدها قياساً على الصلاة، وروى عن أبي يوسف أن النية تكفي قياساً على الصوم بجامع أنهما عبادة كف عن المخظورات وقياسنا أولى لأنه التزام أفعال كالصلاة لا مجرد كف بل التزام الكف شرط فكان بالصلاة أشبه . والمراد بالتلبية شرط من خصوصيات النسك، سواء كان تلببة أو ذكر يقصد به التعظيم أو سوق الهدي أو تقليد البان كما ذكره المصنف في المستصفى. وذكر الأسبيجابي أنه لو ساق هدياً قاصداً إلى مكة صار محرماً بالسوق، نوى شئت. لا كذا في الشرح. قال في النهر : فالظرف بمعنى «على» لأن الزيادة إنما يكون بعد الإتيان بها في خلالها كما في السراج . هـ. قوله : (فإذا نقص عنها فكذلك بالأولى قال في النهر فيه نظر ففي الفتح التلبية مرة شرط والزيادة سنة . قال في المحيط : حتى لا يلزمه الإساءة بتركها . ثم قال : إن رفع الصوت بها سنة فإن تركه كان مسيئاً ! فالنقص بالإساءة أولى ! هـ. لكن في الفتح أيضاً : ويستحب في التلبية كلها رفع الصوت من غير أن يبلغ الجهد في ذلك كي لا يضعف، وقد نقله المؤلف عن الحلبي وقد ينازع في دعوى الأولوية على أنه قد ذكر المؤلف فيما سبق أن الإساءة دون الكراهة فليتأمل قوله : (أفاد أنه لا يكون محرماً إلا بهما قال في النهر : ثم إن هذه العبارة لا يستفاد منها إلا أنه يصير محرماً عند النية والتلبية، أما أن الإحرام بهما أو بأحدهما بشرط ذكر الآخر فلا . وذكر الشهيد أنه يصير شارعاً بالنية عند التلبية لا بها كشروعه في الصلاة لكن عند التكبير لا به كذا في الفتح تبعاً للشارح . وبه اندفع ما قد يتوهم من ظاهر كلام المصنف أنه يصير شارعاً بالتلبية بشرط النية مع أن المحكي عن الشهيد عكسه كما مر ومن ثم غير بعض المتأخرين العبارة فقال : إذا نوى ملبياً فقد أحرم لأن الأصل في انعقاد الإحرام . هو النية وأنت خبير بأنه إذا كان المفاد إنما هو صيرورته محرماً فالعبارتان على حد سواء
His statement: '(When you have pronounced the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram)' indicates that one does not become a muhrim except with both of them. So when he performs both, he has entered specific prohibitions, and they are the very essence of ihram legally. Husam al-Din al-Shahid mentioned that one becomes initiator (of ihram) by intention, but at the time of talbiyah, not by the talbiyah itself, just as one becomes initiator in prayer by intention but at the time of takbir, not by the takbir. One does not become initiator by intention alone, by analogy to prayer. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that intention alone suffices, by analogy to fasting, on the basis that both are acts of worship involving abstention from prohibitions. Our analogy is more appropriate because it (ihram) involves undertaking actions like prayer, not mere abstention; rather, the undertaking of abstention is a condition, so it is more similar to prayer. What is meant by talbiyah is a condition of the specific rites, whether it is talbiyah, or remembrance intended for veneration, or driving a hady, or garlanding a sacrificial animal, as mentioned by the author in al-Mustasfa. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that if one drives a hady intending towards Mecca, he becomes a muhrim by the driving, whether he intends something or not. No? That is in the commentary. He said in al-Nahr: 'The adverb (at) means 'on', because increase only occurs after performing it (the talbiyah) within it, as in al-Siraj.' H. His statement: 'So if he decreases from it, then likewise a fortiori.' He said in al-Nahr: 'There is consideration in it. In al-Fath, talbiyah once is a condition, and increase is sunnah.' He said in al-Muhit: 'So that he is not liable for blame for leaving it.' Then he said: 'Raising the voice with it is sunnah; if he leaves it, he is blameworthy. So decreasing (the talbiyah) would be blameworthy a fortiori.' H. But in al-Fath also: 'It is recommended to raise the voice in all of the talbiyah without overexerting so as not to weaken.' The author has transmitted this from al-Halabi, and one may dispute the claim of a fortiori, given that the author mentioned previously that blame is less than dislike, so reflect. His statement: 'It indicates that one does not become a muhrim except with both.' He said in al-Nahr: 'Then this expression only benefits that one becomes a muhrim at the time of intention and talbiyah. As to whether ihram is by both or by one with the condition of mentioning the other, it does not.' And al-Shahid mentioned that one becomes initiator by intention at the time of talbiyah, not by it, as in his initiation in prayer but at the takbir, not by it. That is in al-Fath following the commentator. And with this, what might be understood from the apparent wording of the author that one becomes initiator by talbiyah with intention is repelled, while the report from al-Shahid is the opposite as passed. Hence some later scholars changed the expression and said: 'If he intends while pronouncing the talbiyah, he has entered ihram,' because the basis for contracting ihram is intention. And you are aware that if what is meant is his becoming muhrim, then both expressions are equivalent.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: how exactly does one enter ihram? The matn states that pronouncing the talbiyah with intention accomplishes ihram. The commentator examines whether intention alone suffices or if both are needed. Husam al-Din al-Shahid compares ihram to prayer: in prayer, one enters with intention at the time of takbir, not by the takbir itself. Similarly, for ihram, intention at the time of talbiyah is necessary, but talbiyah is the action that accompanies the intention. Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, analogizes to fasting: just as intention alone suffices for fasting (since it is abstention), so too for ihram. However, the majority (including the author) reject this because ihram involves undertaking specific actions and prohibitions, not mere abstention; thus it is more like prayer. The text further explains that alternatives to talbiyah, such as sending a sacrificial animal (hady) or garlanding it, can also initiate ihram. A side note discusses the issue of decreasing the talbiyah and raising the voice. Ultimately, the relied-upon position is that both intention and talbiyah (or its equivalent) are required for ihram. The later scholars clarified the wording to avoid misunderstanding: 'If he intends while pronouncing the talbiyah, he has entered ihram.' The intention remains the essence, but it must be accompanied by the initiating action.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-iḥrām): The state of being a pilgrim, which is contracted by intending to perform Hajj or Umrah and pronouncing the talbiyah. According to this text, it is the entrance into specific prohibitions.
النية (al-niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform Hajj or Umrah, which is essential for the validity of ihram. This text discusses whether it alone suffices or must accompany talbiyah.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The verbal declaration of the pilgrim, considered the customary action that accompanies the intention to enter ihram. The text discusses its role as a condition or a mere sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is required to enter ihram?
A) Intention alone
B) Talbiyah alone
C) Intention accompanied by talbiyah or equivalent action
D) Reciting the Quran

Key Takeaway
Ihram is contracted by intention combined with an initiating action (talbiyah or equivalent), not by intention alone, analogous to the takbir in prayer.

What Qualifies as Talbiyah? Alternatives and Sunnahs
Expanding on the definition and rulings of talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the actions that qualify as talbiyah (including sending a hady), explain the ruling on decreasing the talbiyah, and state the sunnah of raising the voice.

Core Idea
Talbiyah includes any act of veneration or sending a sacrificial animal, and reciting it once suffices as a condition, while increasing and raising voice are sunnah.

This passage expands on the definition of talbiyah beyond mere words. It explains that driving a hady or garlanding a sacrificial animal can also initiate ihram. It then addresses the minimum requirement: one recitation of talbiyah is a condition, while additional recitations and raising the voice are recommended. A subtle dispute arises about whether decreasing the talbiyah incurs blame.

Guided Path
1
Define talbiyah broadly
Talbiyah can be any remembrance intended for veneration, or sending a hady (sacrificial animal).
Also includes garlanding the animal.
2
Note the alternative of sending a hady
If one drives a sacrificial animal towards Mecca with intention, he becomes muhrim even without verbal talbiyah.
This is the view of al-Asbijabi.
3
Determine the minimum talbiyah
Reciting talbiyah once is a condition for ihram; additional recitations are sunnah.
From al-Fath.
4
Understand the ruling on decreasing
If one intentionally decreases the talbiyah, there is a dispute whether blame attaches. Some argue a fortiori from the case of leaving the sunnah of raising voice.
The author of al-Nahr questions this reasoning.
5
Note the sunnah of raising voice
Raising voice in talbiyah is sunnah, but without straining so as not to weaken oneself.

Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: how exactly does one enter ihram? The matn states that pronouncing the talbiyah with intention accomplishes ihram. The commentator examines whether intention alone suffices or if both are needed. Husam al-Din al-Shahid compares ihram to prayer: in prayer, one enters with intention at the time of takbir, not by the takbir itself. Similarly, for ihram, intention at the time of talbiyah is necessary, but talbiyah is the action that accompanies the intention. Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, analogizes to fasting: just as intention alone suffices for fasting (since it is abstention), so too for ihram. However, the majority (including the author) reject this because ihram involves undertaking specific actions and prohibitions, not mere abstention; thus it is more like prayer. The text further explains that alternatives to talbiyah, such as sending a sacrificial animal (hady) or garlanding it, can also initiate ihram. A side note discusses the issue of decreasing the talbiyah and raising the voice. Ultimately, the relied-upon position is that both intention and talbiyah (or its equivalent) are required for ihram. The later scholars clarified the wording to avoid misunderstanding: 'If he intends while pronouncing the talbiyah, he has entered ihram.' The intention remains the essence, but it must be accompanied by the initiating action.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The verbal declaration of the pilgrim, considered the customary action that accompanies the intention to enter ihram. The text discusses its role as a condition or a mere sunnah.
الهدي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram, which can serve as an alternative to verbal talbiyah for initiating ihram.
الإساءة (al-isā’a): Blameworthy action; in this context, leaving a sunnah may incur isā’a, which is less than karāhah (dislike).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the minimum required to fulfill the condition of talbiyah for ihram?
A) Reciting the full talbiyah three times
B) Reciting the talbiyah once
C) Sending a hady without intention
D) Raising the voice in remembrance

Key Takeaway
Reciting talbiyah once is the minimum condition for ihram; sending a hady or other acts of veneration can substitute, and raising voice is sunnah, not required.

Prohibitions of Ihram: Rafath, Fusooq, and Jidal
Explaining prohibitions of ihram with Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the three prohibitions of ihram and state which one invalidates the Hajj.

Core Idea
Only rafath (sexual intercourse) invalidates Hajj; fusooq and jidal are haram but do not spoil it.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq that clarifies the three prohibitions mentioned in the Quranic verse (2:197) during Hajj. The commentator highlights the strength of the prohibition and distinguishes between their legal consequences. Understanding this distinction is crucial for every pilgrim aspiring to perform a valid Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic evidence and its grammatical force
Read the verse: 'فَلَا رَفَثَ وَلَا فُسُوقَ وَلَا جِدَالَ فِي الْحَجِّ'. Note that the prohibition is in the form of negation, which the commentator states is the strongest form. Analyze how this construction implies a command to avoid these acts completely.
The negation 'لا' combined with the noun indicates a universal prohibition.
2
Define each term: rafath, fusooq, jidal
Rafath is primarily sexual intercourse (based on Quran 2:187) and secondarily obscene talk. Fusooq means all acts of disobedience. Jidal means quarreling. Note the difference between the verse's interpretation by mufassirun and the fuqaha's usage.
Ibn Abbas restricted rafath to obscene talk in the presence of women, but the Hanafi view prioritises intercourse.
3
Distinguish the legal consequence
According to al-Muhit, if a pilgrim commits rafath (sexual intercourse) before standing at Arafah, the Hajj is invalidated. Committing fusooq or jidal does not spoil the pilgrimage, though it is sinful.
The condition is that rafath occurs before Arafah; after that, it does not invalidate.
4
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider real situations: a pilgrim engages in obscene talk (rafath by some opinions) – does it invalidate? According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, only actual intercourse invalidates. A pilgrim argues with a servant (jidal) – this is haram but does not break the pilgrimage.
The severity of fusooq and jidal is greater in ihram than outside, but they are not invalidating.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that among the three prohibitions, only rafath (sexual intercourse) is a nullifier of Hajj, provided it occurs before the standing at Arafah. Fusooq and jidal are forbidden but do not affect the validity.
This is based on the Quranic negation and the definition of rafath from another verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فاتق الرفث والفسوق والجدال للآية الكريمة فلا رفت ولا فسوق ولا جدال في الحج [البقرة : ۱۹۷] وهذا نهي بصيغة النفي وهو آكد ما يكون من النهي كأنه قيل فلا يكونن رفث ولا فسوق ولا جدال في الحج وهذا لأنه لو بقي أخبار التطرق الخلف في كلام الله تعالى لصدور هذه الأشياء من البعض فيكون المراد بالنفي وجوب انتفائها وإنها حقيقة بأن لا تكون كذا في الكافي والرفث الجماع لقوله تعالى أحل لكم ليلة الصيام الرفث إلى نسائكم ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] وقيل الكلام الفاحش لأنه من دواعيه فيحرم كالجماع إلا أن ابن عباس يقول : إنما يكون الكلام الفاحش رفئاً بحضرة النساء حتى روي أنه كان ينشد في إحرامه : وهن يمشين بنا إن يصدق الـطـيــرنــنــك لميســا فقيل له : أترفث وأنت محرم ؟ فقال : إنما الرفث بحضرة النساء . والضمير في «هن» للإبل والهميس صوت نقل أخفافها، وقيل المشي الخفي. ولميس اسم جارية والمعنى نفعل بها ما نريد إن صدق الفال والفسوق المعاصي وهو منهي عنه في الإحرام وغيره إلا أنه في الأحرام أشد كلبس الحرير في الصلاة والتطريب في قراءة القرآن، والجدال الخصومة مع الرفقاء والخدم ،والمكارين ومن ذكر من الشارحين أن المراد به مجادلة المشركين بتقديم وقت الحج وتأخيره أو التفاخر بذكر آبائهم حتى أفضى ذلك إلى القتال فإنه يناسب تفسير الجدال في الآية لا الجدال في كلام الفقهاء فلهذا اقتصرنا على الأول وفي المحيط : إذا رفث يفسد حجه وإذا فسق أو جادل لا لأن الجماع من محظورات الأحرام .اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه مقيد بما قبل الوقوف بعرفة وإلا فلا فساد في الكل.
His statement: 'So beware of rafath, fusooq, and jidal' because of the noble verse: 'So there is no rafath, nor fusooq, nor jidal during Hajj' [Quran 2:197]. And this is a prohibition in the form of negation, which is the strongest form of prohibition, as if it were said: 'Let there be no rafath, nor fusooq, nor jidal during Hajj.' This is because if there remained the possibility of these things occurring from some, there would be discrepancy in Allah's speech; so what is meant by the negation is the obligation of their non-existence and that it is fitting for them not to occur. Thus in al-Kafi. And rafath is sexual intercourse because of Allah's saying: 'It is permitted to you on the night of fasting to approach your wives (rafath)' [Quran 2:187]. And it is said it is obscene talk because it is a cause of intercourse, so it is prohibited like intercourse. Except that Ibn Abbas says: 'Obscene talk is only rafath in the presence of women.' It is narrated that he recited in his ihram: 'And they walk with us, if the bird foretells true, we will do [with] Lamisa...' So he was asked: 'Do you commit rafath while you are muhrim?' He said: 'Rafath is only in the presence of women.' The pronoun 'they' refers to camels, and 'hamis' is the sound of their footsteps, or it is said soft walking. Lamisa is the name of a slave girl, and the meaning is that we will do what we want with her if the omen proves true. And fusooq are acts of disobedience; it is prohibited during ihram and otherwise, but during ihram it is more severe, like wearing silk in prayer and melodious recitation of the Quran. And jidal is argumentation with companions, servants, camel drivers, and others. Some commentators have said that what is meant by it in the verse is disputation with polytheists about advancing or delaying the time of Hajj, or boasting about one's forefathers until that led to fighting; this interpretation suits the exegesis of jidal in the verse, not the jidal in the speech of the fuqaha. So we have confined to the first. And in al-Muhit: 'If he commits rafath, his Hajj is spoiled; if he commits fusooq or jidal, it is not, because sexual intercourse is from the prohibitions of ihram.' End. And it is not hidden that this is restricted to before standing at Arafah; otherwise, there is no spoiling in any of them.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage explains the three major prohibitions during ihram mentioned in the Quranic verse (2:197). The commentator emphasizes the force of the negation form, indicating a strong command to avoid these acts. Rafath is defined primarily as sexual intercourse, based on Quran 2:187. There is a secondary opinion that it includes obscene talk, but it is considered less severe. A narration from Ibn Abbas shows that he considered rafath only in the presence of women, but the commentator does not adopt this as the main view. Fusooq encompasses all sins; it is prohibited always but more strictly during ihram. Jidal is defined as quarreling; some exegetes interpret it as disputing with polytheists, but the fuqaha generally mean arguments with fellow pilgrims. The key ruling, cited from al-Muhit, is that only rafath (sexual intercourse) invalidates the Hajj (if before Arafah); fusooq and jidal, though sinful, do not spoil the pilgrimage. The passage concludes by noting that this invalidation is conditional on occurring before the standing at Arafah.

Key Terms
الرفث (al-rafath): In the context of ihram, it primarily means sexual intercourse, and by extension obscene talk. It is the most severe prohibition and invalidates the hajj before Arafat.
الفسوق (al-fusūq): All acts of disobedience to Allah, which are prohibited in ihram more severely than outside, but do not invalidate the hajj.
الجدال (al-jidāl): Quarreling and arguing with companions, servants, or others. Also interpreted as disputing about the timing of Hajj with polytheists. The text notes that the fuqaha's usage differs from the Quranic interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if a pilgrim commits rafath (sexual intercourse) before standing at Arafah?
A) His Hajj is still valid but he must offer a sacrifice
B) His Hajj is invalidated
C) He must repeat the Hajj the next year
D) He is not liable because it occurred before Arafah

Key Takeaway
Only rafath (sexual intercourse) invalidates the Hajj, and only if committed before the standing at Arafah; fusooq and jidal are haram but do not spoil the pilgrimage.

The Three Major Prohibitions of Ihram
Explains the three major prohibitions of ihram with Quranic and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibitions of ihram, explain their Hanafi definitions, and distinguish which one invalidates the Hajj.

Core Idea
Only rafath (sexual intercourse) invalidates the Hajj; fusooq and jidal are sins but do not spoil it.

The Quran commands pilgrims to avoid rafath, fusooq, and jidal during Hajj. This lesson unpacks each term and explains the legal consequences of committing them. You will see how the Hanafi school derives the strongest prohibition from the verse's negation form and applies it to the rules of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
From the Quranic verse and the text, note the three forbidden acts: rafath, fusooq, and jidal. Understand that these are prohibited from the moment of ihram.
The verse uses a negation form which the Hanafi school interprets as the strongest prohibition.
2
Understand the proof
The proof is Surah Al-Baqarah 2:197. The negation 'la' with a noun indicates absolute avoidance according to Hanafi usul. The author explains that if these acts could occur, the negation would be meaningless, so it mandates their complete absence.
This is a Quranic proof with qati thubut and dalala.
3
Define each term
Rafath primarily means sexual intercourse (Quran 2:187), but also includes obscene speech leading to it. Fusooq is general disobedience, with added severity in ihram. Jidal is argument with companions, servants, or muleteers.
Ibn Abbas restricts obscene speech as rafath only in the presence of women.
4
Learn the consequences
Only rafath (actual intercourse) invalidates the Hajj, and that is restricted to before standing at Arafah. Fusooq and jidal are haram but do not invalidate the Hajj.
The text from Al-Muhit states: 'If he commits rafath, his Hajj is spoiled; if he commits fusooq or jadal, it is not.'
5
Note exceptions and nuances
The invalidation by rafath applies only before Arafah. After Arafah, even rafath does not spoil the Hajj. Also, the prohibitions apply from the moment of ihram, which is established by intention combined with talbiyah.
This nuance prevents misunderstanding about the timing of invalidation.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning three prohibitions during ihram: rafath (sexual activity or obscene speech), fusooq (disobedience), and jidal (argument). The proof is the Quranic verse (2:197) which uses a negation form, which the author explains as the strongest prohibition. The commentary defines each term: rafath primarily means sexual intercourse based on verse 2:187, but also includes obscene speech as a precursor. The view of Ibn Abbas is mentioned that rafath is only obscene speech in the presence of women. Fusooq is general disobedience, but its prohibition is more severe during ihram, analogized to wearing silk in prayer. Jidal is defined as argument with companions, servants, etc., though some commentators interpret it as arguing with polytheists about the timing of Hajj. The passage also clarifies that rafath invalidates the Hajj (if it occurs before standing at Arafah) while fusooq and jidal do not, as per Al-Muhit. The discussion then turns to the issue of talbiyah and intention, concluding that entering ihram is achieved by both intention and utterance, and both expressions are equivalent. The hadith about the one who avoids these acts is cited to emphasize the reward of Hajj free from these sins.

Key Terms
الرفث (ar-rafath): In this text, primarily sexual intercourse, but also obscene speech leading to it.
الفسوق (al-fusooq): Disobedience and sin; prohibited in ihram more severely than outside.
الجدال (al-jidal): Argumentation and quarrelling, especially with companions, servants, or muleteers; not including juristic debate.

Prohibition of Hunting and Wearing Stitched Garments in Ihram
Explains prohibitions of hunting, indirect assistance, and specific clothing while in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibitions of killing game, pointing/indicating, and wearing stitched garments during ihram, and identify the hadith evidence (dalil) for indirect assistance.

Core Idea
Killing game, assisting in it indirectly, and wearing stitched clothes are all haram in ihram.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq details two key sets of prohibitions for a muhrim: actions related to hunting and restrictions on clothing. The author clarifies that the term 'sayd' refers to the hunted animal, and that pointing or indicating game is forbidden based on the hadith of Abu Qatada. The clothing prohibitions are precise, including the definition of the 'ka'b' joint that determines acceptable sock length.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of prohibitions
The passage covers hunting-related prohibitions (killing, pointing, indicating) and clothing-related prohibitions (shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak, socks, dyed garments). Locate each in the text.
2
Analyze the first category: killing and assisting in hunting
Direct killing is prohibited by the Quran. Pointing (isharah) and indicating (dalalah) are prohibited by the hadith. The difference: isharah is for present game, dalalah for absent game.
3
Examine the hadith of Abu Qatada as evidence
The Prophet allowed eating the hunted meat only after confirming no one had pointed or ordered. This indicates that pointing and ordering are prohibited. Some versions include 'helping' and 'indicating'.
4
Analyze the second category: prohibited clothing
List the garments: shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak (qaba'), and socks unless cut below the ka'b joint. Garments dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower are prohibited unless washed and scent-free.
The ka'b in ihram is the joint in the middle of the foot, not the protruding ankle bone.
5
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on qaba'
Wearing a qaba' with arms inserted is haram. Without inserting arms, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Zufar who prohibits absolutely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام والدلالة عليه ولبس القميص والسراويل والعمامة والقلنسوة والقباء والخفين إلا أن لا تجد النعلين فاقطعهما أسفل من الكعبين، والثوب المصبوغ بورس أو زعفران أو عصفر قوله : (وقتل الصيد والإشارة إليه والدلالة عليه أي فاتق إذا أحرمت التعرض لصييد البر. قال المصنف في المستصفى: أريد بالصيد ههنا المصيد إذ لو أريد به المصدر وهو الاصطياد لما صح إسناد القتل إليه وحرمة قتله ثابتة بالقرآن وحرمة الإشارة والدلالة بحديث أبي قتادة كما سيأتي والفرق بين الإشارة والدلالة أن الإشارة تقتضي الحضرة والدلالة تقتضي الغيبة قوله : (بحديث أبي قتادة وهو ما رواه الشيخان أنه عليه السلام قال حين سألوه عن لحم حمار وحش اصطاده أبو قتادة هل منكم من أمره أو أشار إليه؟ قالوا : لا . قال : فكلوا ما بقي من علق حله على عدم الإشارة والأمر كذا في التبيين. وقد أحال المؤلف على ما سيأتي ومحله الجنايات ولم يذكره هناك بل قال : ولحديث أبي قتادة السابق. ثم إنه ليس في الحديث التصريح بالدلالة بل بالأمر والإشارة لكن الحديث في الهداية بلفظ هل أشرتم أو أعنتم أو للتم» فقال: «لا، فقال: إذن فكلوا» لكن قال الحافظ بن حجر في التخريج: متفق عليه بلفظ «هل منكم أحد أمره أن يحمل عليها أو أشار إليها؟ قال: لا. قال فكلوا ما بقي من لحمها والمسلم والنسائي «هل أشرتم أو أعنتم؟ قالوا : لا . قال : فكلوا». اهـ. وسيأتي في الجنابات أن الدلالة التحقت بالقتل استحساناً وسيأتي إيضاحه إن شاء الله تعالى. وزاد في اللباب هنا والإعانة عليه قال شارحه : أي بنوع من أنواع الإعانة والسراويل أعجمية والجمع سراويلات منصرف في أحد استعماليه ويؤنث والقباء المد على وزن فعال بالفتحة والورس صبغ أصفر يؤتى به من اليمن. واختلف في قولهم لا ينفض» فقيل لا يفوح، وقيل لا يتناثر والثاني غير صحيح لأن العبرة للطيب لا للتناثر ألا ترى أنه لو كان ثوباً مصبوغ وغاً له رائحة طيبة ولا يتناثر منه شيء فإن المحرم يمنع منه كذا في المستصفى. والمراد بلبس القباء أن يدخل منكبيه ويديه في كميه لأنه لو لم يدخل يديه في كميه فإنه يجوز عندنا خلافاً لزفر . في غاية البيان والكعب هنا المفصل الذي في وسط القدم عند معقد الشراك فيما روى هشام عن محمد بخلافه في الوضوء فإنه العظم الناتئ أي المرتفع، ولم يعين في الحديث أحدهما لكن لما كان الكعب يطلق عليه، وعلى الثاني حمله عليه احتياطاً. كذا في فتح القدير . أي حمل الكعب في الإحرام على المفصل المذكور لأجل الاحتياط لأن الأحوط فيما كان أكثر وهو قيماً قلنا . فالحاصل أنه يجوز لبس كل شيء في رجله لا يغطي الكعب الذي في وسط القدم، سرموزه كان أو مداساً أو غير ذلك. ويدخل في لبس القميص لبس الزردة والبرنس، وخرج باللبس الارتداء بالقميص ونحوه لأنه ليس بلبس. وذكر الحلبي في مناسكه كذا كشفاً لحمه .
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: and indicating it, and wearing the shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak, and socks unless you do not find sandals, then cut them below the ankles; and the garment dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower. His statement: (and killing game, and pointing to it, and indicating it) meaning: beware, when you enter ihram, of approaching land game. The author said in al-Mustasfa: 'By game here is meant the hunted animal, because if the masdar (hunting) were intended, attributing killing to it would not be correct.' Its prohibition is established by the Quran, and the prohibition of pointing and indicating is by the hadith of Abu Qatadah as will come. The difference between pointing and indicating is that pointing requires presence, indicating requires absence. His statement: (by the hadith of Abu Qatadah) which is what the two Shaykhs narrated that he, peace be upon him, said when they asked him about the meat of a wild ass that Abu Qatadah had hunted: 'Did any of you order him or point to him?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat what remains of its meat.' This indicates the permissibility [of eating] based on the absence of pointing and ordering. So in al-Tabyin. The author referred to what will come, and its place is in al-Jinayat, and he did not mention it there, rather he said: 'and by the previous hadith of Abu Qatadah.' Further, in the hadith there is no explicit mention of indication, but rather ordering and pointing. However, the hadith in al-Hidayah is worded: 'Did you point, help, or indicate?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat.' But al-Hafiz ibn Hajar said in al-Takhrij: It is agreed upon with the wording: 'Did any of you order him to carry her or point to her?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat what remains of her meat.' Muslim and al-Nasa'i: 'Did you point or help?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat.' End. And it will come in al-Jinayat that indication is attached to killing by istihsan, and its clarification will come insha'Allah. And it was added in al-Lubab here: 'and helping him'; its commentator said: 'i.e., by any type of help.' And 'sarawil' is a foreign word, its plural is 'sarawilat', irregular in one of its uses, and it is feminine. 'Qaba' is a cloak on the measure of 'fa'ala' with a fatha. 'Wars' is a yellow dye brought from Yemen. They differed regarding their statement 'does not give off scent': it is said it does not emit fragrance, and it is said it does not scatter; the second is not correct because the criterion is perfume, not scattering. Do you not see that if a garment is dyed and has a good smell and nothing scatters from it, the muhrim is prevented from it. So in al-Mustasfa. What is meant by wearing the qaba' is that he inserts his shoulders and hands into its sleeves, because if he does not insert his hands into its sleeves, then it is permissible according to us, contrary to Zufar. In Ghayat al-Bayan. The 'ka'b' here is the joint in the middle of the foot at the point where the shoestring ties, according to what Hisham narrated from Muhammad, contrary to its meaning in wudu, where it is the protruding bone, i.e., the high one. Neither is specified in the hadith, but since 'ka'b' applies to both, it is interpreted as the first out of precaution. So in Fath al-Qadir, i.e., interpreting 'ka'b' in ihram as the mentioned joint for precaution, because the precautionary measure in what is more common and more valuable... So the conclusion is that it is permissible to wear anything on the foot that does not cover the 'ka'b' which is in the middle of the foot, whether it is a 'sarmuzah' or 'madas' or other. Included in 'wearing a shirt' is wearing a 'zardah' and 'burnus', and excluded by 'wearing' is wrapping oneself in a shirt and the like because it is not wearing. Al-Halabi mentioned in his Manasik: 'so and so, uncovering his flesh.'
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage continues the prohibitions of ihram. It covers two main rulings: first, the prohibition of killing game, as well as pointing to it and indicating its location to others. The author clarifies that the term 'sayd' here means the hunted animal itself, not the act of hunting. The prohibition of killing is from the Quran; the additional prohibitions of pointing and indicating are derived from the hadith of Abu Qatada regarding a wild ass. The passage distinguishes: pointing implies the game is present, while indicating implies it is absent. The hadith is examined in detail, showing that the prohibition extends to ordering, pointing, helping, and indicating. The second part covers prohibited clothing for men in ihram: shirts, trousers, turbans, caps, cloaks, and socks (with the exception of socks if sandals are unavailable, then they must be cut below the ankles). Also prohibited are garments dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower unless they are washed and no scent remains. The commentary explains specific terms: qaba' is worn by inserting arms; wearing it otherwise is permissible. The definition of ka'b is clarified as the joint in the middle of the foot, not the protruding bone (as in wudu), and this is for precaution. The rule is that any footwear covering this joint is prohibited; anything below is permissible. Also, wearing a shirt includes wearing chainmail or a hood, but wrapping oneself in a shirt is not considered 'wearing'.

Key Terms
الصيد (as-sayd): In this context, the hunted animal (the quarry), not the act of hunting.
الإشارة والدلالة (al-isharah wa ad-dalalah): Isharah is pointing to game that is present; dalalah is indicating game that is absent. Both are prohibited as they lead to killing.
القميص (al-qamees): A stitched shirt; wearing it is prohibited for muhrim men.
الكعب (al-ka'b): Here the joint in the middle of the foot where the shoestring ties, not the protruding ankle bone. Used to determine the permissible length of socks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding wearing a qaba' (cloak) for a muhrim?
A) It is absolutely prohibited to wear it.
B) It is prohibited only if the arms are inserted into the sleeves; otherwise it is permissible.
C) It is always permissible.
D) It is prohibited unless it is cut below the ankles.

Key Takeaway
In ihram, the prohibitions on hunting and clothing extend to indirect assistance and specific garments, with careful definitions from the Hanafi school.

Prohibition of Killing Game and Pointing in Ihrām
Explains the prohibition of hunting, pointing, and indicating game for the muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited actions in ihram regarding game and distinguish between ishara and dalala.

Core Idea
A muhrim is prohibited not only from killing game but also from pointing or indicating its location.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks a concise ruling in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn prohibits killing game, pointing to it, and indicating it. The sharh clarifies the linguistic scope of 'sayd' and the difference between two forms of indirect facilitation. Understanding this distinction is essential for the muhrim to avoid major sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
Locate the three actions explicitly prohibited in the matn: killing, pointing (ishara), and indicating (dalala). Note that each has a different legal source.
The prohibition of killing is from the Quran; pointing and indicating are from hadith.
2
Understand the linguistic clarification of 'sayd'
The author notes that 'sayd' in the matn refers to the hunted animal (masid), not the act of hunting. This is because 'killing' is attributed to the animal itself.
This avoids a logical contradiction: you cannot kill the act of hunting.
3
Distinguish ishara from dalala
Ishara is pointing when the game is present; dalala is indicating when it is absent. The distinction affects when the muhrim becomes liable for the prohibition.
Both are haram, but the practical application differs.
4
Note the sources of prohibition
The Quran (5:94-96) prohibits killing game. The hadith of Abu Qatada (to be cited later) prohibits pointing and indicating. Recognize the different evidentiary weights.
The Quranic proof is qat'i al-thubut; the hadith is ahad but accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقتل الصيد والإشارة إليه والدلالة عليه أي فاتق إذا أحرمت التعرض لصييد البر. قال المصنف في المستصفى: أريد بالصيد ههنا المصيد إذ لو أريد به المصدر وهو الاصطياد لما صح إسناد القتل إليه وحرمة قتله ثابتة بالقرآن وحرمة الإشارة والدلالة بحديث أبي قتادة كما سيأتي والفرق بين الإشارة والدلالة أن الإشارة تقتضي الحضرة والدلالة تقتضي الغيبة
His saying: (and killing game and pointing to it and indicating it) i.e. beware, when you enter ihram, of approaching land game. The author said in al-Mustasfa: what is meant by 'sayed' here is the hunted animal, because if what was meant was the verbal noun which is hunting, then attributing murder to it would not be correct. The prohibition of killing it is established by the Quran, and the prohibition of pointing and indicating is by the hadith of Abu Qatada as will come. The difference between pointing and indicating is that pointing requires presence and indicating requires absence.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the prohibition of killing game in ihram. The author clarifies the term 'sayed' in the matn: it refers to the animal (masid), not the act of hunting, because attributing 'killing' to the act would be incorrect. Killing game is prohibited by the Quran; pointing to or indicating game is prohibited by the hadith of Abu Qatada, which will be detailed later. The author distinguishes pointing (ishara) from indicating (dalala): pointing implies the game is present, while indicating implies it is absent. This distinction has practical implications for when the muhrim is liable.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game animal of the land, permissible outside ihram.
إشارة (ishara): Pointing to the game when it is present.
دلالة (dalala): Indicating the location of game when it is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Ishara is for a close target; dalala is for a distant target.
B) 'Ishara is pointing when the game is present; dalala is indicating when the game is absent.
C) 'Ishara is verbal; dalala is non-verbal.
D) 'Ishara is for land game; dalala is for sea game.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must avoid killing, pointing to, or indicating land game; indirect facilitation is also haram.

Prohibited Garments in Ihrām: The List and Exceptions
Lists prohibited garments and exceptions for the muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven types of garments prohibited in ihram and identify the conditions under which khuffayn and dyed garments are permitted.

Core Idea
A muhrim must avoid sewn garments and scented dyes; only khuffayn can be worn if no sandals exist, and only scentless dyed clothes are allowed.

When entering the sacred state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, certain everyday garments become forbidden. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists them clearly: the shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak, leather socks, and any garment dyed with fragrant substances like saffron or wars. However, there are two important exceptions: leather socks can be worn if sandals are unavailable (after cutting them below the ankles), and dyed garments are permitted if they have been washed and no longer emit fragrance. Understanding these distinctions is essential for performing the pilgrimage correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited garments
From the text, enumerate the seven types of garments that the muhrim must not wear: qamees, sarawil, imama, qalansuwa, qaba, khuffayn, and thob masbug (dyed garment). Note the foreign origins of some terms.
The prohibition is general; each item is specifically mentioned in hadith.
2
Recognize the exception for khuffayn
If a muhrim cannot find sandals (na'layn), he may wear khuffayn after cutting them below the ankles. This makes them resemble sandals. The condition is necessity.
Cutting below the ankles is a symbolic removal of the sewn covering.
3
Understand the rule for dyed garments
Garments dyed with fragrant plants like wars, saffron (zafaran), or safflower (usfur) are prohibited. But if the garment is washed (ghaseelan) and does not release scent (la yunfad), it becomes permissible.
The key is the scent, not the dye itself. Even if no particles scatter, if it smells, it is prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولبس القميص والسراويل والعمامة والقلنسوة والقباء والخفين إلا أن لا تجد النعلين فاقطعهما أسفل من الكعبين، والثوب المصبوغ بورس أو زعفران أو عصفر إلا أن يكون غسيلاً لا ينفض) كما دل عليه حديث الصحيحين والسراويل أعجمية والجمع سراويلات منصرف في أحد استعماليه ويؤنث والقباء المد على وزن فعال بالفتحة والورس صبغ أصفر يؤتى به من اليمن. واختلف في قولهم لا ينفض» فقيل لا يفوح، وقيل لا يتناثر والثاني غير صحيح لأن العبرة للطيب لا للتناثر ألا ترى أنه لو كان ثوباً مصبوغ وغاً له رائحة طيبة ولا يتناثر منه شيء فإن المحرم يمنع منه كذا في المستصفى
His saying: (And wearing the shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak, and khuffayn (leather socks) unless you do not find sandals, then cut them below the ankles, and the garment dyed with leaves, safflower, or safflower except if it is washed and does not release scent)—as indicated by the hadith of the Two Sahihs. 'Sarawil' (trousers) is a foreign word, its plural is 'sarawilat', it is declinable in one usage and feminine. 'Qaba' (cloak) is a Persian word on the measure of 'fial' with fatha. 'Wars' is a yellow dye brought from Yemen. There is disagreement on the phrase 'does not release scent': some say it means it does not give off fragrance, others say it does not scatter (lint). The second is not correct because the consideration is for the scent, not for scattering. Do you not see that if there is a dyed garment that has a pleasant smell and nothing scatters from it, the muhrim is prevented from wearing it—this in al-Mustasfa.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates the garments prohibited in ihram, beginning with the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The muhrim must not wear the qamees (shirt), sarawil (trousers), imama (turban), qalansuwa (cap), qaba (cloak), khuffayn (leather socks), and any garment dyed with saffron, safflower, or wars. Exceptions: if one cannot find sandals, he may wear khuffayn after cutting them below the ankles. A dyed garment is permitted if it has been washed and no longer gives off scent. The commentator explains the meanings of foreign words and the debate on 'does not release scent': the correct opinion is that it means does not emit fragrance, not that it does not scatter particles. The prohibition is due to the scent.

Key Terms
القميص (al-qamees): A sewn shirt worn on the upper body.
السراويل (al-sarawil): Trousers, prohibited in ihram.
ورس (wars): A yellow plant dye from Yemen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can a muhrim wear khuffayn?
A) He may wear them without cutting.
B) He may wear them if he does not have sandals and cuts them below the ankles.
C) He may wear them if he is sick.
D) He may not wear them under any condition.

Key Takeaway
The muhrim must avoid sewn garments and scented dyes; only worn-out leather socks become permissible if no sandals exist, and only washed, scentless dyed clothes are allowed.
