Hadith of Abu Qatada as Proof for Prohibition of Pointing
Cites and analyzes the hadith of Abu Qatada for prohibition of pointing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim pointing to game, cite the hadith of Abu Qatada as proof, and explain the wajh al-dalalah.

Core Idea
Pointing to game while in ihram is as prohibited as killing it.

The prohibition of hunting while in ihram extends beyond direct killing. Even a gesture or a word directing a hunter towards game can invalidate the meat. This lesson examines the key hadith evidence that establishes this ruling and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what specific actions are being ruled upon (pointing, ordering, helping) and the legal consequence (meat becomes unlawful, act is haram).
Focus on the muhrim as the actor.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Abu Qatada is cited from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. Note the different wordings and the common core: the Prophet conditioned permission on the absence of pointing, ordering, or helping.
Ibn Hajar's clarification on the wording is useful for precision.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith implies prohibition: the Prophet only allowed eating because no such actions occurred; conversely, if they had occurred, the meat would be forbidden.
This is a mafhum al-mukhalafa (inference from the condition).
4
Note the extension by istihsan
The text states that indicating (dalala) is annexed to killing by istihsan. Also, helping (i'ana) is included. Recognize that the ruling is not limited to the literal words of the hadith but is expanded analogically.
Istihsan here operates to treat indirect causation as equivalent to direct action.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Test the ruling on cases like lending a knife, pointing with a hand, or giving directions. Confirm that any such assistance renders the game unlawful for the muhrim.
Use the modern mapping to reinforce: electronic pointing (GPS) also falls under the prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبحديث أبي قتادة وهو ما رواه الشيخان أنه عليه السلام قال حين سألوه عن لحم حمار وحش اصطاده أبو قتادة هل منكم من أمره أو أشار إليه؟ قالوا : لا . قال : فكلوا ما بقي من علق حله على عدم الإشارة والأمر كذا في التبيين. وقد أحال المؤلف على ما سيأتي ومحله الجنايات ولم يذكره هناك بل قال : ولحديث أبي قتادة السابق. ثم إنه ليس في الحديث التصريح بالدلالة بل بالأمر والإشارة لكن الحديث في الهداية بلفظ هل أشرتم أو أعنتم أو للتم» فقال: «لا، فقال: إذن فكلوا» لكن قال الحافظ بن حجر في التخريج: متفق عليه بلفظ «هل منكم أحد أمره أن يحمل عليها أو أشار إليها؟ قال: لا. قال فكلوا ما بقي من لحمها والمسلم والنسائي «هل أشرتم أو أعنتم؟ قالوا : لا . قال : فكلوا». اهـ. وسيأتي في الجنابات أن الدلالة التحقت بالقتل استحساناً وسيأتي إيضاحه إن شاء الله تعالى. وزاد في اللباب هنا والإعانة عليه قال شارحه : أي بنوع من أنواع الإعانة كإعارة سكين أو مناولة رمح أو سوط ا هـ
And by the hadith of Abu Qatada, which is what the Two Sheikhs narrated: that he عليه السلام said when they asked him about the meat of a wild donkey that Abu Qatada hunted, 'Is there anyone among you who ordered him or pointed to him?' They said, 'No.' He said, 'Then eat what remains of its meat.' He made its permissibility conditional on the absence of pointing and ordering. This is in al-Tabyeen. The author referred to what will come later, and its place is in the chapters on penalties, but he did not mention it there; rather he said, 'And by the hadith of Abu Qatada that preceded.' Then, there is no explicit mention in the hadith of 'dalala' (indicating), rather it mentions ordering and pointing. However, in al-Hidayah the wording is: 'Did you point or help or call?' They said, 'No.' He said, 'Then eat.' But al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in al-Takhrij: It is agreed upon with the wording: 'Is there anyone among you who ordered him to carry it or pointed to it?' They said, 'No.' He said, 'Then eat what remains of its meat.' Muslim and al-Nasa'i: 'Did you point or help?' They said, 'No.' He said, 'Then eat.' End. And it will come in the chapters on penalties that indicating (dalala) is treated like killing by istihsan, and its clarification will come, God willing. And in al-Lubab, there is an addition: 'and helping him.' The commentator said: i.e., by any type of assistance, like lending a knife or handing over a spear or a whip, etc.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage provides the dalil for the prohibition of pointing and indicating game in ihram. The hadith of Abu Qatada is cited from the Two Sahihs. The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم conditionally permitted eating the game only when no one had ordered, pointed, or helped the hunter. This establishes that any such action by a muhrim makes the meat unlawful for him and possibly for everyone. The author notes that in al-Hidayah the wording includes 'a'antum' (helped), which further extends the prohibition to aiding. Ibn Hajar clarifies the wording. The author adds that indicating (dalala) is annexed to killing by istihsan, meaning it carries the same ruling. The passage also includes a quote from al-Lubab extending the prohibition to any form of assistance, such as lending tools.

Key Terms
إعانة (i'ana): Assistance in hunting, e.g., lending tools.
الدلالة (al-dalala): Indicating the location of game when absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Abu Qatada, what condition made the game permissible for the muhrim?
A) The game was killed by a non-muhrim.
B) No muhrim ordered, pointed, or helped in the hunt.
C) The muhrim did not eat the game himself.
D) The game was a sea creature.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Abu Qatada establishes that any intentional act by a muhrim to facilitate hunting, whether pointing, ordering, indicating, or helping, is haram and renders the game unlawful.

Garments Prohibited in Ihram: Definition and Application to Gloves and Cut Khuff
Defines what constitutes 'wearing', rulings on gloves, and cutting khuffayn when sandals available.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for prohibited garments in ihram and apply it to gloves and cut khuff, identifying the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Anything sewn to fit the body is prohibited in ihram; gloves are haram for men, cut khuff permissible only when sandals unavailable.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refines the definition of 'wearing' prohibited garments in ihram. It establishes a general criterion and then applies it to two contested items: gloves (quffazayn) and khuff cut below the ankles. By studying this text, you will learn how Hanafi jurists derive specific rulings from a broad principle and resolve intra-madhhab differences through tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Extract the criterion
Identify the definition of prohibited 'wearing' (اللبس) in the text: anything made to fit the body or a limb, held by sewing or sticking, that stays on by itself when worn.
This is a conceptual definition, not a simple list.
2
Apply the criterion to gloves
Determine whether gloves (quffazayn) fall under this definition. The text confirms they do because they are sewn to fit the hands. Then note the dispute: Al-Farisi permitted them with dislike; the majority (Sindi, al-Bada'i') prohibit them for men.
The key distinction is between 'wearing' (sewn) and 'covering' (e.g., with a cloth).
3
Analyse the daliil and tarjih on gloves
Follow the reasoning: the Prophet's prohibition of gloves is taken as absolute for men, and reconciled with women's permission. The majority interpret it as haram for men via qiyas to other sewn garments.
The qiyas panel in the source analogises gloves to a qamees (shirt).
4
Apply the criterion to cut khuff
Examine the ruling on khuff cut below the ankles when sandals are available. The text notes a narration from Abu Hanifa that it is not allowed, but the relied-upon view is that cutting is only obligatory when no sandals are found; otherwise, it is permissible but disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it contradicts the sunnah.
Imam al-Tabari reported a stricter view, but it is not the madhhab.
5
Identify the mufta bihi positions
Consolidate: for men, gloves are haram; for women, permissible (though better not). Wearing cut khuff when sandals exist is makruh tanzihan, not haram.
These are the operative rulings for fatwa according to later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن ضابطه لبس كل شيء معمول على قدر البدن أو بعضه بحيث يحيط به بخياطة أو تلزيق بعضه ببعض أو غيرهما ويستمسك عليه بنفس لبس مثله إلا المكعب. ويدخل في الخفين الجوربان ولم أر من صرح بما إذا كان قادراً على النعلين فهل له أن يقطع الخفين أسفل من الكعبين، والظاهر من الحديث وكلامهم أنه لا يجوز بمعنى لا يحل لما فيه من إتلاف ماله لغير ضرورة . قوله : ( كل شيء معمول على قدر البدن أو بعضه) يدخل فيه القفازان وهما ما يلبس في اليدين . قال في شرح اللباب : وكذا أي يحرم لبس المحرم القفازين لما نقل عز الدين بن جماعة من أنه يحرم عليه لبس القفازين في يديه عند الأئمة الأربعة. وقال الفارسي : ويلبس المحرم القفازين ولعله محمول على جوازه مع الكراهة في حق الرجل فإن المرأة ليست ممنوعة عن لبسهما وإن كان الأولى لها أن لا تلبسهما لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام ولا تلبس القفازين» جمعاً بين الدلائل . كذا ذكروه لكن ليس فيه ما يدل على أن الرجل ممنوع من تغطية يديه اللهم إلا إن يقال هو نوع من لبس المخيط والله أعلم اهـ . وقال السندي في المنسك الكبير : وما ذكره الفارسي من جواز لبسهما خلاف كلمة الأصحاب لأنهم ذكروا جواز لبسهما فيما يختص بالمرأة. قال في البدائع : لأن لبس القفازين لبس لا تغطية وأنها غير ممنوعة عن ذلك وقوله عليه السلام) ولا تلبس القفازين هي : ندب ، حملناه عليه جمعاً بين الدلائل بقدر الإمكان ا هـ . وعلى هذا فقول السندي في منسكه المتوسط المسمى باللباب «أنه يباح له تغطية يديه» أراد به تغطيتهما بنحو منديل لأن التغطية غير اللبس فلا يدخل فيه لبس القفازين . قوله : (ولم أر من صرح الخ) قال في النهر في لباب المناسك : ولو وجد النعلين بعد لبسهما أي لبس الخفين المقطوعين يجوز له الاستدامة على ذلك يجوز لبس المقطوع مع وجود النعلين ا هـ . قال شارحه : لكنه لا ينافي الكراهة المرتبة على مخالفة السنة . وقال قبله ما حاصله : حكى الطبري عن حنيفة أنه إذا كان قادراً على النعلين لا يجوز له لبس الخفين ولو قطعهما لكن هذا خلاف المذهب ولعله رواية عنه . والظاهر أن لبسهما حينئذ مخالف للسنة فيكره وتحصل به الإساءة. وقال ابن الهمام: اختلف المشايخ في جوازه ومقتضى النص أنه مقيد بما إذا لم يجد نعلين. أقول: الظاهر أن قيد عدم وجدان النعلين لوجوب قطع الخفين بخلاف ما إذا وجدا فإنه لا يجب القطع حينئذ لما فيه
That the criterion is wearing every thing made according to the size of the body or part of it such that it encompasses it by sewing or sticking some parts together or other means, and it is held by itself by wearing like it, except the cube (?). And included in khuffayn are jorab (socks). And I have not seen anyone explicitly state when he is able to get sandals, is it permissible for him to cut the khuffayn below the ankles? The apparent from the hadith and their statements is that it is not permissible in the sense that it is not lawful because it involves destroying his property without necessity. His saying: (every thing made according to the size of the body or part of it) includes quffazayn (gloves), which are worn on the hands. It is said in Sharh al-Lubab: likewise, it is prohibited for the muhrim to wear gloves, as transmitted from Izz al-Din ibn Jama'a that it is prohibited for him to wear gloves on his hands according to the four Imams. Al-Farisi said: and the muhrim may wear gloves, and perhaps it is carried on permissibility with dislike in the case of a man, whereas a woman is not prevented from wearing them, although it is better for her not to wear them due to his saying عليه السلام: 'Do not wear gloves,' reconciling the evidences. So they mentioned this, but there is nothing in it to indicate that a man is prevented from covering his hands, unless it is said that it is a type of wearing stitched clothes, and Allah knows best. And al-Sindi said in al-Mansak al-Kabir: what al-Farisi mentioned about permissibility is contrary to the word of the companions because they mentioned permissibility of wearing them (gloves) only for women. It is said in al-Bada'i': because wearing gloves is wearing, not covering, and she (the woman) is not prevented from that. And his saying عليه السلام: 'Do not wear gloves' is interpreted as recommendation (nadb), and we have carried it upon that reconciling the evidences as much as possible. According to this, the statement of al-Sindi in his medium booklet called al-Lubab that 'it is permissible for him to cover his hands' meant covering them with something like a handkerchief, because covering is not wearing, so wearing gloves is not included. His saying: (And I have not seen anyone explicitly state...) He said in al-Nahr in Lubab al-Manasik: and if he finds sandals after wearing them, i.e., after wearing the cut khuffayn, it is permissible for him to continue wearing them; it is permissible to wear the cut khuffayn even if sandals are present. Its commentator said: but this does not negate the dislike that follows from opposing the Sunnah. And he said before that: al-Tabari narrated from Abu Hanifa that if he is able to get sandals, it is not permissible for him to wear khuffayn even if he cuts them, but this is contrary to the madhhab and perhaps it is a narration from him. The apparent is that wearing them then is contrary to the Sunnah, thus it is disliked and involves doing wrong. Ibn al-Humam said: the mashayikh differed on its permissibility, but the implication of the text is that it is conditioned on not finding sandals. I say: the apparent is that the condition of not finding sandals is for the obligation of cutting the khuffayn; if sandals are found, then cutting is not obligatory because of what is involved.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage defines the general rule for prohibited garments in ihram: anything sewn or tailored to fit the body or a limb. It clarifies that gloves (quffazayn) are included and discusses the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars. For men, gloves are prohibited because they are a sewn garment; for women, they are permitted but recommended not to wear. The ruling on khuffayn when sandals are available is also debated: the preferred view is that cutting them below the ankles is only required if no sandals exist; if sandals exist, one may wear cut khuffayn with dislike. Eating the meat after the end of the page was not needed.

Key Terms
القفازان (al-quffazayn): Gloves worn on the hands.
الخف المقطوع (al-khuff al-maqtu'): Khuff cut below the ankles, permissible when no sandals are available.
الضابط (al-dabit): The criterion: anything sewn to fit the body or limb, held by itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a man wearing gloves (quffazayn) in ihram according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) Permissible.
B) Disliked (makruh tanzihan).
C) Haram.
D) Obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines prohibited garments in ihram as anything sewn to fit the body; gloves are haram for men, and cut khuff is only wajib when sandals are unavailable.

Covering the Face in Ihrām: Living vs. Deceased Muhrim
Ruling on covering face and head, with ḥadīth and discussion on deceased muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on covering the face of a living vs. deceased muhrim, explain the Hanafi proof, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The living muhrim must not cover his face; the deceased muhrim must be covered like any other corpse.

This lesson examines the prohibition of covering the face and head during ihram, a key ruling that differs between the Hanafi and Shafi'ī schools. The source of dispute lies in how to interpret the famous hadith of the Bedouin who died in ihram. While the literal wording seems to apply to both living and deceased, the Hanafis use legal reasoning (ta'līl) to restrict it to the living, and the Shāfi'īs apply it only to the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is covering the face and head by a muhrim. What is the Hanafi ruling for the living? For the deceased?
Living: haram. Deceased: wajib to cover as per general burial.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalīl
The ḥadīth of the Bedouin: 'Do not cover his head nor his face, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection in the state of talbiya.' How is it used as evidence?
It is a ḥadīth of the Prophet ﷺ.
3
Analyze the Hanafi method: ta'līl vs. manṭūq
The Hanafis derive the prohibition for the living from the legal cause (ta'līl) that he will be resurrected in iḥrām. They do not apply the literal wording to the deceased.
This is a critical refinement of the text.
4
Understand the Shāfi'ī position
Shāfi'īs apply the ḥadīth literally to the deceased but allow covering for the living.
They permit covering with something not touching the face.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter with the ḥadīth on cessation of deeds, arguing that iḥrām ends at death, so the deceased is like any other corpse.
This reconciles the two evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وستر الوجه والرأس أي واجتنب تغطيتهما لحديث الأعرابي الذي وقصته ناقته «لا تخمروا رأسه ولا وجهه فإنه يبعث يوم القيامة ملبياً». واعلم أن أئمتنا استدلوا بهذا الحديث على حرمة تغطية الوجه على المحرم الحي المفهوم من التعليل ولم يعملوا بمنطوقه في حق الميت المحرم فإن حكمه عندنا كسائر الأموات في تغطية الوجه والرأس، والشافعية عملوا به فيما إذا مات المحرم ولم يعملوا به في حالة الحياة. وأجاب في غاية البيان عن بأنهم إنما لم يعملوا به في الموت لأنه معارض بحديث إذا مات ابن آدم انقطع عمله إلا من ثلاث والإحرام عمل فهو منقطع فيغطي العضوان ولهذا لا يبنى المأمور بالحج على إحرام الميت اتفاقاً، وهو يدل على انقطاعه بالموت والأعرابي مخصوص من ذلك بأخبار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم
His saying: (And covering the face and head) i.e., avoid covering them due to the hadith of the Bedouin whose camel broke his neck: 'Do not cover his head nor his face, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection in the state of talbiya.' Know that our Imams used this hadith as evidence for the prohibition of covering the face for the living muhrim, understanding from the legal cause (ta'lil), and they did not act upon its explicit wording regarding the deceased muhrim, because according to us his ruling is like that of other deceased in terms of covering the face and head. The Shafi'is acted upon it regarding the deceased muhrim and did not act upon it in the state of life. And it was answered in Ghayat al-Bayan that they (Shafi'is) did not act upon it in death because it is opposed by the hadith 'When a human dies, his deeds cease except for three' and ihram is an act, so it ceases, so both parts (face and head) are covered. Hence the case of the one ordered to perform hajj is not built upon the ihram of the deceased by agreement, and this indicates that it ceases with death, and the Bedouin is specific from that by the report of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of covering the face and head for the muhrim. The proof is the hadith of the Bedouin who died in ihram, where the Prophet ordered not to cover his head and face. The Hanafis derive from this the prohibition for a living muhrim to cover his face (and head) by understanding the legal cause (ta'lil) that he will be resurrected in ihram, thus the living must remain uncovered. However, the Hanafis apply the general rule for the deceased muhrim: they cover his face and head like other deceased, because the hadith is specific to that Bedouin. The Shafi'is take the opposite: they follow the hadith literally for the deceased (do not cover) but apply a different reasoning for the living. The Hanafi response uses the hadith on cessation of deeds to argue that ihram ends with death, so the deceased muhrim is treated as an ordinary deceased person. Thus there is a clear ikhtilaf between the madhhabs.

Key Terms
ستر الوجه (satr al-wajh): Covering the face, prohibited for living muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on covering the face of a deceased muhrim?
A) It is prohibited.
B) It is obligatory or Sunnah as for any Muslim deceased.
C) It is permissible.
D) It is disliked.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits covering the face for a living muhrim but requires covering for a deceased muhrim, reconciling conflicting hadiths via legal cause and general principles.

Definition of Sewn Garment and Ruling on Gloves (Qafazan)
Definition of sewn garment with examples, specifically ruling on gloves for men and women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a sewn garment (makhit) and apply it to determine the ruling on wearing gloves (qafazan) for men and women in ihram.

Core Idea
A sewn garment is anything tailored to fit the body; gloves are included, so men in ihram cannot wear them.

The concept of 'sewn garment' (makhit) is central to the prohibitions of ihram. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the precise definition and extends it to gloves (qafazan), a common point of confusion. The text also resolves an intra-Hanafi disagreement, establishing the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of makhit
Identify the key components: 'everything made according to the measure of the body or part of it, such that it surrounds it with sewing or attaching, and it clings to itself when worn.' Note the exception: the 'cube' (likely a specific garment).
The definition is broad: any tailored garment, not just those with stitching.
2
Apply definition to qafazan
Recognize that qafazan (gloves) are made to fit the hands, thus they fall under makhit. This triggers the prohibition for men.
The author explicitly includes qafazan in the definition.
3
Distinguish covering from wearing
Understand that covering hands with a loose cloth (e.g., handkerchief) is not considered 'wearing' a sewn garment. The hadith prohibition applies specifically to wearing qafazan, not to covering per se.
Al-Sindi clarifies this distinction.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute and tarjih
Al-Farisi permitted qafazan for men with karahah, but the majority (including al-Sindi and al-Bada'i) prohibit. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is prohibition for men.
For women, the ruling is permissible but better avoided, based on interpreting the hadith as nadb (recommendation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن ضابطه لبس كل شيء معمول على قدر البدن أو بعضه بحيث يحيط به بخياطة أو تلزيق بعضه ببعض أو غيرهما ويستمسك عليه بنفس لبس مثله إلا المكعب. ويدخل في الخفين الجوربان ولم أر من صرح بما إذا كان قادراً على النعلين فهل له أن يقطع الخفين أسفل من الكعبين، والظاهر من الحديث وكلامهم أنه لا يجوز بمعنى لا يحل لما فيه من إتلاف ماله لغير ضرورة قوله : ( كل شيء معمول على قدر البدن أو بعضه) يدخل فيه القفازان وهما ما يلبس في اليدين . قال في شرح اللباب : وكذا أي يحرم لبس المحرم القفازين لما نقل عز الدين بن جماعة من أنه يحرم عليه لبس القفازين في يديه عند الأئمة الأربعة. وقال الفارسي : ويلبس المحرم القفازين ولعله محمول على جوازه مع الكراهة في حق الرجل فإن المرأة ليست ممنوعة عن لبسهما وإن كان الأولى لها أن لا تلبسهما لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام ولا تلبس القفازين» جمعاً بين الدلائل . كذا ذكروه لكن ليس فيه ما يدل على أن الرجل ممنوع من تغطية يديه اللهم إلا إن يقال هو نوع من لبس المخيط والله أعلم اهـ . وقال السندي في المنسك الكبير : وما ذكره الفارسي من جواز لبسهما خلاف كلمة الأصحاب لأنهم ذكروا جواز لبسهما فيما يختص بالمرأة. قال في البدائع : لأن لبس القفازين لبس لا تغطية وأنها غير ممنوعة عن ذلك وقوله عليه السلام) ولا تلبس القفازين هي : ندب ، حملناه عليه جمعاً بين الدلائل بقدر الإمكان ا هـ . وعلى هذا فقول السندي في منسكه المتوسط المسمى باللباب «أنه يباح له تغطية يديه» أراد به تغطيتهما بنحو منديل لأن التغطية غير اللبس فلا يدخل فيه لبس القفازين .
That its definition is wearing everything made according to the measure of the body or part of it such that it surrounds it with sewing or attaching some of it to some or other than that and it clings to him by itself like its wearing except the cube. And included in the khuff are the socks; and I have not seen anyone explicitly state regarding when he is able to wear sandals, whether he may cut the khuff below the ankles, and the apparent from the hadith and their statements is that it is not permissible in the sense of not being allowed because of the destruction of his wealth without necessity. His statement: (Everything made according to the measure of the body or part of it) includes the qafazan, which are what are worn on the hands. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: Likewise, it is haram for the muhrim to wear qafazan because it is narrated from 'Izz al-Din ibn Jama'ah that it is haram for him to wear qafazan on his hands according to the four imams. And al-Farisi said: The muhrim may wear qafazan, and perhaps it is carried on permissibility with karahah in the case of a man, for the woman is not prevented from wearing them, although it is better for her not to wear them due to his statement, peace be upon him, 'And do not wear qafazan' as a combination of evidences. Thus they mentioned it, but there is nothing in it indicating that the man is prevented from covering his hands, unless it is said that it is a type of wearing sewn garment, and Allah knows best. End. And al-Sindi said in al-Mansak al-Kabir: What al-Farisi mentioned of permissibility of wearing them is contrary to the statement of the companions because they mentioned permissibility of wearing them in what is specific to women. He said in al-Bada'i: Because wearing qafazan is wearing, not covering, and she is not prevented from that, and his statement 'and do not wear qafazan' is a recommendation, we carried it on that combining between evidences as much as possible. End. And upon this, the statement of al-Sindi in his intermediate manasik called al-Lubab 'that it is permissible for him to cover his hands' means covering them with something like a handkerchief because covering is not wearing, so wearing qafazan is not included.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage defines what constitutes a sewn garment (makhit) for the muhrim: anything made to fit the body or its part, encircling it by sewing or attaching, and it stays on by itself. An exception is the 'cube' (possibly a certain type of garment). The definition includes khuff (leather socks) and qafazan (gloves). The commentator notes a gap in scholarly discussion about cutting khuff below the ankles when one can afford sandals, suggesting it is not allowed due to wasting wealth. On qafazan, there is a difference of opinion: the stronger Hanafi position is that men are prohibited from wearing them like any sewn garment, while women may wear them but it is better not to, based on combining the hadith 'do not wear qafazan' as a recommendation (nadb). Al-Sindi clarifies that 'covering hands' with a cloth is not the same as wearing qafazan.

Key Terms
مخيط (makhit): Sewn garment that fits the body, prohibited for men in ihram.
قفازان (qafazan): Gloves that cover the hands, considered a sewn garment.
ندب (nadb): Recommended act, at the level of sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a man wearing qafazan (gloves) while in ihram?
A) Permissible without karahah.
B) Permissible but makruh.
C) Haram.
D) Wajib to wear.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of sewn garment (makhit) includes gloves (qafazan), so men in ihram are prohibited from wearing them, while women may do so but better not.

Wearing Cut Khuff When Sandals Are Available
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the permissibility of wearing cut khuff when sandals are available

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing cut khuff when sandals are available and explain why it is makruh despite being permissible.

Core Idea
Cutting khuff permits them, but wearing them when sandals are available is still makruh due to abandoning the sunnah.

When a muhrim has sandals available, the sunnah is to wear them. But what if he already has cut his khuff? The Hanafi school debates whether he may continue wearing them. This lesson examines the relied-upon position and the reasoning behind the karahah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah
State the Hanafi position: wearing cut khuff when sandals are available is permissible but with karahah (dislike).
The karahah is due to abandoning the sunnah, not because the act is sinful.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A narration from Abu Hanifah (via al-Tabari) holds it impermissible. Recognize this as a rare, non-reliant view.
The majority of mashayikh follow the permissibility view.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
The asl: wearing khuff when no sandals are found – permissible after cutting. The far': wearing them when sandals are available. The illa: necessity (dharurah) – present in asl, absent in far'.
Without necessity, cutting is not obligatory (due to waste), but wearing cut khuff remains permissible.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a muhrim wears cut khuff despite having sandals, his ihram is valid but he commits a makruh act (not a sin unless it is makruh tahrimi, but here it is tanzihi).
Some scholars classified it as makruh tahrimi; but the relied-upon is tanzihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa: permissible with karahah, following the majority of later Hanafi authorities.
Ibn al-Humam and al-Nahr support this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم أر من صرح الخ) قال في النهر في لباب المناسك : ولو وجد النعلين بعد لبسهما أي لبس الخفين المقطوعين يجوز له الاستدامة على ذلك يجوز لبس المقطوع مع وجود النعلين ا هـ . قال شارحه : لكنه لا ينافي الكراهة المرتبة على مخالفة السنة . وقال قبله ما حاصله : حكى الطبري عن حنيفة أنه إذا كان قادراً على النعلين لا يجوز له لبس الخفين ولو قطعهما لكن هذا خلاف المذهب ولعله رواية عنه . والظاهر أن لبسهما حينئذ مخالف للسنة فيكره وتحصل به الإساءة. وقال ابن الهمام: اختلف المشايخ في جوازه ومقتضى النص أنه مقيد بما إذا لم يجد نعلين. أقول: الظاهر أن قيد عدم وجدان النعلين لوجوب قطع الخفين بخلاف ما إذا وجدا فإنه لا يجب القطع حينئذ لما فيه
His statement: (And I have not seen anyone explicitly state etc.) He said in al-Nahr in Lubab al-Manasik: If he finds sandals after wearing them, i.e., wearing the cut khuff, it is permissible for him to continue wearing them; it is permissible to wear the cut khuff while sandals are present. End. Its commentator said: But this does not negate the karahah that is due to violating the sunnah. And he said before that its summary: al-Tabari narrated from Hanifah that if he is able to wear sandals, it is not permissible for him to wear khuff even if he cuts them, but this is contrary to the madhhab and perhaps it is a narration from him. And the apparent is that wearing them then is against the sunnah, so it is makruh and it entails sin. And Ibn al-Humam said: The mashayikh differed regarding its permissibility, and the requirement of the text is that it is restricted to when he does not find sandals. I say: The apparent is that the condition of not finding sandals is for the obligation of cutting the khuff, unlike if he finds them, for then cutting is not obligatory because of the waste.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about wearing khuff (leather socks) when the muhrim is able to obtain sandals. The matn statement 'I have not seen anyone explicitly state' is clarified by al-Nahr in Lubab al-Manasik: if a person wears khuff and cuts them below the ankles, and then finds sandals, it is permissible to continue wearing the cut khuff. However, the commentator notes that this does not lift the karahah (dislike) for violating the sunnah, since the sunnah is to wear sandals. Al-Tabari reported a view from Abu Hanifah that wearing khuff even cut is not allowed when sandals are available, but this is not the relied-upon position. Ibn al-Humam notes that the condition of not finding sandals is for the obligation to cut; if sandals are available, cutting is not obligatory due to waste of property. The final conclusion is that wearing uncut khuff when sandals are available is makruh tahrimi (sinful), but some scholars allow it with karahah.

Key Terms
خُفّ (khuff): Leather socks worn inside sandals; during ihram, men must cut them below the ankles if worn.
نعل (na'l): Sandals that are permitted to wear in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a muhrim wears cut khuff (below ankles) while he has sandals available?
A) It is haram and invalidates ihram.
B) It is permissible without any dislike.
C) It is permissible but makruh.
D) It is obligatory to switch to sandals.

Key Takeaway
Wearing cut khuff when sandals are available is permissible but makruh tanzihi because the sunnah is to wear sandals.

Prohibition of Covering the Face and Head for the Muhrim
Ruling with proof from hadith and intra-madhhab debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the face and head for both living and deceased muhrims and explain the hadith proof and the intra-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The prohibition of covering the face and head applies only to the living muhrim; a dead muhrim is covered like any other deceased.

In this passage, the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the ruling that a muhrim must avoid covering his face and head. The proof comes from the famous hadith of the bedouin who died in ihram. However, the Hanafi school restricts the application of this hadith to the living, treating the dead muhrim as ordinary deceased. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the inter-madhhab debate with the Shafi'is.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for the living muhrim
The text states that covering the face and head is prohibited (haram) for the living muhrim. This is derived from the command in the hadith.
The prohibition includes covering any part of the face, such as the mouth or chin.
2
Locate the dalil and examine its structure
The hadith says: 'Do not cover his head nor his face, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection in talbiyah.' The imperative 'do not cover' indicates prohibition, and the reasoning (ta'lil) shows the illa is maintaining ihram.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its dalala (meaning) is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for the living muhrim
The Hanafis argue that the reasoning (for he will be raised in talbiyah) implies the prohibition is because the person is still in ihram. Therefore, it applies to any living muhrim who is still in the state of ihram.
The ta'lil is used to extend the ruling beyond the specific incident.
4
Note the ikhtilaf: Shafi'i position on the dead muhrim
The Shafi'is apply the hadith's explicit command to any muhrim who dies, thus prohibiting covering the face even after death. The Hanafis counter that the hadith is specific to the bedouin and is overridden by the general principle that deeds end at death.
The Hanafi response reconciles the hadith with the hadith 'When the son of Adam dies, his deeds are cut off' by specifying the bedouin as an exception.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered stronger because it harmonizes both texts: the prohibition applies during life, but after death the general rule of covering the dead applies. Thus the dead muhrim is covered like any other deceased (mustahab).
The practical difference: Hanafis cover the face of a deceased muhrim; Shafi'is leave it uncovered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وستر الوجه والرأس أي واجتنب تغطيتهما لحديث الأعرابي الذي وقصته ناقته «لا تخمروا رأسه ولا وجهه فإنه يبعث يوم القيامة ملبياً». واعلم أن أئمتنا استدلوا بهذا الحديث على حرمة تغطية الوجه على المحرم الحي المفهوم من التعليل ولم يعملوا بمنطوقه في حق الميت المحرم فإن حكمه عندنا كسائر الأموات في تغطية الوجه والرأس، والشافعية عملوا به فيما إذا مات المحرم ولم يعملوا به في حالة الحياة. وأجاب في غاية البيان عن بأنهم إنما لم يعملوا به في الموت لأنه معارض بحديث إذا مات ابن آدم انقطع عمله إلا من ثلاث والإحرام عمل فهو منقطع فيغطى العضوان ولهذا لا يبنى المأمور بالحج على إحرام الميت اتفاقاً، وهو يدل على انقطاعه بالموت والأعرابي مخصوص من ذلك بأخبار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أئمتنا كإعارة سكين أو مناولة رمح أو سوط ا هـ ببقاء إحرامه وهو في غيره مفقود فقلنا بانقطاعه بالموت، ولأن المرأة لا تغطي وجهها إجماعاً مع أنها عورة مستورة وفي كشفه فتنة فلأن لا يغطي به عادة كالعدل والطبق والإجانة، ولا فرق بين ستر الكل والبعض والعصابة ولهذا ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أنه لا يغطي فاه ولا ذقنه ولا عارضه ولا بأس بأن يضع يديه على أنفه وهو في غيره مفقود أي بقاء الإحرام مفقود في غير الأعرابي المخصوص بتلك الخصوصية لعدم ما يدل على ذلك فقلنا بانقطاعه بالموت على الأصل، وفي بعض النسخ وهو غير مفقود وهو تحريف.
His statement: (And covering the face and head means he must avoid covering them due to the hadith of the bedouin whose camel broke his neck: 'Do not cover his head nor his face, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection in the state of talbiyah.' Know that our imams used this hadith as evidence for the prohibition of covering the face for the living muhrim, understood from the reasoning, and they did not act upon its explicit text regarding the dead muhrim, for his ruling with us is like other dead in covering the face and head. The Shafi'is acted upon it regarding when the muhrim dies and did not act upon it in the state of life. He answered in Ghayat al-Bayan that they only did not act upon it regarding death because it is contradicted by the hadith 'When the son of Adam dies, his deeds are cut off except from three' and ihram is a deed, so it is cut off, so the two limbs are covered, and for this reason the one commanded for Hajj is not built upon the ihram of the deceased by agreement, and it indicates its cutting off by death, and the bedouin is specified from that by the reports of the Prophet, peace be upon him. Our imams like lending a knife or handing a spear or a whip end. With the continuation of his ihram and it is lacking in others, so we said it is cut off by death, and because the woman does not cover her face by consensus while it is a covered 'awrah and in its uncovering is temptation, so even more so should it not be covered ordinarily like the saddle, plate, and basin, and there is no difference between covering all, part, or the headband, and for this reason Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa that he does not cover his mouth, nor his chin, nor his cheek, and there is no harm in him placing his hands on his nose. And it is lacking in others means the continuation of ihram is lacking in other than the bedouin specified with that particularity due to the absence of evidence indicating that, so we said it is cut off by death according to the principle, and in some copies it is 'ghayr mawjud' and it is a corruption.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith of the bedouin who died in ihram. The Hanafis use this hadith to prohibit covering the face for the living muhrim, but they do not extend it to the dead muhrim, whom they cover like any other deceased. They argue that ihram ends at death, so the hadith is specific to that bedouin. The response from Ghayat al-Bayan explains that the Shafi'i position is based on the hadith's general application, but the Hanafis counter with the principle that deeds are cut off at death. The passage also clarifies that it is impermissible to cover even part of the face, such as the mouth or chin, and that placing a hand on the nose is allowed. The final note addresses a variant reading in some manuscripts.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj/Umrah, with prohibitions and special dress.
تغطية الوجه (taghtiyat al-wajh): Covering the face, which is prohibited for the living muhrim according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on covering the face of a muhrim who dies while in ihram?
A) It is haram like a living muhrim.
B) It is mustahab to cover the face like any other deceased.
C) It is wajib to leave the face uncovered.
D) It is makruh to cover the face.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of covering the face and head for a muhrim is restricted to life; after death, the usual rules of covering the deceased apply.

Washing the Head with Khitmi: Penalty for a Muhrim
Ruling on washing head with khitmi and the penalty (dam vs sadaqah) for doing so.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on washing the head with khitmi for a muhrim, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the penalty, and identify the legal basis for each position.

Core Idea
Washing head with khitmi in ihram incurs a penalty; Abu Hanifa says dam, the two companions say sadaqah.

This lesson examines a specific fiqh issue: a muhrim using khitmi (a perfumed plant) to wash the head. While the obligation to avoid it is agreed upon, the penalty required differs between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions. The difference stems from whether khitmi is considered a kind of perfume (tib) — which would trigger a dam — or merely a cleansing agent, which would only require sadaqah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that it is wajib (obligatory) to avoid washing the head and beard with khitmi while in ihram. Doing so is therefore prohibited and incurs a penalty.
2
Recognize the agreement and disagreement
All Hanafi authorities agree on the prohibition. The disagreement is only on the type of penalty: dam (sheep sacrifice) or sadaqah (charity).
3
Analyze the two positions
Abu Hanifa argues that khitmi is a type of perfume because it has a pleasant scent, hence the general prohibition on perfume applies and requires a dam. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that khitmi kills vermin and softens hair without being a perfume, so only sadaqah is needed.
The passage notes this is a difference in interpretation (tafsir) of what constitutes 'perfume'.
4
Understand the nature of the difference
The ikhtilaf is not a fundamental disagreement but a legal interpretation of the term 'tib'. Both views are sound within the school.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compares this to differences like the ruling on soap or breaking fast with dripping water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وغسلهما بالخطمي) أي وليجتنب غسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي واللحية لما كانت في الوجه. أعاد الضمير عليها وإن لم يتقدم لها ذكر ووجوب اجتنابه متفق عليه لكن يجب عليه دم إذا لم يجتنبه عنده لأنه نوع طيب وعندهما صدقة لأنه يقتل الهوام ويلين الشعر وليس بطيب، وهذا الاختلاف راجع إلى تفسيره وليس باختلاف حقيقة كالاختلاف في الصابئة والإفطار بالإقطار في الإحليل. والخطمي بكسر الخاء نبت يغسل به الرأس، وقيد بالخطمي لأنه لو غسل رأسه بالحرض والصابون لا شيء عليه باتفاقهم
His statement: (And washing them with khitmi) meaning let him avoid washing his head and beard with khitmi, and the beard because it is on the face. He repeated the pronoun for them even though they were not mentioned before. The obligation to avoid it is agreed upon, but he must give a dam if he does not avoid it according to him (Abu Hanifa) because it is a type of perfume, while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he gives sadaqah because it kills vermin and softens hair and is not perfume. This difference returns to its interpretation and is not a difference in reality, like the difference regarding soap and breaking the fast with dripping into the urethra. Khitmi (with kasr on the kha) is a plant with which the head is washed. He restricted it to khitmi because if he washes his head with ash (?) or soap, nothing is required according to all.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage rules on washing the head and beard with khitmi (a plant used like soap). It is wajib to avoid it. If a muhrim does it, there is a penalty. Abu Hanifa says it is a dam (sacrifice of a sheep) because khitmi is considered a perfume, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is sadaqah (charity) because it is not perfume but kills insects and softens hair. This is a legal difference in interpretation, not a dispute about the ruling. Washing with ordinary soap or ash (?) is permissible without penalty by agreement.

Key Terms
خطمي (khitmi): A plant used for washing hair; considered perfume-like by Abu Hanifa.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (sheep) required as penalty for violating certain ihram restrictions.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity (often half a sa' of wheat or equivalent) as a lighter penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what penalty do Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require for a muhrim who washes his head with khitmi?
A) Dam (sacrifice of a sheep).
B) Sadaqah (charity).
C) Nothing, as it is permissible.
D) Invalidation of ihram.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the penalty for using khitmi highlights how interpretation of a substance's legal category (perfume vs cleanser) can alter the required expiation.

Prohibition of Perfume for the Muhrim
Ruling on avoiding perfume in any form during ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on using perfume in ihram and identify which substances are considered perfume according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The muhrim must avoid all fragrant substances — perfume is haram.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the prohibition of perfume during ihram is absolute. It defines what constitutes perfume in Islamic law, listing specific examples. Understanding this helps avoid common mistakes, such as using unscented but fragrant substances thinking they are permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
The act is 'touching perfume' (مس الطيب), meaning applying perfume to body or clothing.
The prohibition is general.
2
Recognize the evidence
The hadith describes the muhrim as 'al-sha'ith al-tafil' (disheveled and unscented), implying no perfume.
This is a dalil naqli.
3
Learn the definition of perfume in Shariah
Perfume (tib) is any substance with a pleasant scent, including saffron, violet, rose, etc.
The list is illustrative.
4
Note the omission of oil
The author did not list oil; either it is included as the essence of perfume or due to a difference of opinion.
This will be discussed later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومس الطيب) أي واجتنبه مطلقاً في الثوب والبدن لقوله عليه السلام «الخاج الشعث التفل» وهو بكسر العين مغبر الرأس، والتفل بكسر الفاء تارك الطيب، وهو في اللغة نقيض الخبث وفي الشريعة وهو جسم له رائحة طيبة كالزعفران والبنفسج والياسمين والغالية والورد والورس والعصفر والحناء ولم يذكر المصنف هنا الدهن كما في الوافي، إما أنه أصل الطيب فدخل تحته وإما للاختلاف كما سيأتي في باب الجنايات
His statement: (And touching perfume) meaning let him avoid it absolutely, on clothing and body, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The valiant, disheveled, and unscented.' 'Al-sha'ith' (with kasr on the 'ayn) means dusty-headed, and 'al-tafil' (with kasr on the fa) means one who leaves perfume. In language it is the opposite of foulness, and in Shariah it is a substance with a pleasant scent, like saffron, violet, jasmine, a blend, rose, turmeric, safflower, and henna. The author did not mention oil here as in al-Wafi, either because it is the essence of perfume so it is included under it, or because of disagreement as will come in the chapter of penalties.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage states the prohibition of using any perfume on the body or clothing during ihram. The hadith describes the muhrim as 'disheveled and unscented.' The definition of perfume in Islamic law is any pleasant-smelling substance like saffron, rose, etc. The author notes that oil is not explicitly listed here, but it is either implied as a perfume or left out due to a difference of opinion that will be covered later.

Key Terms
طيب (tib): Any substance with a pleasant fragrance, prohibited in ihram.
الخاج الشعث التفل (al-khaj al-sha'ith al-tafil): A descriptive phrase for the muhrim: disheveled and unscented.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT considered 'tib' (perfume) according to the definition in this passage?
A) Saffron
B) Violet
C) Rose
D) Ordinary unscented oil

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of perfume for the muhrim is absolute, covering any substance with a pleasant fragrance, as supported by the prophetic description of the muhrim as unscented.

Prohibition of Hair and Nail Removal in Ihram
Ruling on hair and nail removal during ihram with Quranic proof and an exception for eye hair.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hair/nail removal during ihram, identify the Quranic proof, and apply the exception for eye hair.

Core Idea
Removing any hair or nail in ihram is haram; even plucking requires a dam, except eye hair.

The prohibition of shaving the head in ihram is explicit in the Quran. The Hanafi school extends this to all hair removal from the body, including cutting nails, based on qiyas. However, an exception is made for hair growing in the eye due to necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is any removal of hair or nails during ihram. The ruling is haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 2:196: 'Wa la tahliqoo ruoosakum' (And do not shave your heads) is the primary proof.
Transmission (thubut) and meaning (dalala) are both definitive (qat'i).
3
Extend by analogy
Cutting, plucking, burning, etc., are all included by qiyas because they share the meaning (ma'na) of hair removal.
The text explicitly states 'al-qass fi ma'nahu' (cutting is in its meaning).
4
Note the exception
Some Hanafi mashayikh exempt removing hair growing in the eye (to alleviate pain), with no penalty.
This is an istithna' based on necessity.
5
State the consequence
Prohibited removal (without exception) requires a dam (sacrifice) as compensation.
The dam is wajib; the act is haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وحلق رأسه وقص شعره وظفره أي واجتنب هذه الأشياء لقوله تعالى ولا تحلقوا رؤسكم [البقرة : ١٩٦] والقص في معناه فثبت دلالة والمراد إزالة الشعر كيفما كان حلقاً وقصاً ونتفاً وتنوراً وإحراقاً من أي مكان كان من الرأس والبدن مباشرة أو تمكيناً لكن قال الحلبي في مناسكه: ويستثنى منه قلع الشعر النابت في العين فقد ذكر بعض مشايخنا أنه لا شيء فيه عندنا
His statement: (And shaving his head and cutting his hair and nail) meaning let him avoid these things due to the statement of Allah Most High: 'And do not shave your heads' [2:196]. Cutting is in its meaning, so dalalah is established. The intention is removal of hair however it is: shaving, cutting, plucking, by depilatory, burning, from any place on the head or body, directly or enabling. But al-Halabi said in his Manasik: An exception is made for pulling out the hair growing in the eye, for some of our mashayikh have mentioned that there is nothing upon him in our school.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage prohibits any form of hair removal from the body during ihram, based on Quran 2:196. The prohibition includes all methods: shaving, cutting, plucking, etc., and applies to all body hair, whether on the head or elsewhere. The exception is hair growing in the eye (which causes pain), which is exempt from penalty according to some Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving, a form of hair removal prohibited in ihram.
قص (qass): Cutting, also prohibited by analogy.
ظفر (zuffar): Nail, cutting is also prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a muhrim plucking his armpit hair?
A) Permissible because it is not shaving.
B) Prohibited and requires a dam.
C) Permissible without penalty.
D) Only prohibited if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
All intentional hair or nail removal in ihram is haram and requires a dam, except for eye hair where some scholars exempt.

Permissibility of Bathing, Shading, and Wearing Himyan in Ihram
List of actions not prohibited for the muhrim despite misconceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which three actions are permissible for a muhrim and identify the condition for shading.

Core Idea
A muhrim may bathe, shade without head contact, and wear a money belt — none are prohibited acts.

Many assume that the state of ihram prohibits all forms of covering and grooming. However, the Hanafi school clarifies that certain actions remain permissible based on Prophetic practice. This lesson presents three such actions: bathing, shading oneself (as long as the cover does not touch the head or face), and wearing a himyan (money belt). The conditions attached to these rulings protect the integrity of ihram while acknowledging legitimate needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three permissible acts
The passage lists ightisal (bathing), istizlal (shading), and shadd al-himyan (tying the money belt). Note each action.
2
Understand the condition for shading
Shading is allowed only if the cover does not touch the head or face. If it does, it becomes makruh and may require a penalty (jaza).
3
Recognize the rationale for himyan
The himyan is permissible because it is not a sewn garment (laysa labs makhit). This ruling extends to belts, swords, rings.
4
Note the evidence for bathing
The permission is based on the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) bathed while in ihram (Muslim).
5
Distinguish sewn garments from accessories
Anything that is not a sewn garment (like a money belt) is allowed; sewn garments are prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا) الاغتسال ودخول الحمام) أي لا يتقيهما لما روى مسلم أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم اغتسل وهو محرم قوله : (والاستظلال بالبيت والمحمل أي لا يجتنبه. والمحمل بفتح الميم الأولى وكسر الثانية أو عكسه، وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يصب رأسه ولا وجهه فلو أصاب أحدهما يكره كما لو حمل ثياباً على رأسه فإنه يلزمه الجزاء بخلاف ما إذا حمل نحو الطبق أو الإجانة والعدل المشغول قوله : وشد الهميان في وسطه أي لا يجتنبه وهو بالكسر ما يجعل فيه الدراهم ويشد على الحقو. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان فيه نفقته أو نفقة غيره لأنه ليس بلبس مخيط ولا في معناه. وأشار إلى أنه لا يكره شد المنطقة والسيف والسلاح والتختم بالخاتم. ومما لا يكره من إضاعة المال عبئاً وهو لا ينافي ما إذا قطعهما ولبسهما مع وجود النعلين ا هـ
His statement: (No) bathing and entering the bathhouse meaning he does not avoid them because Muslim narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, bathed while he was in ihram. His statement: (And shading with the house and the howdah) meaning he does not avoid it. Al-mahmil (with fat-h on the first meem and kasr on the second or opposite) is restricted to when it does not touch his head or face; if it touches either, it is makruh just as if he carries clothes on his head, for then penalty is required, unlike if he carries something like a plate or basin or a loaded saddle. His statement: (And tying the himyan around his waist) meaning he does not avoid it. Himyan (with kasr) is something in which dirhams are placed and tied around the waist. He generalizes it, so it includes whether it contains his expenses or another's expenses, because it is not wearing a sewn garment nor similar. He indicated that there is no karahah in tying a belt, sword, weapon, or wearing a ring. And from what is not disliked is wasting wealth? It does not contradict what if he cuts them and wears them while sandals are present.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage clarifies three actions that are not prohibited for the muhrim: (1) Bathing and entering the bathhouse are allowed based on the Prophet's example. (2) Shading oneself with a house or howdah is allowed as long as it does not touch the head or face; if it does, it is makruh and may require a penalty. (3) Wearing a himyan (money belt) around the waist is allowed because it is not a sewn garment. Similarly, belts, swords, rings are not makruh. The final line notes that some things like wasting wealth are not disliked in the sense that cutting khuff and wearing them while sandals are present is permissible (as previously discussed).

Key Terms
محمل (mahmil): A howdah or litter on a camel that provides shade.
هميان (himyan): A money belt worn around the waist.
اغتسال (ightisal): Bathing, allowed in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, which of the following is permissible for a muhrim?
A) Wearing a stitched shirt.
B) Tying a money belt (himyan) around the waist.
C) Covering the head with a turban.
D) Using scented soap.

Key Takeaway
Bathing, shading (without direct head contact), and wearing a money belt are all permissible for a muhrim — the prohibition is on sewn garments and covering the head, not on all coverings.

Prohibitions in Ihram: Khitmi, Perfume, and Hair Removal
Explaining prohibition and penalties for three ihram violations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited acts in ihram, identify the Hanafi dispute on the penalty for using khitmi, and apply the ruling to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Using khitmi in ihram is prohibited; Abu Hanifa requires a dam, the Sahibayn only sadaqa.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains three key prohibitions for the muhrim: washing with khitmi, applying perfume, and removing hair. While the prohibition of perfume and hair removal is straightforward, the penalty for khitmi is disputed within the Hanafi school. Let's examine the details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibitions and their sources
List the three acts: washing head/beard with khitmi, touching perfume, and shaving/cutting hair. Note that perfume is prohibited by hadith, hair removal by Quran (2:196).
The prohibition of khitmi is based on it being considered a type of perfume by Abu Hanifa.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on khitmi
Understand that Abu Hanifa says dam because khitmi is perfume-like, while the Sahibayn say sadaqa because it kills lice and softens hair.
The difference is interpretive, not a fundamental disagreement on the prohibition itself.
3
Apply to similar cases
Note that washing with soap or alkali incurs no penalty by agreement. The restriction is specific to khitmi.
4
Note exceptions and details
For hair removal, the exception of pulling an eyelash that grows into the eye is mentioned by al-Halabi, with no penalty.
This exception is based on necessity and is accepted by some Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أن يكون غسيلاً لا ينفض وستر الوجه والرأس وغسلهما بالخطمى ومس الطيب ببقاء إحرامه وهو في غيره مفقود فقلنا بانقطاعه بالموت، ولأن المرأة لا تغطي وجهها إجماعاً مع أنها عورة مستورة وفي كشفه فتنة فلأن لا يغطي به عادة كالعدل والطبق والإجانة، ولا فرق بين ستر الكل والبعض والعصابة ولهذا ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أنه لا يغطي فاه ولا ذقنه ولا عارضه ولا بأس بأن يضع يديه على أنفه قوله : ( وغسلهما بالخطمي) أي وليجتنب غسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي واللحية لما كانت في الوجه. أعاد الضمير عليها وإن لم يتقدم لها ذكر ووجوب اجتنابه متفق عليه لكن يجب عليه دم إذا لم يجتنبه عنده لأنه نوع طيب وعندهما صدقة لأنه يقتل الهوام ويلين الشعر وليس بطيب، وهذا الاختلاف راجع إلى تفسيره وليس باختلاف حقيقة كالاختلاف في الصابئة والإفطار بالإقطار في الإحليل. والخطمي بكسر الخاء نبت يغسل به الرأس، وقيد بالخطمي لأنه لو غسل رأسه بالحرض والصابون لا شيء عليه باتفاقهم قوله : (ومس الطيب) أي واجتنبه مطلقاً في الثوب والبدن لقوله عليه السلام «الخاج الشعث التفل» وهو بكسر العين مغبر الرأس، والتفل بكسر الفاء تارك الطيب، وهو في اللغة نقيض الخبث وفي الشريعة وهو جسم له رائحة طيبة كالزعفران والبنفسج والياسمين والغالية والورد والورس والعصفر والحناء ولم يذكر المصنف هنا الدهن كما في الوافي، إما أنه أصل الطيب فدخل تحته وإما للاختلاف كما سيأتي في باب الجنايات قوله: (وحلق رأسه وقص شعره وظفره) أي واجتنب هذه الأشياء لقوله تعالى ولا تحلقوا رؤسكم والقص في معناه فثبت دلالة والمراد إزالة الشعر كيفما كان حلقاً وقصاً ونتفاً وتنوراً وإحراقاً من أي مكان كان من الرأس والبدن مباشرة أو تمكيناً لكن قال الحلبي في مناسكه: ويستثنى منه قلع الشعر النابت في العين فقد ذكر بعض مشايخنا أنه لا شيء فيه عندنا .
Except when it is a washing that does not shake off, and covering the face and head, and washing them with khitmi, and touching perfume, with the continuation of his ihram, and it is absent in other than him; so we said it is cut off by death. Because the woman does not cover her face by consensus even though she is a covered awrah and in uncovering it there is temptation, so it is even more befitting that it is not covered by custom like the saddle, basin, and bowl. And there is no difference between covering all, part, or the bandage. For this reason Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa that he does not cover his mouth, nor his chin, nor his cheek, and there is no harm in him placing his hands on his nose. His statement: (And washing them with khitmi) i.e., he should avoid washing his head and beard with khitmi, and the beard is included since it is on the face; he used the pronoun for both even though it was not mentioned previously. The obligation of avoiding it is agreed upon, but he must give a dam if he does not avoid it according to him (Abu Hanifa) because it is a type of perfume, while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is a sadaqa because it kills insects and softens the hair and it is not perfume. This difference goes back to its interpretation and not a real difference, like the difference regarding soda ash and breaking the fast by inserting oil into the urethra. Khitmi (with kasra on the kha) is a plant used to wash the head. He restricted it to khitmi because if he washes his head with alkali or soap, there is nothing on him by agreement. His statement: (And touching perfume) i.e., avoid it absolutely in garment and body, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The pilgrim is dusty and unperfumed.' 'Ash'ath' (with kasra on 'ayn) means dusty hair, 'tafil' (with kasra on fa) means one who avoids perfume. In language it is the opposite of 'khabith', and in Sacred Law it is a body with a pleasant fragrance like saffron, violet, jasmine, musk, rose, safflower, carthamus, and henna. The author did not mention oil here as in al-Wafi, either because it is the origin of perfume so it is included, or because of difference as will come in the chapter of penalties. His statement: (And shaving his head, cutting his hair and his nails) i.e., he avoids these things due to His statement: 'And do not shave your heads' (al-Baqarah 2:196), and cutting is in its meaning, so the indication is established. What is intended is removing hair in any way, by shaving, cutting, plucking, using a depilatory, or burning, from any place on the head or body, directly or by enabling. But al-Halabi said in his Manasik: 'An exception is made for pulling out a hair growing in the eye, for some of our shuyukh have mentioned that there is nothing on him according to us.'
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, discusses three prohibited acts of ihram: washing the head with khitmi, touching perfume, and shaving or cutting hair. For khitmi, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa considers it a type of perfume, thus requiring a dam (sacrifice) if used; the two companions (Sahibayn) consider it only a cleanser, requiring sadaqa. The difference is interpretive, not essential. Perfume is prohibited absolutely based on the hadith describing the muhrim. Shaving or cutting hair is prohibited by Quranic verse, but an exception is made for pulling out an eyelash that grows into the eye, according to some Hanafi scholars, with no penalty.

Key Terms
الخطمي (al-khitmi): A specific plant (Althaea officinalis) used for washing the head, considered a type of perfume in ihram context.
الطيب (al-tib): Any substance with a pleasant fragrance, like saffron, rose, etc., prohibited in ihram.
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving or removing hair from any part of the body, prohibited in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the penalty for washing the head with khitmi according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)?
A) No penalty
B) Sadaqa (charity)
C) Dam (sacrifice)
D) Expiation (kaffarah)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, using khitmi in ihram incurs a penalty, with a dispute on whether it is a dam or sadaqa; the prohibition is certain, the penalty level differs.

Permissible Acts in Ihram: Ghusl, Shade, and Money Belt
Clarifying that certain common acts are permitted in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl, seeking shade, and wearing a money belt for a muhrim, and identify the condition that triggers a penalty.

Core Idea
A muhrim may bathe, seek shade (if it does not touch head/face), and wear a money belt—these are mubah with conditions.

In the state of ihram, many actions are restricted, but not all. This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that some common acts are entirely permissible. Understanding these exceptions prevents unnecessary hardship while preserving the sanctity of the sacred state.

Guided Path
1
Identify each act and its ruling
List the acts mentioned: ghusl (full bath), entering a bathhouse, seeking shade under a howdah or roof, and tightening a money belt. The text declares them permissible (mubah).
2
Note the condition for shade
Seeking shade is permissible only if the shade does not touch the head or face. If it touches, it becomes disliked and may require compensation.
This condition prevents the shade from resembling the head covering that is prohibited in ihram.
3
Identify the evidence for ghusl
The author cites the hadith from Muslim that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed ghusl while in ihram, establishing permissibility.
This is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli).
4
Distinguish actions that incur penalty
Carrying clothes on the head requires a penalty (dam), but carrying a basin or a loaded saddle does not. The difference lies in whether the item is akin to a head covering.
The money belt is not considered stitched clothing, so it is permissible without penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا) الاغتسال ودخول الحمام أي لا يتقيهما لما روى مسلم أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم اغتسل وهو محرم قوله : (والاستظلال بالبيت والمحمل أي لا يجتنبه. والمحمل بفتح الميم الأولى وكسر الثانية أو عكسه، وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يصب رأسه ولا وجهه فلو أصاب أحدهما يكره كما لو حمل ثياباً على رأسه فإنه يلزمه الجزاء بخلاف ما إذا حمل نحو الطبق أو الإجانة والعدل المشغول قوله : وشد الهميان في وسطه أي لا يجتنبه وهو بالكسر ما يجعل فيه الدراهم ويشد على الحقو. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان فيه نفقته أو نفقة غيره لأنه ليس بلبس مخيط ولا في معناه. وأشار إلى أنه لا يكره شد المنطقة والسيف والسلاح والتختم بالخاتم. ومما لا يكره من إضاعة المال عبئاً وهو لا ينافي ما إذا قطعهما ولبسهما مع وجود النعلين ا هـ . قوله : (وهو في غيره مفقود أي بقاء الإحرام مفقود في غير الأعرابي المخصوص بتلك الخصوصية لعدم ما يدل على ذلك فقلنا بانقطاعه بالموت على الأصل، وفي بعض النسخ وهو غير مفقود وهو تحريف.
His statement: (No) for ghusl and entering the bath) i.e., he does not avoid them because Muslim narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed ghusl while in ihram. His statement: (and seeking shade under the house and the howdah) i.e., he does not avoid it. Al-mahmil (with fatha on the first meem and kasra on the second, or vice versa) is restricted to when it does not touch his head or face; if it touches either, it is disliked, just as when he carries clothes on his head, then a compensation is due, unlike when he carries something like a basin, bowl, or loaded saddle. His statement: (and tightening the himyan on his waist) i.e., he does not avoid it. Al-himyan (with kasra) is what dirhams are placed in and tied around the waist. He made it absolute, so it includes when it contains his expenses or another's expenses, because it is not wearing stitched clothing nor equivalent to it. And he indicated that there is no dislike in tightening the belt, sword, weapon, and wearing a ring. And among that which is not disliked is wasting wealth without benefit, and it does not contradict when he cuts them and wears them while sandals exist. His statement: (And it is absent in other than him) i.e., the continuation of ihram is absent in other than the specific Bedouin due to lack of evidence indicating that, so we said it is cut off by death according to the original principle. And in some copies, 'and it is not absent' which is a corruption.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage explains several actions that are permissible for a muhrim. Ghusl (full body wash) and entering a bathhouse are allowed because the Prophet himself performed ghusl in ihram. Seeking shade under a roof (bayt) or a howdah (mahmil) is permissible only if it does not touch the head or face; if it does, it becomes disliked and may require compensation (like carrying clothes on the head). Fastening a money belt (himyan) around the waist is allowed because it is not stitched clothing and serves a necessary purpose. The final part clarifies a special ruling about the continuation of ihram after death, which applies only to a specific Bedouin incident narrated earlier; for others, ihram ends at death.

Key Terms
الاغتسال (al-ightisal): Full body washing, permissible in ihram.
المحمل (al-mahmil): A howdah or saddle used for shade; permissible if it does not touch head or face.
الهميان (al-himyan): A money belt tied around the waist, considered not stitched clothing and thus permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a muhrim wearing a money belt (himyan) that contains his expenses?
A) Prohibited
B) Disliked
C) Permissible
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
Ghusl, seeking shade (with condition), and wearing a money belt are all mubah for a muhrim; the key condition for shade is that it must not touch the head or face, otherwise a penalty may be due.

Talbiyah: When and How to Perform It
Ruling and etiquettes of talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the occasions for increasing talbiyah, classify its legal ruling (fard once, sunnah to repeat, mustahabb at specific times), and list its key etiquettes.

Core Idea
Talbiyah is fard once, sunnah to repeat, and mustahabb at specific times and places.

This lesson examines the rulings and etiquettes of talbiyah from the Hanafi text al-Bahr al-Raiq. The passage clarifies that talbiyah is not a single utterance but a multi-level act: obligatory once at the start of ihram, sunnah to repeat, and recommended to increase at certain occasions such as after prayer, on high ground, and at dawn. Understanding these nuances helps the pilgrim perform hajj correctly and maximize reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Extract from Fath al-Qadir cited in the text: talbiyah is fard (obligatory once at the start of ihram), sunnah (to repeat), and mustahabb (to increase at specific occasions). This threefold classification forms the foundation.
The initial fard is the first utterance; repetition is sunnah, not fard.
2
List the occasions for increasing talbiyah
The text mentions five occasions: after prayer (متى صليت), when ascending a high place (علوت شرفاً), when descending into a valley (هبطت وادياً), when meeting a rider (لقيت ركبا), and at dawn (بالسحر).
The word 'prayer' (صلاة) has a dispute: does it include all prayers or only fard?
3
Analyze the dispute on 'prayer'
The phrase 'متى صليت' is absolute in the apparent narration (ظاهر الرواية), encompassing fard, wajib, and nafl. Al-Tahawi restricted it to fard prayers by analogy to takbirs of tashriq. The text supports the general view, which is the relied-upon position.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the practical effect is whether to increase talbiyah after a nafl prayer.
4
Apply the etiquettes of talbiyah
The text outlines recommended practices: repeat three times each time one begins, perform continuously without interruption, avoid speech unless returning a greeting (which is disliked except for the greeter), say 'Labbayk inna al-‘aysh…' when seeing something pleasing, send blessings on the Prophet secretly, supplicate for Paradise and seek refuge from Hellfire, and raise the voice moderately without straining.
Raising the voice is sunnah, but one should not exhaust himself as common people do.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من كتاب الحج/ باب الإحرام وحلق رأسه وقص شعره وظفره لا الاغتسال ودخول الحمام والاستظلال بالبيت والمحمل وشد الهميان في وسطه وأكثر التلبية متى صليت أو علوت شرفاً أو هبطت له أيضاً الاكتحال بغير المطيب وأن يختتن ويفتصد ويقلع ضرسه ويجبر الكسر ويحتجم وأن يحك رأسه وبدنه غير أنه إن خاف سقوط شيء من شعره بسبب ذلك حكه برفق وإن لم يخف ذلك فلا بأس بالحك الشديد قوله : (وأكثر من التلبية متى صليت أو علوت شرفا أو هبطت وادياً أو لقيت ركبا وبالاسخار رافعاً (صوتك أي أكثر منها على وجه الاستحباب عند اختلاف الأحوال كتكبير الصلاة عند الانتقال. أطلق الصلاة فشمل فرضها وواجبها ونفلها وهو ظاهر الرواية وخصها الطحاوي بالمكتوبات قياساً على تكبيرات التشريق كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وعلوت شرفاً أي صعدت مكاناً مرتفعاً، وقيل بضم الشين جمع شرفة. والركب جمع راكب كتجر جمع تاجر، والسحر السدس الأخير من الليل. وصرح في الميحط بأن الزيادة منها على المرة الواحدة سنة حتى تلزمه الإساءة بتركها قال في فتح القدير : فظهر أن التلبية فرض وسنة ومندوب ويستحب أن يكررها كلما أخذ فيها ثلاث مرات ويأتي بها على الولاء ولا يقطعها بكلام، ولو رد السلام في خلالها جاز لكن يكره لغير السلام عليه في حالة التليية. وإذا رأى شيئاً يعجبه قال لبيك إن العيش عيش الآخرة، وتقدم أنه يصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عقب تلبيته سراً ويسأل الله الجنة ويتعوذ من النار ورفع الصوت بها سنة إلا أنه لا يجهد نفسه كما يفعله العوام.
From the Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: And shaving his head, cutting his hair and his nails; no (prohibition) for ghusl, entering the bath, seeking shade under the house and howdah, and tightening the himyan on his waist; and increase the talbiyah whenever you pray, or ascend a high place, or descend, also for him: applying kohl without perfume, and to perform circumcision, bloodletting, extract a tooth, set a bone, cup, and to scratch his head and body; however, if he fears that something of his hair will fall due to that, he scratches gently; if he does not fear that, there is no harm in vigorous scratching. His statement: (And increase the talbiyah whenever you pray, or ascend a high place, or descend into a valley, or meet a rider, and at dawn, raising your voice) i.e., increase it by way of recommendation at different occasions like the takbirs of prayer at transitions. He made prayer absolute, so it includes obligatory, wajib, and supererogatory prayers; this is the apparent narration, but al-Tahawi restricted it to the prescribed prayers by analogy to the takbirs of tashriq, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. 'And you ascend a high place' i.e., you climb to a high place; it is also said with a damm on the shin, plural of sharafa. 'Al-rakb' is plural of raakib, like tujr plural of tajir. 'Al-sahar' is the last sixth of the night. And it is stated in al-Muhit that increasing it beyond one time is sunnah, such that he commits a misdeed by leaving it. He said in Fath al-Qadir: 'Thus it appears that talbiyah is fard, sunnah, and mustahabb.' It is recommended to repeat it three times each time one begins, and to perform it continuously and not interrupt it with speech. If he returns a greeting during it, it is permitted, but it is disliked to greet someone other than the one greeting him during the state of talbiyah. If he sees something pleasing, he says 'Labbayk, inna al-'aysh 'aysh al-akhirah'. It has preceded that he sends prayers on the Prophet (peace be upon him) after his talbiyah secretly, and asks Allah for Paradise, and seeks refuge from Hellfire. Raising the voice is sunnah, except that he should not exhaust himself as the common people do.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage discusses the etiquettes and rulings of talbiyah. The base line from the matn enumerates various permissible acts, then focuses on talbiyah: it is recommended to increase it at specific occasions: after prayer, when ascending a high place, descending into a valley, meeting a rider, and at dawn. Talbiyah has three categories: fard (obligatory once at the start of ihram), sunnah (to repeat), and mustahabb (to increase on these occasions). The commentator notes differences of opinion on whether 'prayer' includes all prayers or only fard. Etiquettes include repeating three times, not interrupting with speech, returning greetings cautiously, and raising the voice without straining.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The declaration 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' said by the pilgrim, with multiple legal statuses.
السحر (al-sahar): The last sixth of the night, dawn, one of the recommended times for talbiyah.
الركب (al-rakb): A group of riders (plural of raakib).
شرف (sharaf): A high place, elevation; also read with damm (shuruf) as plural of sharafa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is it recommended to increase talbiyah?
A) Only after fard prayers
B) When ascending a high place
C) At noon only
D) When entering the Masjid al-Haram

Key Takeaway
Talbiyah has three legal levels: fard once, sunnah to repeat, and mustahabb at specific times.
